601 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 28,280-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,280 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/26/96); 677 So. 2d 589; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1325



June 26, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 71,325. Honorable Harmon Drew, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, which convicted him of burglary of an inhabited dwelling, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2, and imposed the maximum sentence of 12 years at hard labor. Defendant argued that the State failed to prove that the residence was inhabited as required under § 14:62.2 and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because the victim was in the process of moving into the house, the evidence did not establish that the house was inhabited as required under § 14:62.2. The victim testified that he did not consider the house to be his residence at the time. The court cited caselaw that accepted a dual residence possibility. The victim owned the house. It had belonged to his mother and contained his property. The utilities were connected. The victim spent some nights there while remodeling and intended to make it his permanent residence. The totality of this evidence showed that the house was inhabited pursuant to § 14:62.2. Defendant could not challenge his sentence on appeal because he failed to make or file the required motion for reconsideration pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(D). Regardless, the 12-year statutory maximum sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive for a third felony offender who had been arrested a total of 33 times. Defendant's sentence was actually illegally lenient under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2 because it did not prohibit parole, probation, or suspension during the first year, but the State had not appealed the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and 12-year sentence for burglary of an inhabited dwelling.

 

602 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


NUMBER 96-37


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-37 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/26/96); 677 So. 2d 692; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1362



June 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Peyton Cunningham, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 95-0724.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches, State of Louisiana, denying defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distribution of a controlled dangerous substance and was sentenced to 20 years of hard labor. Prior to defendant's sentence defendant filed a motion for a new trial. The trial court denied the motion and immediately sentenced defendant in violation of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's sentence. The case was remanded for resentencing. First, the court noted that the trial court properly considered defendant's prior criminal acts despite the fact that there was no full adjudication. The trial court properly relied on the presentence report and defendant was given an opportunity to present evidence to contradict the report. The court did find that reversible error occurred where defendant was not offered the 24-hour delay after the denial of the motion for a new trial. Because the sentence was illegally imposed, although it was not constitutionally excessive, it was null, and constituted no valid premise for continued incarceration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's sentence and remanded the case for resentencing.

 

603 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Safety Net for Abused Persons v. Segura


No. 94-1471


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-1471 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/26/96); 677 So. 2d 152; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1364



June 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Carl Williams, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 78565.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. WRIT OF MANDAMUS VACATED AND SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, municipal court judges and clerks, appealed the judgment of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which issued a writ of mandamus compelling the judges and clerks to collect a fee in addition to normal fines, costs, or forfeitures for each civil filing or criminal case in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906. The judges and clerks claimed § 13:1906 violated La. Const. art. 7, § 14(A).


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906 required the judges and clerks to collect a fee in addition to normal fines, costs, or forfeitures for each civil filing or criminal case. The clerk was required to disburse the funds to plaintiff private non-profit corporation, which provided support and counseling for victims of family violence. The judges and clerks refused to collect the fee and the corporation filed suit. The trial court issued a writ of mandamus requiring the judges and clerks to comply with § 13:1906. The judges and clerks claimed § 13:1906 violated La. Const. art. 7, § 14(A). The court held that art. 7, § 14(A) prohibited a political subdivision from donating funds to nonprofit corporations and that to the extent La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1906 required the judges and clerks to collect and remit the funds to the corporation it was unconstitutional under La. Const. art. 7, § 14(A). The court recognized that the state or a political subdivision thereof could contract with a private entity under La. Const. art. 7 § 14(C) but found that there was no contract between the corporation and the judges and clerks' courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, and recalled, vacated, and set aside the writ of mandamus issued by the trial court.

 

604 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Angus Chem. Co.


NUMBER 94 CA 1148


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1148 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/26/96); 679 So. 2d 454; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1549



June 26, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Department of Environmental Quality State of Louisiana. Glenn A. Miller, Assistant Secretary.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL TRANSFERRED TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens groups sought review of a decision of appellee department (Louisiana) that granted an exemption to appellee company from Louisiana's ban on the land disposal of hazardous waste. The corporation filed a motion to dismiss the citizens groups' review for lack of jurisdiction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 30:2050.21, 30:2050.31.


OVERVIEW: The citizens groups challenged the department's decision that granted an exception to the ban on the disposal of hazardous waste. The corporation sought to dismiss the challenge on the ground of lack of jurisdiction, and the citizens groups challenged the constitutionality of the statute relied on by the corporation. The court transferred the appeal to another court, and found that the basis of the citizens groups' challenge to the constitutionality of the statute was that the retroactive application of the jurisdiction provisions of the statute was an impermissible encroachment on the court in contravention to La. Const. art. II, §§ 1, 2. The court held that the state constitution permitted the legislature to provide for appellate jurisdiction, and the retroactive application of jurisdiction did not encroach on the power and integrity of the court. The court held that under La. Const. art. V, § 10(A), it was vested with appellate jurisdiction over "civil matters" but the decision of the department regarding hazardous waste was not a civil matter because the issue was not originally delegated to the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the citizens groups' appeal of the department's decision to another court.

 

605 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hamilton


No. 96-K-0807


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0807 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/07/96); 677 So. 2d 539; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1133



June 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 373-783, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. McKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED. SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review, via writ application, of an order of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section H, Louisiana, that sentenced the defendant to 18 months imprisonment as a double offender. The trial court found the minimum sentence of two and a half years under a plea agreement to be excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation, relative to crime against nature. She entered into a plea bargain with the state, and the trial court charging her to be a twice- convicted felon, while she in actuality was a thrice-convicted felon. Under the agreement she was to be sentenced to 30 months at hard labor. The trial judge maintained that such a sentence was excessive and sentenced defendant to 18 months at hard labor. The state sought review. The court reviewed the record and determined that there was a specific and unambiguous plea struck by the state, defendant and the court. The state was aggrieved by the failure of the court to perform a promise upon which the state had relied to its tangible detriment. It relinquished its opportunity to file a triple offender bill in exchange for a commitment by defendant, her counsel and the court that defendant would receive a sentence of two and a half years. Strong public policy considerations supported the finality of plea bargains. The trial court had no authority to impose a sentence which did not comport with the agreement reached among all parties. The court vacated the sentence and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the trial court that sentenced the defendant to 18 months imprisonment, for the offense of prostitution, as a double offender and remanded for resentencing.

 

606 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Schulker v. Roberson


NUMBER 91-1228


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


91-1228 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/05/96); 676 So. 2d 684; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1241



June 5, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, the Honorable B. Dexter Ryland, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which had denied her relief in her wrongful death action against defendant corporation, which owned a tavern. Defendant driver had been drinking at the tavern prior to an automobile accident where his car struck that of plaintiff, causing her severe injuries and killing her unborn child.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was severely injured in a head-on collision with defendant driver, who had been intoxicated. She also lost her unborn child. The trial court rendered judgment in her favor against defendants, driver and her parents' uninsured/underinsured motorist insurer, but denied her claims against the corporation that owned the tavern where defendant driver had been drinking just prior to the accident. She contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.1 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and held that § 9:2800.1, the statute that shields drinking establishments from liability when an intoxicated patron drives and causes injury, was constitutional. The burden was on plaintiff, as the party claiming unconstitutionality, to show that the statute had no rational basis. She did not sustain the burden. The state had an interest in narrowing the scope of liability of tavern keepers and social hosts and in allocating the consequences of irresponsible drinking to the person doing the drinking. The court held that 9:2800.1 was rationally related to this interest. The tavern did not assume a duty to protect the public from intoxicated patrons, nor was it a nuisance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying plaintiff relief in her negligence action against the tavern, which had sold intoxicants to the driver, whose car had struck the car of plaintiff.

 

607 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Department of Social Servs. v. City of New Orleans


No. 95-CA-1757, C/W No. 95-CA-1758


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1757 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/29/96); 676 So. 2d 149; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1116



May 29, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 94-7177 c/w 94-16291, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an investment company, a shareholder, and the State of Louisiana, Department of Social Services, appealed from the judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division E (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendants, the City of New Orleans and its Department of Safety and Permits, and dismissed plaintiffs' petition challenging the city council's decision denying an application for a conditional use permit.


OVERVIEW: The company agreed to construct and lease to the State an 11,672 square foot building. Its permit application said that the building would be 9,615 square feet. Plaintiffs knew of the discrepancy. Under art. 5, § 33.6 of the Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance of the City of New Orleans, a conditional use permit was needed to operate a new development that was more than 10,000 square feet. Plaintiffs sought this permit after completion. The planning commission was deadlocked, and the council denied the application. The record supported the council's decision, and the district court correctly found that it was not arbitrary or capricious. The non-conforming use was in operation and square footage could not be changed before the application was sought. Art. 5, § 33.6 was valid as written and applied. Plaintiffs' due process rights were not violated even if the council was not pleased with plaintiffs' past actions; plaintiffs were given an opportunity to present their case. Plaintiffs' equal protection rights were not violated; conditional use permits granted to other applicants were distinguishable from this application. Finally, there had been no unlawful taking of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court upholding the city council's decision to deny plaintiffs' application for a conditional use permit.

State v. Randleston


No. 96-K-0069


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0069 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/29/96); 675 So. 2d 804; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1136



May 29, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 372-017, SECTION "C", HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State applied for a supervisory writ, contending that the trial court erred in making a downward departure from the sentencing guidelines when it sentenced defendant for possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of cocaine and was sentenced as a second offender to 90 days' imprisonment.. In a writ application the State argued that the trial court erred by deviating from the mandatory minimum sentence of 30 months. The court granted the writ, but affirmed the sentence. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, if the trial court found that the punishment mandated was constitutionally excessive, the trial court had the option, indeed the duty, to reduce such sentence to one that would not be constitutionally excessive. The trial court had to provide adequate support for any sentence which was less than the statutory minimum, making a meaningful assessment sufficient to justify a sentence below the mandatory minimum of § 15:529.1. The trial court clearly expressed its belief that the mandatory minimum sentence was constitutionally excessive. The testimony from the probation officer and the administrator at the Drug Foundation provided the foundation for the sentence. The record reflected the trial court's careful consideration of this particular defendant, the facts and defendant's efforts to rehabilitate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence.

State v. Huls


95 KA 0541


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0541 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/29/96); 676 So. 2d 160; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1547



May 29, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 66105), PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE BRUCE C. BENNETT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The conviction is AFFIRMED. The sentence is AFFIRMED as AMENDED. The case is REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which found him guilty of second-degree murder, claiming that his trial was unconstitutional and unfair.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his ex-wife and was indicted for first-degree murder. Defendant was found guilty of second-degree murder and appealed his conviction. Although the court held that the allotment method used to select the trial judge was illegal, the error was harmless because the evidence of defendant's guilty was overwhelming. The court also determined that defendant's statements to the police prior to requesting an attorney were properly admitted at trial because he failed to argue this point in his motion to suppress and thus waived it. The court further stated that exculpatory material from witnesses that was disclosed at the trial did not warrant a new trial because defendant had time to review the evidence before the witnesses testified. In addition, the court held that the jury was not biased, and photographs of the victim were correctly admitted at trial, because they were not prejudicial. Finally, the court concluded that the evidence was sufficient for a jury to find defendant guilty of second-degree murder and the jury instructions were free from error. The court affirmed the conviction and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Nazar


No. 96-K-0175


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0175 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/24/96); 675 So. 2d 780; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 931



May 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIORARI FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-912, SECTION "A". HONORABLE MORRIS W. REED, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) that reversed criminal defendant's conviction of simple battery and acquitted him of the charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of simple battery. However his conviction was later reversed and he was acquitted of the charge. In affirming the decision in part, the court held that it was error to clarify the verdict to guilt of simple battery. The trial court had no authority to vacate a prior verdict of guilty on attempted simple battery, even though not a recognized crime, and to find defendant guilty of the greater offense of simple battery. The original verdict of guilty of attempted simple battery was a non-crime and invalid. Nevertheless, the verdict of guilty of a non-crime could not serve as an acquittal or a conviction for double jeopardy purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that reversed defendant's conviction and sentence, but reversed defendant's acquittal, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Wheeler v. Louisiana DOT & Dev.


No. 95-CA-1700


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1700 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/24/96); 675 So. 2d 788; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 924



May 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 91-8895, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division E (Louisiana), which ordered that the state pay pre-judgment interest to appellees insureds and insurer, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. Art. 2924.


OVERVIEW: The insureds, husband and wife, filed an action against the state seeking damages for personal injuries and loss of consortium, sustained as a result of an injury to the husband while in the course and scope of his employment. The husband's employer was insured under a worker's compensation policy. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the insureds and the insurer. The state forwarded checks for satisfaction of the judgment, with pre-judgment interested computed at six-percent interest pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5112(C). The insureds and the insurer reserved the right to dispute the calculation of the pre-judgment interest. The state filed several procedural exceptions. The trial court overruled the exceptions and ordered the pre-judgment interest to be paid pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2924. The court held that the parties reserved their rights and were entitled to pre-judgment interest. The court noted that whether or not the trial court intended that pre-judgment legal interest on the award of damages was to be paid pursuant to the statute, was an incidental question arising in the course of judicial proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment ordering the state to pay pre-judgment interest to the insureds and insurer pursuant to statutory requirements.

 

612 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Marine Mktg. Servs. v. Louisiana Dep't of Ins.


95 CA 1879


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1879 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/96); 673 So. 2d 335; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 972



May 10, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 414,383), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE FRANK SAIA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reverse the lower court's finding. The Commissioner's Cease and Desist Order and the ruling of the administrative law judge sanctioning MMS are vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed from a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed the finding of the administrative law judge that the insurer was transacting insurance business without authority granted by plaintiff Louisiana Department of Insurance (department).


OVERVIEW: The department audited the insurer and challenged its policies on recreational boats. The department then issued a cease and desist order and a show cause order. The administrative law judge issued a ruling affirming the cease and desist order and fined the insurer. The insurer appealed to the trial court, which affirmed. The insurer appealed and argued that it was exempt from the authorization requirements under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1247(B)(7) as a marine insurer. The court noted that the trial court found that an insurer was exempt only when a vessel was in use in water and therefore the policy provisions which provided coverage if the boat was stolen on land violated the statute. The court held that the statute exempted insurers of vessels whether the vessels were on land or in use in water. The court found that the administrative law judge and trial court improperly considered the legislative intent of a clear and unambiguous statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

613 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Denomes


No. 95 KA 1201


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1201 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/96); 674 So. 2d 465; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 975



May 10, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST TAMMANY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. SUIT NO. 214317. HONORABLE JOHN W. GREENE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana, convicting defendant of one count of aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15: 529. Defendant argued that certain provisions of the statute were unconstitutional, that the trial court improperly relied on a conviction from the state of California, and that he was not properly informed of his rights in the habitual offender proceedings. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the § 15: 529 was presumed constitutional. Defendant had the burden of showing that the statute was unconstitutional. The court stated that the challenged statutory provisions did not violate defendant's rights to due process and fair trial under the Louisiana Constitution. Second, the court held that the trial court did not err by using the California plea to find defendant as a habitual offender because the state showed that defendant was represented by counsel when he entered his plea. The burden then shifted to defendant and defendant failed to show that there was an irregularity in the procedure. Third, the court held that although defendant was not properly informed of his rights, there was no prejudice because he plead not guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded the case to give defendant credit for time served.

 

614 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Risk Exch.


NUMBER 95 CA 2199


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2199 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/96); 674 So. 2d 484; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 990



May 10, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 399,595. Honorable Bob H. Hester, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant director of a failed insurance company complained of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, which was rendered in favor of plaintiff Commissioner of Insurance for the State of Louisiana to recover payments arising out of certain subordinated surplus debentures of the insurance company.


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana Supreme Court had the authority to appoint the trial judge, the director failed to make such complaint to the trial court, and the judge did not try this case, so his authority or jurisdiction had no relevance to the judgment. The commissioner was acting under an order of liquidation that empowered him to deal with the insurance company's business. An insurer's business includes filing suit to collect monies owed to it. Thus, no court approval was necessary to bring this suit. The commissioner succeeded to all rights of the insurance company, which had a right of action against the debenture holders for return of any payments made which were not due. While he might also have had an action against them under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 745.1 or 745.3, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 745.3(K)(3) specifically permitted other types of claims, and his action was neither preempted nor prescribed. The trial court found "sums were paid in violation of the language in the debenture itself." The court interpreted this as a finding of undercapitalization. The director was not entitled to a setoff because the insurance company owed her no debt; any obligation to repay the debentures was null.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that the commissioner was entitled to recover payments arising out of certain subordinated surplus debentures of the insurance company.

 

615 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 28,095-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,095 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/08/96); 674 So. 2d 1018; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 846



May 8, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 93-F0628. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), in which he was convicted of aggravated burglary, adjudicated to be a habitual offender, and sentenced to 30 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: defendant was convicted of aggravated burglary, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60, after he forcibly entered the victim's car and sexually assaulted her. Following the attack she arrived at a friend's home bloody and disheveled. She gave a description of defendant, his car, and license plate number. The court held that the description gave police sufficient information to have probable cause to arrest defendant. The court found that a photo array out of which the victim picked defendant was not suggestive even though it had a 12-digit number on the bottom that contained the date of the photograph. The court held that a mistrial was properly granted under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 775 after the jury could not reach a verdict on attempted rape charges. The court found that double jeopardy did not attach pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 591. The prosecution was entitled to sever charges against defendant for his first trial and then rejoin them for the second trial. Defendant made no showing that he was prejudiced. Specific intent to commit a sexual battery was properly inferred from evidence that defendant touched the victim's breast.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

616 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baker


No. 28,152-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,152 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/08/96); 674 So. 2d 1108; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 861



May 8, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 20, 1996. Released for Publication June 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 30,112. Honorable Robert Y. Butler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana, which convicted him of one count of distribution of a Schedule II Controlled Dangerous Substance, cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 40:967A, and sentenced him to 10 years in prison at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant urged that the deputies' identification of him was unreliable and that the testimony of the defense witnesses refuted the State's chain of evidence. The court found that the testimony of defendant and his friends and relatives was not "physical evidence" that he owned or wore no pants with pockets, and the testimony did not dispute the State's chain of evidence. Defendant also contended that the State offered no proof that his conduct was not pursuant to a valid prescription or order of a practitioner. The court found, however, that neither the statute under which defendant was charged, nor any other statute, required the State to prove the absence of a prescription. The court also found that the participation by the confidential informant (CI) by introduction of the agent was precisely the type of de minimis role that did not to warrant disclosure of the CI. The court held that the prosecutor's conclusion regarding the evidence that was reasonably drawn from the evidence was not improper. Further, the court found nothing it considered to be error patent under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

617 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Gygax v. Brugoto


No. 95-CA-1995


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1995 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/08/96); 674 So. 2d 366; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 910



May 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE 34th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, ST. BERNARD PARISH. NO. 61-621, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE DAVID S. GORBATY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED & RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA), as successor in liquidation of defendant insurer, sought review of the judgment of the 34th Judicial District Court, St. Bernard Parish, Division B (Louisiana), which did not apply La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1379(3)(d) and ordered LIGA to pay all interest and costs awarded in plaintiff worker's suit, whether incurred before or after the insurer's insolvency.


OVERVIEW: The insurer became insolvent following the entry of judgment against it and the insureds for damages of $ 215,000 sustained by the worker in an accident. As the insurer's legal successor in liquidation, LIGA was added as a defendant and raised issues founded on the law applicable to LIGA. On appeal from the trial court's judgment, LIGA argued that its liability was capped by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1382(A)(1)(a) at $ 149,900, including interest. In reversing, the court ruled that § 22:1382(A)(1)(a) did indeed limit LIGA's liability but that court costs were excepted from the limit and that the effect of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1379(3)(d) was to limit recovery of court costs to those incurred after insolvency of the insurer. The court noted that, at the time of the accident giving rise to the insurer's liability, § 22:1379(3)(d) did not limit recovery of court costs but that at the time of the insurer's insolvency, the § 22:1379(3)(d) limitation had come into effect. The court ruled that the right of action against RIGA did not arise until such insolvency and that, therefore, the law in effect at that time, including § 22:1379(3)(d), was applicable to the worker's claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered judgment for the worker against the insureds and LIGA, limiting LIGA's liability to its statutory limit, plus court costs accruing after the insurer's insolvency.

Sonnier v. Opelousas Gen. Hosp.


NUMBER 95-1560


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1560 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/08/96); 688 So. 2d 1040; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1030



May 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Alonzo Harris, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed the decision from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which found for plaintiff patient in the patient's suit for damages incurred when the patient contracted hepatitis from contaminated blood he was administered while a patient.


OVERVIEW: The patient, treated at the hospital, believed he contracted hepatitis from contaminated blood he was administered while at the hospital. The hospital filed exceptions of prematurity and no right or cause of action which were denied by the trial court. The trial court found for the patient and the hospital appealed. On review the court noted that the transfusion occurred in 1979 but he did not become aware of the hepatitis until 1994 and did not file until 1995. The court also noted the hospital's argument that the claim should have been first submitted to a medical review panel. Under the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(B)(1)(a)(i), all medical claims had to be submitted to a medical review panel before a suit could be filed. Noting this the court reversed the decision for the patient and ordered the suit dismissed as premature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision for the patient in his suit against the hospital and ordered the suit dismissed.

State v. Collins


NUMBER CR95-1503


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1503 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/08/96); 677 So. 2d 500; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1041



May 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Anne L. Simon, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which sentenced defendant to 16 years hard labor after defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: The state charged the defendant with various drug-related crimes. The defendant entered into a plea agreement wherein the defendant pled guilty to the charge of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute and the remaining charges were dismissed. The trial court sentenced the defendant to 16 years hard labor. On appeal, the court affirmed the sentence. The court held that the trial court correctly decided that it was not bound by the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines, which had been repealed before sentencing, that the sentence fell within the sentencing range of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967B, and that the trial court properly considered defendant's previous convictions for aggravated battery and other violent acts. However, the court remanded the case so that the trial court could credit defendant for time served pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 880. The court also rejected defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim because defendant's counsel did pursue appeal of the sentencing decision based on a non-frivolous argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had sentenced defendant to 16 years hard labor after he pled guilty to the charge of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute and remanded to enter credit for time served.

 

620 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. Cr 95-1688


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1688 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/08/96); 677 So. 2d 480; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1067



May 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERNON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE TED R. BROYLES, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number: 49674.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Vernon Parish (Louisiana), which denied his motion to reconsider his sentence after defendant entered a plea of no contest to two counts of aggravated incest, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1A and B, and was sentenced pursuant to the plea agreement.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920, the court reviewed the record for errors patent on its face and found no errors patent. Defendant argued that the district court erred in imposing an excessive sentence and failed to give adequate consideration to mitigating factors. Defendant was sentenced after the repeal of the sentencing guidelines therefore the sentence was only reviewed for constitutional excessiveness. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor on both counts to run concurrently with each other, less than the maximum of 20 years provided by law. The court held that the trial court was not required to articulate every circumstance or read through a checklist of items to comply with the requirements of La. Code Crim. P. art. 894.1, and that the trial court's failure to do so would not result in a remand for resentencing when there was an adequate factual basis in the record for the sentence. The court found that it was not unconstitutional to assess an indigent defendant a fine and costs as special conditions of probation, as long as jail time was not ordered in the event of default.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences imposed by the district court.

 

621 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Pellegrini v. Crellin


No. 95-CA-2654


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2654 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/08/96); 674 So. 2d 463; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1518



May 8, 1996, Decided  
May 8, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 31, 1996. Released for Publication May 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-17208, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.

Reported in Table Case Format at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1283.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In response to appellant's amended and supplemental petition, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220, seeking damages for failure to settle in a fair and prompt manner, appellee insurer filed an exception of no cause of action. The Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) maintained the insurer's exception of no cause of action and dismissed the first amended and supplemental petition with prejudice. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was rear-ended by a car driven by an insured of the insurer. After the insurer answered appellant's original petition for damages, appellant filed a supplemental and amending petition seeking damages from the insurer for their failure to settle in a fair and prompt manner. Appellant based his claim on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220. The court noted that the duty imposed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(A) was a duty owed by the insurer to its insured. The duty could be breached in any of the ways listed in § 22:1220(B). In arguing that the insurer was liable to him for failing to settle in a fair and prompt manner and in failing to make a reasonable effort to settle the claim, appellant sought to bring himself within the coverage provided by § 22:1220(B)(5). However, according to the court, the language of § 22:1220(B)(5) allowed only an insured to state a claim under that subsection. Accordingly, the court held that because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(B)(5) granted a right of action to the insured only, and appellant failed to state a cause of action under § 22:1220(B)(1) - (B)(4), the trial court correctly granted the insurer's exception of no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement of the trial court granting the insurer's exception of no cause of action.

Billingsley v. City of Baton Rouge


No. 95 CA 2162


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2162 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/30/96; 673 So. 2d 300; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 985



April 30, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 396,387. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, personnel administrator, and civil service board (board), appealed from a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found that the board exceeded its authority in limiting accumulation of vacation days for plaintiff police officers.


OVERVIEW: The officers filed an action against defendants for a declaratory judgment that the board's policy which limited vacation time accumulated to that earned during the last five years violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2214. The trial court rendered judgment in the officers' favor and defendants appealed. The court noted that under § 33:2214 an employee must be granted 15 days of vacation each year after one year of service but that § 33:2214 did not address accumulation of leave. The court held that under its decisionmaking authority the board had the right to promulgate rules relating to the accumulation of leave if they were not contrary to law. The court held that the trial court erred in entering judgment for the officers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dismissed the officers' petitions for declaratory relief.

Adams v. City of Baton Rouge


No. 95 CW 2515


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2515 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/30/96); 673 So. 2d 624; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 992



April 30, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 398,693, 403,380, 405,016, 405,674. Honorable Joseph M. Keogh, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT MADE PEREMPTORY. JUDGMENT STRIKING REQUEST FOR JURY TRIAL REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Parish of East Baton Rouge sought review of a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found that the parish was not entitled to a jury trial, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105, in a wrongful death suit initiated by plaintiff survivor which alleged negligent maintenance and design of a roadway shoulder and guardrail.


OVERVIEW: During the pendency of the survivor's wrongful death action against the Parish the legislature amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105 to provide that the Parish had the right to request a jury trial in civil actions filed against it. The court found that the right to a jury trial in a civil action was governed by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 1731 and 1732 and that it was not a constitutionally guaranteed right. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105 was a procedural statute and that it could be applied retrospectively because the legislature had not expressed a contrary intent. Although the Parish made its request for a jury trial more than ten days after the last pleading, contemplated by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1733(C), the court found that the request was timely because it was made within ten days of the effective date of the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for a jury trial.

Ostheimer v. Venvirotek, Inc.


NUMBER 95 CA 2126


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2126 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/30/96); 674 So. 2d 337; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1002



April 30, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF TERREBONNE STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 109,520. HONORABLE JOHN T. PETTIGREW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED, REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a parcel owner and its mortgagee, sought review of the judgment of the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which sustained plaintiff tract owners' exception of no cause of action, dismissed the mortgagee's answer and intervention, and rendered partial summary judgment in favor of the tract owners, invalidating all but one of the parcel owner's rights of way over the tract owners' property.


OVERVIEW: The tract owners acquired property enclosing the parcel owner's lot from a lienor that had purchased the tract in its execution sale. The tract owners filed suit for declaratory and injunctive relief against the parcel owner's easements for roads and a pipeline. The parcel owner answered, and its mortgagee sought to intervene and answer. On appeal from the trial court's adverse judgment granting partial summary judgment, the parcel owner and its mortgagee argued that the mortgagee received no notice of the execution by the tract owners' predecessor, that no motion for summary judgment was filed against the mortgagee, and that the parcel owner had a right of way by necessity under La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 689 - 696. In dismissing the parcel owner's appeal, the court held that the partial summary judgment was interlocutory because it did not grant relief but merely foreclosed one basis of defense and that, under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2083, the judgment was unappealable. In reversing as to the mortgagee, the court held that a no cause of action exception was an inappropriate device to oppose a petition to intervene and no relief had been requested against the mortgagee.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the parcel owner's appeal, reversed the trial court's judgment sustaining the exception of no cause of action and granting partial summary judgment dismissing the mortgagee's intervention, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Blanchard v. City Parish of E. Baton Rouge


No. 95 CW 2011


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2011 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/30/96); 674 So. 2d 317; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1009



April 30, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 384,043. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT MADE PEREMPTORY. JUDGMENT STRIKING REQUEST FOR JURY TRIAL REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Parish of East Baton Rouge sought review of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which denied its request for a jury trial, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(C) on claims brought be plaintiff protesters who were detained by public safety officers while they were participating in an anti-abortion rally.


OVERVIEW: The trial court refused to address issues related to the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105, stated that the Parish's request was untimely, and that there was not showing that the amount in controversy exceeded the jurisdictional amount. The court held that the statute had retrospective application because it effected a procedural right rather then a substantive right. The court affirmed the constitutionality of this statute. Although the Parish did not request a jury trial within ten days of the last pleading, as contemplated by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1733, the Parish's request was timely because it was within ten days of the effective date of the statute. The court held that the burden was on the protester's to prove that the amount in controversy was less than the jurisdictional limit. The court held that an amendment to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1732 which raised the jurisdictional limit to $ 50,000 was interpretive law which could not be applied retrospectively. Therefore the court found that the jurisdictional limit for this action, initiated before the amendment remained at $ 20,000.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded for a jury trial.

Succession of Jurisich


No. 94-CA-1262


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1262 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/25/96); 694 So. 2d 928; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 716



April 25, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 31, 1996. Released for Publication May 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 91-17112, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE YADA T. MAGEE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, adult children of the deceased, appealed the judgment of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which found that the last will and testament of the deceased, the children's father, was valid.


OVERVIEW: The deceased's will specifically stated that he was excluding his six children from his will because they had not contacted him for more than a period of two years. The children challenged the will contending that they had tried to contact their father and further that the disinheritance was based on the undue influence of their father's second wife. The trial court upheld the will and the children appealed. The court affirmed after reviewing the extensive testimony. The court held that the deceased could legally exclude his adult children under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1621 if they failed to contact him over a two-year period. The court noted that the children's alienation from their father spanned a period of 14 years and that the children failed to prove that the cause stipulated for disinheritance did not exist or that they had reconciled with the deceased. The court rejected the children's contention that the deceased's wife was the cause of the alienation. The court further held that the children failed to prove that that the deceased's will was made under the fraud or duress of his wife, noting that the wife was not even present when the will was executed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Levron v. State ex rel. Department of Health & Hosps.


No. 94-CA-2094


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-2094 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/24/96); 673 So. 2d 279; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 717



April 24, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 31, 1996. Released for Publication May 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 92-6924, DIVISION "E", HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND AMENDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants doctor and hospital sought review of a decision of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff patient and awarded him damages for medical malpractice after he was forced to undergo a liver transplant. The patient challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(F) which limited the patient's recovery to $ 500,000.


OVERVIEW: The doctor breached the standard of care for physicians, set forth by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2794(A), when he prescribed PTU, a hepatotoxic agent used for the treatment of Grave's disease, to the patient who suffered from liver problems. The court found that the doctor breached the standard of care when he failed to notify the patient immediately after test results indicated that he was suffering from serious liver dysfunction. The doctor waited until the patient's next scheduled appointment before he reviewed the test results. The patient was forced to undergo a liver transplant. The court found that the patient proved that he lost a chance to save his liver as a proximate result of the doctor's negligence. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2794(A)(3) did not require the patient to prove that he would not have needed the transplant anyway. The trial court properly awarded interest on the judgment from the time the patient requested that a medical review board be convened, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39.1(K). The court held that the $ 500,000 ceiling on medical malpractice awards, based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(F), was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment to award the patient interest on the judgment from the time he requested that a medical review board be convened, and affirmed.

In re E. I. du Pont de Nemours & Co.


No. 94 CA 2549


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2549 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/24/96); 674 So. 2d 1007; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 952



April 24, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1996. Released for Publication June 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. Glenn A. Miller, Assistant Secretary.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant community and environmental organizations sought review of the decision of appellee Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) (Louisiana), which granted appellee chemical company an exemption from Louisiana's land disposal restrictions pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2193.


OVERVIEW: The chemical company injected fluid hazardous waste into porous rock formations below the ground surface. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2193 the deep-well injection of hazardous waste was prohibited unless an exemption was granted by the DEQ. The DEQ granted an exemption and the community and environmental organizations appealed. The court found that the organizations had a real and actual interest that was or could be adversely affected by the DEQ's decision and thus had standing under § 30:2024(C). The court held that in reaching a decision the DEQ was required to make basic findings supported by evidence and ultimate findings that flowed rationally from the basic findings and it had to articulate a rational connection between the facts found and the order used. The court found that the letter notifying the chemical company that the permit had been granted under certain conditions contained no basic findings supported by the evidence, ultimate findings, or an articulated rational connection between the facts found and the order issued. The court held that in the absence of such findings the petition was approved erroneously without proper evaluation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and set aside the DEQ's approval of the chemical company's petition for an exemption from the land disposal restrictions and remanded for the issuance of findings to support the approval.

Thompson v. State of LA


94 CA 2610 CONSOLIDATED WITH 94 CA 2611


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2610 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/23/96); 688 So. 2d 9; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 828



April 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 15, 1996. Limited Rehearing Granted December 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3266. Released for Publication January 6, 1997. Rehearing of December 30, 1996, Reported at: 688 So. 2d 9 at 23.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 9101175), PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE JAMES E. KUHN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiffs, a driver, the driver's wife, and a passenger, against defendant Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) to obtain damages for personal injuries sustained by the driver and the passenger in a vehicular accident on a state highway, the DOTD sought review of the judgments of the 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana) in favor of the driver, the wife, and the passenger.


OVERVIEW: The driver and the passenger were traveling down a state highway that was located on a federal enclave when their car collided with another vehicle. The driver, the passenger, and the wife alleged that the accident was caused when the driver's car struck an overhanging or felled tree limb. The trial court held that the DOTD was strictly liable under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2317. On appeal, the court reversed. The trial court improperly found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:347 gave the DOTD the authority to cut trees hanging over the highway. The trial court erroneously relied on a contract between the State and a contractor in determining that the trees with overhanging limbs were growing within a DOTD right-of-way through federal property; the contract was for a different highway and was irrelevant. The trial court improperly relied on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2317 in imposing liability. The felled tree limb was a temporary condition, not a defect; furthermore, the trees were outside of the DOTD's right-of-way and were therefore outside its ownership. Because the DOTD did not have notice of the alleged hazard, it was not negligent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court.

State v. Morgan


No. 96-K-0354


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0354 (La.App. 4 Cir.04/17/96); 673 So. 2d 256; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 646



April 17, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 377-018, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION GRANTED, SENTENCE VACATED, CASE REMANDED FOR RESE1NTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought a writ of certiorari and prohibition to the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), asking the court to review what the State alleged to be an illegally lenient sentence of seven years at hard labor, 13 years less than the mandatory minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law for a fourth felony offense for defendant's conviction for simple burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27(62).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of simple burglary, and the State filed a multiple offender bill charging defendant as a fourth felony offender. The trial court sentenced defendant to seven years at hard labor, 13 years less than the mandatory minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law of 20 years at hard labor. On appeal, the court found that the trial court clearly understood that before a sentence could be reduced below the mandatory minimum, the trial court was required to find that the mandatory minimum sentence was unconstitutionally excessive as to defendant. The court found that the conclusory statements of the trial court, however, did not constitute the type of "meaningful assessment" sufficient to justify imposing a sentence below the mandatory minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law. Resentencing was required.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's application, vacated defendant's sentence, and remanded the case for resentencing.

State v. Bolden


NUMBER Cr95-749


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-749 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/17/96); 680 So. 2d 6; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1063



April 17, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, Honorable Michael S. Ingram, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 238,403.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for perjury from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was acquitted of the murder of a college woman. Several years later, he confessed to the murder to police in New Jersey. He was then extradited to Louisiana where he was convicted of committing perjury during the earlier murder trial. He was sentenced to ten years in prison. The court affirmed, rejecting as without merit the numerous errors raised by defendant on appeal. The court held that the evidence introduced in the perjury trial did not constitute a relitigation of the issues and that the state did not violate the collateral estoppel doctrine. The State limited its presentation to evidence that corroborated the confession and the murder. Testimony of the forensic pathologist and autopsy photos corroborated that physical contact had occurred, contrary to defendant's prior testimony, and that manual strangulation was the cause of the death. The court held that the State did not err in using excerpted portions of defendant's prior trial testimony, where it used only testimony that was relevant to the perjury charge. Jurors' prior knowledge that defendant had confessed to the murders did not prejudice defendant because the confession was used at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

632 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Carollo


95 CA 1840


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1840 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/04/96); 674 So. 2d 283; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 801



April 4, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 9314754, Division "B". Honorable Stephen A. Duczer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a legal malpractice case, plaintiff, a former client, appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which granted the attorney's motion for summary judgment based on the plea of prescription and/or peremption.


OVERVIEW: The client filed a legal malpractice suit against his former attorney alleging that a document prepared by the attorney damaged him in a succession suit. The attorney raised the plea of prescription of one year and peremption of three years, and the court granted summary judgment in the attorney's favor. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 9:5606 legislatively abrogated the ten-year prescriptive period for breach of contract in legal malpractice claims. The court held that the client's claim was untimely because the statute similarly reduced the time period within which his breach of contract claim could be brought. The court also held that the clients claim was perempted when the statutory grace period expired. The issue of whether the statute was unconstitutional was not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court granting the attorney's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.

 

633 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Salat


No. 95 KA 0072


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0072 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/04/96); 672 So. 2d 333; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 802



April 4, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 1996.
Writ denied by State v. Salat, 679 So. 2d 1378, 1996 La. LEXIS 2630 (La., Oct. 4, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. TRIAL COURT NO. 7-92-1867. HONORABLE MICHAEL R. ERWIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Salat, 623 So. 2d 1284, 1993 La. LEXIS 2373 (La., 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an attorney, sought review of an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which entered judgment convicting him of six counts of filing false public records under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:133 and sentenced him to six two-year concurrent sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a deputy clerk backdate six petitions filed in the clerk of court's office. Defendant argued that the indictment did not set out a crime punishable by law, that the filing of a petition for damages containing incorrect information was not a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:133, and that the definition of "public record" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44: 1(A)(2) was not met by the petitions he filed. The charge was not that defendant filed incorrect pleadings, but that he knowingly and intentionally filed false documents into a public record, the behavior which La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:133 sought to punish. The court found that it was clear that the jury must have believed that defendant had knowledge that the petitions he filed alleged false dates of filing, that any rational trier of fact could have found that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the sentence, of six two-year concurrent sentences, was not excessive. The statutory maximum under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:133 would have been six five-year sentences, to run consecutively, or thirty years. The court held that the sentence was commensurate with the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment of conviction and sentencing of defendant for filing false public records.

 

634 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Meredith v. Ieyoub


No. 95 CA 0719


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0719 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/04/96); 672 So. 2d 375; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 809



April 4, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 412,269. Honorable A. Foster Sanders, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney general and intervenor law firms sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which, in a suit filed by plaintiff oil producers and their association, invalidated a contingent fee contract between the attorney general and the law firms for enforcement of the state's environmental laws and enjoined the performance of the contract.


OVERVIEW: The oil producers and their association filed suit to invalidate the attorney general's contract employing the law firms to enforce the state's environmental laws for contingent fees. On appeal from the judgment invalidating the contract and enjoining performance, the attorney general and the law firms argued that the oil producers and their association lacked standing and that the trial court erred in finding contingent fees to be invalid. In affirming, the court ruled that taxpayers had sufficient interest at stake to confer standing under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 681 and that irreparable harm was not required where the challenged actions were unlawful. The court also ruled that, while the attorney general was the state's chief legal officer under La. Const. art. IV, § 8 and was authorized to hire outside counsel, the law firms' receipts from environmental violators were state funds and La. Const. art. VII, § 9 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2205(A)(1) were explicit in requiring all funds recovered in environmental enforcement actions to be deposited in the state treasury. The court ruled that contingent fees were permitted only where specifically authorized by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

635 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Carver, Inc. v. Department of Pub. Safety & Corrections


No. 95 CA 1664


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1664 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/04/96); 672 So. 2d 1141; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 813



April 4, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 16, 1996. Rehearing Denied May 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 412,620. Honorable William H. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed a hearing officer's determination that defendant Louisiana Video Gaming Division was entitled to revoke the restaurant's video gaming license on the ground that it allowed a minor to play or operate a video poker device.


OVERVIEW: The Division issued a citation to the restaurant and proposed to revoke the restaurant's video gaming license on the grounds that it allowed a minor to play or operate a video poker device and failed to provide an employee to prevent access to the gaming area by minors, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4862.19(A); La. Admin. Code tit. 42 §§ XI:2417(A)(5), XI:2415(C)(1)(b)(iii). A hearing officer, finding that she had no authority to review the constitutionality of the applicable statutes, found that the restaurant was responsible for the violations and affirmed the proposed license revocation. The trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. Revocation of the restaurant's license was not too harsh a penalty; revocation was required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4862.19(B). The hearing officer's decision was not contrary to the evidence; while there was conflicting testimony as to whether a child actually entered the video gaming area, the officer's credibility determinations were entitled to great deference. Evidence of the restaurant's voluntary actions was sufficient to establish the intent required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4862.19(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

636 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Boyle v. Board of Supervisors of La. State Univ. & Agric. & Mech. College


NUMBER 95 CA 1803


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1803 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/04/96); 672 So. 2d 254; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 825



April 4, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 354,567. Honorable Paul B. Landry, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state university appealed an order from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of plaintiffs, an accident victim and her husband, in an action seeking damages for injuries sustained when the victim slipped and fell on the university campus.


OVERVIEW: The victim slipped and fell on a half-inch crack in a sidewalk. The university challenged the trial court's finding that it was liable for the resulting injuries, finding that the victim's witness was an expert, and finding that the university had knowledge of the defect. The court affirmed the judgment. First, the court held that the victim's witness was properly qualified as an expert witness because the witness had the necessary knowledge and experience. Second, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the half-inch crack rendered the sidewalk defective. The university's expert witness testimony that a depression of less than two inches was not defective was based on personal opinion. Third, the court held that although the university did not have actual knowledge of the depression, there was evidence that the defect had existed for a number of years. Given the length of time the defect existed and the opportunity the university had to discover it, together with the testimony that it would have been discovered had the university made routine inspections, the trial court's findings were not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Pardue


No. 28,264-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,264 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/03/96); 671 So. 2d 1226; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 582



April 3, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 56,400A. Honorable Harmon Drew, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his sentences, imposed after a guilty plea to two counts of rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43, from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster (Louisiana). The trial court imposed consecutive 15-year hard-labor sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, 19 years old at the time of the offenses, was babysitting his half-sisters, aged 8 and aged 6. He forced both children to remove their clothing, penetrated the eight-year old anally, and hit her when she cried, causing her nose to bleed and forced the six-year old to submit to vaginal and oral sex with him. The sentencing guidelines recommended a 7-9 year sentence on each count, but the trial judge departed from the guidelines. The court held that the trial court was justified in departing from the guidelines. The court noted that defendant had received an enormous benefit from his plea agreement, which reduced the original charges of aggravated rape, which carried a possible life sentence. The court further noted that defendant had a significant juvenile record, an adult record with felony convictions, and was a drug user. Finally, the court noted that defendant had showed no remorse at the time of sentencing, merely inquiring when he would be eligible for parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's consecutive 15-year sentences.
