State v. Shaw


NOS. 27,892-KA, 27,893-KA (consolidated cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,892 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/03/96); 672 So. 2d 237; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 564



April 3, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 1996.
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Tolliver, 753 So. 2d 958, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 283 (La.App. 2 Cir., Mar. 1, 2000)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Sumler v. State, 760 So. 2d 336, 2000 La. LEXIS 1227 (La., Apr. 20, 2000)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Shaw v. State, 38 So. 3d 351, 2010 La. LEXIS 1629 (La., June 25, 2010)
Writ granted by State v. Shaw, 140 So. 3d 1163, 2014 La. LEXIS 1388 (La., June 20, 2014)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Sumler, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 774 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 2, 2017)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Shaw, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 868 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 17, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 93-F1081. Honorable Carl Van Sharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which convicted them of second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and sentenced them to life at hard labor without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted jointly with another for the shooting and robbery of a fourth man who had won all their money in a dice game. The other perpetrator was severed at the time of trial for appointment of a sanity commission. Defendants appealed their convictions, arguing, among other points, that the evidence was insufficient and that a continuance should have been granted when the proceedings were severed. In affirming, the court found that the evidence was sufficient for any rational trier of fact to have found the essential elements of the crime were proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 704, jointly indicted defendants were tried jointly unless the trial court elected to try them separately, and that once the other perpetrator's mental capacity was raised, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 642 suspended the proceedings as to him, but not as to defendants, and severance was proper. The court also ruled that, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 707 and 712, the decision on the continuance was within the trial court's discretion and was not disturbed, absent an abuse resulting in prejudice to defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions and sentences of defendants.

Parochial Emples. Retirement Sys. v. Caddo Parish Comm'n


95 CA 0243


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0243 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/15/96); 676 So. 2d 105; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 829



March 15, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 408,200), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE JOSEPH F. KEOGH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parish retirement system sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which sustained an exception of prematurity and dismissed its petition for declaratory judgment against appellee parish commission, finding that the system was required to hold a hearing to determine the rights of the employees at issue before filing a declaratory action in district court.


OVERVIEW: After learning that several parish employees had withdrawn their retirement funds from the system to participate in the parish commission's program, the system advised the commission of the mandatory membership provisions applicable to parish employees and stated that it would file a lawsuit in district court to compel the employees at issue to be enrolled in the system. The trial court found that the system was required under the Louisiana Administrative Procedure Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:950, et seq., to hold an adjudicatory hearing before it could file a declaratory action in district court. On appeal, the court noted that one's right to retirement funds constituted a property right. The court found, however, that there was no governmental action that deprived any person of such a right because the system's decision to file suit did not deprive any person of property. Therefore, the court concluded that the trial court erred in granting the exception of prematurity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the exception of prematurity, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Board of Comm'rs v. Connick


No. 95-CA-1456


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1456 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/14/96); 671 So. 2d 1004; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 498



March 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-19508, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GARVEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant levee board appealed an award of attorney's fees to appellee district attorney due to the wrongful issuance of a temporary restraining order in the Civil District Court, For the Parish of Orleans, Division C (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: The district attorney directed a grand jury to investigate possible gambling violations at a casino. Since the levee board derived income from leasing space to the casino, it sought injunctive and declaratory relief to prevent indictment or prosecution. The trial court issued the order, and the district attorney moved to dissolve it, along with peremptory exceptions. The trial court dissolved the temporary restraining order (TRO), denied the motion for preliminary injunction, held the statute unconstitutional and dismissed the peremptory exceptions. The case was appealed directly to the supreme court, which affirmed the trial court's dissolution of the TRO as well as denial of the levee board's motion for preliminary injunction, reversed the unconstitutionality of the statute, maintained the district attorney's peremptory exceptions, and dismissed the suit. The district attorney filed for damages and attorney fees, which were granted. The levee board appealed, and the court held that as two assistant district attorneys, regularly employed, worked on the case, the office was deprived of their regular service, entitling it to an amount for their fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court for the district attorney.

Anne Lind & Assocs. v. Orleans Private Indus.


No. 95-CA-0462


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0462 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/14/96); 673 So. 2d 227; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 496



March 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused May 31, 1996. Released for Publication May 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-9176, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART & REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bidder sought review of the judgment of the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans, Division A (Louisiana), which had held in favor of defendant Orleans Private Industry Council. The bidder argued that the trial court erred in finding that the bidder's suit was premature as she had not exhausted all of her administrative remedies and the suit should have been adjudicated through administrative procedures prior to its filing.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the Orleans Private Industry Council solicited bids for software to be used in computer labs for instruction in a Job Training Partnership Program. The bidder's petition alleged violations of the Public Bid Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:2211 et seq., the procurement laws and the ethics of Louisiana. The trial court held against the bidder. On review, the court the court concluded that the Orleans Private Industry Council was a public corporation, not a private corporation under La. Const. art. 4, § 6 (1921), and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:5107, 13:5109(A) (1992) because of its funding and creators. The court concluded that the trial court properly determined that the bidder's claims based upon the Job Training Partnership Act, 29 C.F.R. 34 et seq., were premature because the Orleans Private Industry Council Program Committee review procedure violated La. Const. art. 1, § 22 in that the review process was arbitrary and an unappealable final administrative decision. The court held that the Orleans Private Industry Council was excluded from the Data Processing Procurement Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 39:196, 39:199(D), and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 39:2(1).


OUTCOME: The court held in favor of the bidder in part. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in part and reversed the trial court's judgment in part.

Bolzoni v. Theriot


No. 95-1233


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1233 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/06/96); 670 So. 2d 783; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 676



March 6, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CAMERON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE H. WARD FONTENOT, DISTRICT JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automobile driver challenged the order of the 38th Judicial District Court, Parish of Cameron (Louisiana), granting appellee insurer summary judgment on the basis that a cow's owner did not knowingly permit the cow to roam on the highway.


OVERVIEW: The driver of an automobile was injured when he hit a cow that was loose on the highway. The driver filed suit, seeking damages for his personal injuries. The cow owner's insurer filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that pursuant to a parish ordinance, the driver had to prove that the cow's owner had to either knowingly or willfully permitted the cow to roam on the highway. The driver filed a supplemental petition adding the state transportation department as a party defendant, alleging that this ordinance was unconstitutional and impermissibly contradicted state law. The court affirmed, finding that the highway at issue was not included in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:2083, so that pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:3001, the parish had the authority to regulated livestock on highways within the parish. Further, the court found that the statute was constitutional where the driver failed to present clear and convincing evidence otherwise. The court then noted that the right to recover in tort was not fundamental right given constitutional protection.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court granting a cow owner's insurer summary judgment in a personal injury suit arising from a collision between the cow and an automobile was affirmed on appeal.

 

643 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Phillips


No. 92-KA-1063


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


92-1063 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/29/96); 670 So. 2d 588; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 347



February 29, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 291-124, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED, MOTIONS GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §14:64, relative to armed robbery, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, relative to convicted felon in possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant cited numerous points of error on appeal. The court affirmed, finding that defendant's assignments of error were without merit or, if error, they were harmless. The court held that a hypothetical situation presented by the court during voir dire was not a comment on the facts or evidence within the purview of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 772, because no evidence had yet been presented in the proceeding. Admission of the contents of a phone call by an unidentified person could be said, beyond a reasonable doubt, not to have contributed to the verdict. Although the testimony was hearsay, it was admissible as part of the res gestae, and supported the victim's testimony that the same person robbed her on both nights in question. Because defendant's arrest for possession of a concealed weapon followed from a legal stop and search, the subsequent identification procedure was not tainted. The trial court's failure to give a circumstantial evidence charge did not constitute reversible error because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction. The failure to give an instruction on circumstantial evidence, assuming that the court failed to do so, was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for armed robbery and possession of a handgun by a convicted felon.

 

644 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flores


No. 27,736-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,736 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/28/96); 669 So. 2d 646; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 333



February 28, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 86,700. Honorable Robert E. Burgess, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana, which convicted him of aggravated incest, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1 and sentenced him to 15 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated incest with his adopted stepdaughter and was sentenced to 15 years hard labor. On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality of aggravated incest statute and argued that the sentence was excessive. The court affirmed and held that statute was not unconstitutional on its face. The court determined that the requirement that the victim be under 18 years of age was not a vague or ambiguous standard. In addition, the statute enumerated a clear list of relatives who could be victims of the offense, specified that the offender had to be aware of his relationship to the victim, and plainly set forth the prohibited acts. The court further determined that although defendant's conduct came within the purview of several statutes, the charge of aggravated incest most closely described defendant's conduct. The court determined that the public policy of protecting juvenile family members from adult relatives far outweighed any unfairness associated with the increased penalty. Moreover, based upon the impact of the crime upon the victim and the duration of defendant's conduct, the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Parker v. St. Tammany Parish Hosp. Serv. Dist.

DISPOSITION: For reasons given herein, the writ of certiorari issued in this case is RECALLED and the application is DENIED. Costs associated with this writ are assessed to Dr. Cazayoux.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor applied for a supervisory writ to the 22nd Judicial District, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which dismissed his exception of prescription and motion to exclude evidence in plaintiff patient's claim for damages.


OVERVIEW: The doctor delivered the patient's baby. There were complications in the delivery and the doctor twisted the baby's head, causing Erb's palsy and diaphragmatic paralysis. The patient sued the doctor for her loss of enjoyment of life, special care and services for the child, and mental anguish damages. The doctor filed an exception of prematurity and argued that the patient had signed a binding arbitration agreement by which she agreed to submit all claims against him to binding arbitration. The doctor then filed an exception of prescription and a motion to exclude evidence. The trial court entered a consent judgment referring the patient's claims to arbitration. The trial court held a hearing on the doctor's motions and dismissed them because it held that they must be submitted to arbitration. The doctor appealed. The court held that because the patient's claims arose out of negligence the doctor was bound by the arbitration agreement. The court found no error in the trial court's ruling.

Phillip v. Home Ins. Co.


No. 95-CA-406


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-406 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/27/96); 671 So. 2d 943; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 642



February 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1996. Rehearing Granted April 17, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1531.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 445-922, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a legal malpractice action, plaintiff clients appealed a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which granted an exception of prescription filed by defendants attorney and his insurer. At issue on appeal were whether a pre-statute breach of contract theory applied, and whether enactment of a statute had disturbed the client's vested right to sue or whether the claim had prescribed prior to enactment.


OVERVIEW: The clients appealed the judgment granting an exception of prescription filed by the attorney and his insurer, in the client's malpractice action. The pre-statute breach of contract theory had not applied, as the clients failed to produce evidence that the attorney warranted a specific result or that he agreed to perform certain work. As to the question of whether the enactment of a statute in 1990, which changed the law, disturbed the client's vested right to sue or whether the claim had prescribed prior to the enactment, the client's filed their action before the cut-off date for the application of the new statute. However, this was irrelevant if the claim was prescribed prior to enactment. The court concluded the client's had the underlying facts necessary to have asserted their cause of action in 1987. It was then that they suffered appreciable damages and then that they knew or should have known that the document would not protect their property from creditors. Thus, the district court had not erred in finding that the claim was prescribed in 1988, under the one year prescriptive period of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492, or under the later enacted statute and its amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed. The costs of the appeal were to have been paid by the clients.

State v. Calhoun


No. 94 KA 2567


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2567 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 669 So. 2d 1351; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 455



February 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 1-94-1488, Honorable Linda Holliday, Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which denied his motion to withdraw his plea of guilty of molestation of a juvenile, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, and sentenced him under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2(B) to six years at hard labor, thereby exceeding the sentencing guidelines of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fraudulently induced young girls to pose for nude photographs with promises of commercial success. The trial court accepted his guilty plea and refused to allow him to withdraw it. On appeal from his conviction and sentence, defendant argued that his sentence was excessive and that he should not have been subjected to registration as a sex offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:540 et seq., which he maintained were unconstitutional. In affirming, the court ruled that the trial court was not required under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 559(A) to permit withdrawal of a knowing and voluntary plea. The court also ruled that defendant was not required to have been informed of the registration and community notification requirements for sex offenders as they were not part of his sentence. The court found that registration and community notification did not violate his privacy rights and were a constitutional means of advancing the compelling state interest in protecting the public from sex offenders. The court held that the trial court stated an adequate basis for exceeding the guidelines of former La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 in imposing sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence of defendant.

State v. Calhoun


No. 94 KA 2568


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2568 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 669 So. 2d 1359; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 456



February 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 2-94-323, Honorable Linda Holliday, Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCED AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), denying his motion to withdraw his guilty plea to the offense of one count of pornography involving juveniles in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1, sentencing him to a maximum sentence of 10 years at hard labor, and ordering him to register as a sexual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's refusal to permit him to withdraw his guilty plea. Defendant videotaped minor girls engaging in sexually compromising acts for his own gratification. The trial court held that defendant's plea was knowing and intelligent. The court opined that because defendant had 12 prior arrests for different crimes, had failed to show remorse, and had inflicted severe emotional damage on the victims, a maximum sentence beyond the statutory guidelines for first-time sexual offenders was appropriate. On appeal, the court held that under the circumstances the sentence was not excessive either under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 or La. Const. art. I, § 20. The trial court articulated sufficient reasons to exceed the recommended sentencing range. However, the trial court erred in ordering defendant to register as a sex offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:540-549 because defendant's offense took place before the effective date of the sexual offender registry statute, i.e., June 18, 1992. As applied to defendant, the registry statute was an invalid ex post facto law under U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10, and La. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and 10-year sentence but reversed the trial court's judgment ordering defendant to register with a statewide sexual offender registry.

Smith v. St. Tammany Sheriff's Office


No. 95 CA 0960


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0960 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 668 So. 2d 1331; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 465



February 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION, STATE OF LOUISIANA, DOCKET NO. 94-06860, DELOS R. JOHNSON, HEARING OFFICER



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision from the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (Louisiana), granting defendant sheriff's exceptions of no cause of action and no right action and denying her claim for benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee contested the dismissal for no cause of action and no right action of her claim for workers' compensation benefits. The employee was injured while working as a school crossing guard in the course and scope of her employment with the parish sheriff's office. On appeal, the court held that the employee was classified as a full-fledged sheriff's deputy and, therefore, was disqualified from receiving worker's compensation benefits by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1034A. Section 23:1034A did not violate the waiver of immunity provision contained in La. Const. art. 12, § 10 (1974). The court rejected the employee's argument that she was not a deputy because she did not have a badge, uniform, or gun or perform traditional law enforcement duties. The fact that she had not completed her oath of office form by signing to indicate that she had received a copy of the state ethics code as required by §§ 42:141 and 42:1162 did not invalidate her employment classification as a deputy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the employee was classified as a sheriff's deputy and, therefore, was disqualified from receiving worker's compensation benefits.

State v. Estate of Griffin


NUMBER 95 CA 1464


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1464 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 669 So. 2d 566; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 488



February 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 20th Judicial District Court in and for West Feliciana Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 13,233. Honorable Wilson R. Ramshur, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought review of a judgment from the 20th Judicial District Court in and for West Feliciana Parish (Louisiana), which dismissed with prejudice the State's expropriation order in a proceeding under the quick-taking statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 48:441 - 48:460, to expropriate additional right of way from defendant landowners for the replacement of a bridge.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the design of the bridge was based on assumptions which, more likely than not, were incorrect and thus concluded that the State was arbitrary and capricious in expropriating the landowners' property on the basis of such design. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, finding that even though the State had wide discretion in determining the necessity and extent of the taking, the State's discretion was not unbridled. The court concluded that an expropriating authority should be in a position to justify and support with cogent reasons a taking for an appropriate purpose. The court found that the State's design engineers could not justify the State's data, particularly traffic counts and hydraulic evaluation used in selecting the design for the bridge. Therefore, the court concluded that the trial court was not manifestly erroneous in finding that the State acted arbitrarily and capriciously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that dismissed with prejudice the State's expropriation order in a proceeding to expropriate additional right of way from the landowners.

 

651 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wingate


95 KW 1874


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1874 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 668 So. 2d 1324; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 493



February 23, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 239,063), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE A. CLAYTON JAMES, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE (FINE) FOR FAILURE TO MAINTAIN RECORDS CONVICTION AFFIRMED. ENTIRE SENTENCE FOR POSSESSION OF UNDERSIZED CATFISH VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING IN ACCORDANCE WITH THE VIEWS EXPRESSED HEREIN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought review by way of writ of application of his misdemeanor convictions for one count of possession of undersized catfish in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:326A(7)(b) and one count of failure to maintain records in violation of § 56:306.4A.


OVERVIEW: By writ of application, relator challenged the trial court's acceptance of his guilty pleas to the misdemeanor offenses of possession of undersized catfish and failure to maintain records. Relator was a Georgia track driver who transported frozen channel catfish across state lines for resale. When stopped by Department of Wildlife and Fisheries agents, as much as 75 percent of the catfish in his truck were undersized in violation of state conservation laws. On appeal, the court held that § 56:326A(7)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague and did not deny relator equal protection of the laws. Relator was more than a mere truck driver--he was a licensed wholesale/retail dealer under § 56:306.B4 and was criminally responsible for transporting undersized catfish because § 56:326A contained no scienter requirement. Relator's 60-day sentence and $ 700 fine were not excessive; however, relator should have been credited with time served. The trial court lacked jurisdiction to make forfeiture of the seized catfish part of relator's sentence because that type of forfeiture was solely within the province of the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries in accordance with §§ 56:58 and 56:60.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed relator's conviction in all respects except for remanding for resentencing to give relator credit for time served.

MRT Exploration Co. v. McNamara


NUMBER 94 CA 0063R, NUMBER 94 CA 0064R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0063 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/96); 669 So. 2d 1338; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 451



February 23, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, SUIT NUMBERS 262,928 AND 323,597, HONORABLE WILLIAM BROWN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought to recover severance taxes paid under protest. The 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Baton Rouge (Louisiana) dismissed the claim, holding that severance tax statutes were valid and enforceable. The district court found for defendant taxation department on its reconventional demand, as it found landowners liable for severance taxes. The landowners filed a writ application that was granted in part.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal was the recovery of severance taxes paid under protest. The landowners contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 52:1 specifically prohibited the levying of severance taxes. They argued that the department's contention that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 52:2 was the controlling statute in the matter, rather than § 52:1, fell when the provisions were compared to La. Const. art. IV, § 12. Section 52:2 had its origin in Act No. 75 of the Louisiana Legislative Session of 1940. Upon analysis, it became obvious that the purpose of the Act was to carry out the provisions of art. IV, § 12. Section 1 of the Act was a verbatim recitation of art. IV, § 12, with § 2 of the Act defining who the authorized representatives were to have been in the event the State or any agency, branch, municipality or subdivision thereof donated or otherwise conveyed to the United States any lands, property, or movable and immovable. Thus, the court found that the department's argument as to the applicability of § 52:2 was without merit. As the court found the pre-amended version of § 52:1 was dispositive of the issue to have been addressed on remand, it was unnecessary to address other arguments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court on the reconventional demand was reversed. The costs of the appeal assessed to the landowners in the original judgment were to have been reassessed and shared pro-rata with the department of revenue and taxation.

 

653 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


No. W 94-598


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-598 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/21/96); 670 So. 2d 493; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 381



February 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 24, 1996. Rehearing Denied April 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, Honorable Lloyd G. Teekell, Judge ad hoc, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs property owners appealed an order from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), finding that the Louisiana Seizure and Controlled Dangerous Substances Property Forfeiture Act of 1989 (ACT), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owners filed a petition alleging that the Act was unconstitutional following the state's seizure of certain property. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. First the court held that statutes were presumed constitutional, and the party challenging a statute's validity must articulate a particular constitutional provision that limits the legislature's powers. The court noted that forfeiture cases were not to be approached in the context of criminal law and in reliance upon criminal precepts, but rather in the context of property law. Forfeiture cases were civil in nature and were governed by the rules of civil procedure. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601 was constitutional in that it did not deprive any of the property owners of due process of the law. Second the court held that pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1732(7), a trial by jury was not available in cases where a jury trial was specifically denied by law. The denial of a jury trial in a civil forfeiture proceeding did not violate the constitution. Lastly, the court held that there was no equal protection violation because the law applied equally to all citizens similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Guillie v. Marine Towing


No. 95-CA-355


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-355 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/14/96); 670 So. 2d 1298; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 375



February 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA DOCKET NO. 401,608, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE DOUGLAS ALLEN, JUDGE, AD HOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Jones Act matter, defendant marine towing corporation challenged a decision of the 24th Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which found it and other defendants negligent and awarded damages to plaintiff deck hand.


OVERVIEW: The parties did not contest the district court's finding that the deck hand was a seaman as contemplated by the Jones Act, 46 U.S.C.S. § 688. At the time of his accident, he was believed to have been employed by marine towing corporation. In actuality, the corporation did not own any assets, but was only a common paymaster. The actual employer was determined. The president of the towing corporation was either the president or vice-president in charge of operations of the actual employer. Thus, although the district court found negligence in failing to maintain a reasonably safe work environment, it was argued that the president, in his personal capacity, should not have been held responsible for liability under the Jones Act, as he was not personally the employer. The court concluded that both the presumed and actual employers had enough connexity with the employment to be considered the deck hand's Jones Act employer. However, the court could not hold the president personally responsible for liability imposed on his corporations. In order to impose such liability, the court had to pierce the corporate veil, and no evidence supported such an action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded in part. The matter was remanded to the district court for an assignment of the percentage of fault. Each party to the appeal was to bear its own costs of the appeal.

Begnaud v. DOT & Dev.


95-CA-714, 95-CA-715


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-714 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/14/96); 679 So. 2d 113; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 373



February 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1996. Rehearing Refused April 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 31,104 C/W 31,332. HONORABLE MARY ANN VIAL LEMMON, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Transportation and Development sought review of the judgment of the 29th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which held in favor of plaintiff passenger. The department challenged the trial court's awards for medical expenses, lost earnings, and general damages under La. Const. art. 12, § 10(c).


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the passenger asserted survivorship and wrongful death claims arising from a one-vehicle car accident in which the passenger was a guest passenger. The passenger's children were substituted as plaintiffs upon the passenger's death. The trial court rendered judgment in solido against the department and another. On review, the court affirmed. The trial court found no error in the determination of the passenger's lost wages. The court found no merit in the department's argument that even if it were proven that the passenger contracted hepatitis from blood transfusions, the state had no duty to protect him from such an occurrence. The court held under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106B(1), (2) (1995) and La. Const. art. 12, § 10(c) (as amended 1995) that the legislature intended to make the triggering date for the cap on damages against the department to have been the date of judicial demand. The court found that there was no cap in the present case on that date. The court concluded that the 500,000 dollar cap did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and held against the department.

 

656 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Rubicon, Inc.


No. 95 CA 0108


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0108 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/96); 670 So. 2d 475; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 449



February 14, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1996. Released for Publication April 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Department of Environmental Quality, No. 009 213 191, Vivian B. Guillory, Administrative Hearing Officer



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public interest groups disputed a decision of appellee Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) granting a company an exemption from La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2193, which prohibited the deep well injection of hazardous waste. The court considered whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2024(C), as amended by 1995 La. Acts 1208, was constitutional, the effect on the court's jurisdiction if not, and the adequacy of DEQ's decision.


OVERVIEW: Under 1995 La. Acts 1208 (Act), which was enacted after the filing of the appeal, the court no longer had jurisdiction to review the DEQ decision. The public interest groups argued that the Act violated La. Const. art. III, § 15(A). On appeal, the court held that, because the issue had not existed before the appeal was filed, the groups could raise it for the first time on appeal. The court held that the Act did violate art. III, § 15(A), because it had two objects, the providing of witness fees in state agency proceedings and the jurisdiction to review agency decisions. Because the Act was void ab initio, the court had jurisdiction over the appeal pursuant to 1995 La. Acts 947, § 1. Although it was not raised as an assignment of error, under La. Const. art. IX, § 1 the court had the duty to consider the adequacy of the DEQ decision. The court held that DEQ's letter notifying the company that the exemption had been granted under certain conditions with the attached conditions and response to public comments fell far short of satisfying the jurisprudential requirements for decision-rendering by the DEQ. The court instructed the DEQ as to what was required and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and set aside the approval of the company's petition for an exemption and remanded for the issuance of findings to support the approval.

State v. Guy


No. 95-KA-0899


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0899 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/31/96); 669 So. 2d 517; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 122



January 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 370-258, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting defendant of murder and imposing a life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree murder. Defendant challenged his conviction asserting that he lacked the required intent and that the eyewitness was not credible. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. First the court held that specific intent was defined as that state of mind which existed when the circumstances indicated that the offender actively desired the prescribed criminal consequences to follow his act or failure to act. The court determined that the fact that the victim was killed by only a single bullet when three shots were fired did not negate the fact that defendant intentionally aimed and fired three shots in close succession directly at the victim. Under these circumstances, the evidence of specific intent was sufficient to convict defendant of second degree murder. The court held that defendant did not commit manslaughter because there was no evidence of passion immediately caused by provocation sufficient to deprive defendant of self-control. Second, the court held that the jury was informed of the eyewitness's criminal record and the fact that he was paid and it was up to the jury to resolve credibility issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

658 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dillon


No. 95-00884


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-00884 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/96); 670 So. 2d 278; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 220



January 31, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, Hon. Arthur Planchard, Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 8469-94.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an adverse ruling on defendant's motions to quash indictment and suppress evidence, she plead guilty in the Fourteenth Judicial District Court Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) to possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and possession of cocaine over 400 grams. In pleading, defendant reserved her right to seek appellate review of the rulings. She was concurrently sentenced to 5 years on the first charge and 15 years on the second.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the adverse ruling on her motions to quash indictment and suppress evidence. She claimed La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:361.1 was unconstitutional, and thus, the stop, search, and arrest based on the statute were illegal. In virtually every case in which a police officer testifies, an impression garnered from the senses was sought. The officer testified that even though he thought the window tinting was too dark, the degree of tinting was determined with a light transmission meter before a violation was found and a ticket issued. The statute had not violated defendant's right to privacy, her constitutional challenge failed. The interest in public safety was weighed against the intrusion into the driver's personal liberty occasioned by requiring her to have maintained windows with significant visibility; the intrusion was minimal. The search fell within the automobile exception to the search warrant requirement. Probable cause existed based on the totality of the evidence: the conflicting stories, the nervousness of the driver and passenger, the record of narcotics violations, and the indication by the dog. Exigent circumstances arose, as the automobile was mobile.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was amended to give defendant credit for time served, and was affirmed as amended. The case was remanded to the district court for amendment of the commitment and minute entry of the sentence to reflect the credit for time served. The costs of the appeal were assessed against defendant.

State v. Lopez


No. 95-00873


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-00873 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/31/96); 670 So. 2d 283; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 221



January 31, 1996, Decided

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 15th Judicial District Court, Parish of Vermillion (Louisiana), which convicted him of simple escape and sentenced him to five years imprisonment at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Cuban national, had been previously convicted of attempted first degree murder and ordered deported by an immigration judge. While serving as a garden trustee at a federal immigration correction center, defendant escaped. He was caught and convicted of simple escape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:110(A)(1), and he was sentenced to five years incarceration at hard labor. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the state court had jurisdiction under La. Const. art. V, § 16 to try and convict defendant of escape from a federal detention facility. The court also held that the sentence of five years was not excessive because defendant was a second felony offender and the first offense was a serious offense. The court also found that defendant showed no remorse, refused to cooperate during his pre-sentence interview, and had no regard for the authority of the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of simple escape and sentenced him to five years imprisonment at hard labor.

State v. BP Exploration & Oil


No. 95-CA-2031


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2031 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/31/96); 667 So. 2d 1219; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 110



January 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NO. 39-107, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE WILLIAM A. ROE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed an order from the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish (Louisiana), granting a portion of defendant oil company's exception of prescription. The oil company also appealed the judgment awarding attorney fees and the award of use and sales taxes for certain tax years.


OVERVIEW: The State initiated proceedings seeking to collect use and sales taxes allegedly owed on two by-products of the refining process, namely, refinery gas and coke-on catalyst. The oil company filed an exception of prescription, alleging that the State could not collect taxes for certain tax years. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment that granted a portion of the exception. The court noted that La. Const. art. 7, § 16 provided that all claims for taxes prescribed within three years after the 31st day of December in the year in which the taxes became due. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1580 provided the circumstances under which prescription was suspended. The court concluded that the trial court's judgment was not erroneous because the trial court was in the best position to judge the parties and determine whether the oil company waived the prescription period. Likewise, the court held that there was no error in finding that prescription had not attached to the taxes owed for certain tax years. Last, the court held that the award of attorney fees was proper because the trial court was in the better position to judge the amount of services performed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

661 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


BP Oil Co. v. Plaquemines Parish Comm'n Council


No. 95-CA-1188


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1188 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/31/96); 669 So. 2d 536; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 99



January 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NOS. 34-001 C/W 34-353 C/W 34-354 C/W 34-805, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Plaquemines Parish Government challenged a judgment from the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish, Division "A" (Louisiana), which on remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305(D)(1)(h) (1985) to determine the amount of the refund due to appellee taxpayer for a sales and use tax overpayment on refinery gas.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer operated a petroleum refinery. The Parish assessed unpaid sales and use taxes against the taxpayer for refinery gas and coke-on-catalyst for the period between January of 1985 and October of 1990. The taxpayer paid the taxes under protest and filed four separate actions to recover refunds. The trial court consolidated the actions and held hearings on cross-motions for summary judgment. The trial court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305(D)(1)(h) unconstitutional and rejected the taxpayer's demands for refunds except for the exemption of refinery gas used for purposes other than as boiler fuel. On appeal, the supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the action for a determination of the value of the taxable refinery gas in accordance with § 47:305(D)(1)(h), and other proceedings. On remand, the trial court recalculated the refund of the tax and penalty paid by the taxpayer as to the refinery gas. On appeal, the court affirmed the amount calculated for the refund. Knowing that some of the taxing period pre-dated the effective date of the Act, the supreme court nonetheless ordered the trial court to use the formula in the post-amendment statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the calculation of the refund due to the taxpayer for the sales and use tax overpayment.

 

662 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Mumphrey


No. 95-CA-643


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-643 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/30/96); 668 So. 2d 1274; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 206



January 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 472-477, DIVISION "E". THE HONORABLE CHARLES E. MCMANUS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother on behalf of her minor children, appealed a decision from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) which granted defendants' exception of no cause of action based on La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.6. Defendants were a motorist, his employer, and the employer's insurer. The court dismissed the action for bystander mental anguish.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a decision granting a motorist's exception of no cause of action based on La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.6, the court affirmed, dismissing an action brought by a mother of minor children. The decedent was hit by a van and killed as he was attempting to cross a highway. The minor children were first cousins of the decedent and witnessed the accident. The mother brought an action for the mental anguish and emotional distress her minor children suffered from witnessing the death of the decedent. The court held that Louisiana law, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.6, recognized a cause of action based upon the so-called "bystander recovery rule." However, the court held that the legislature chose to limit the permissible claimants for bystander mental anguish damages to close relatives of the victim, and not first cousins. Further, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.6 did not violate the mother's right to equal protection of the laws and was constitutional. Thus, the mother had no right of action for mental anguish based on the death of decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which granted the motorist's exception of no cause of action and held that a mother of minor children did not have a cause of action for bystander mental anguish based on the witnessing of the death of the children's first cousin in a vehicular accident.

 

663 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Gilbert


No. 95-CA-426


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-426 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/30/96); 668 So. 2d 1212; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 213



January 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 1996. Rehearing Refused March 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 424-407, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN P. ZENO, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the surviving second wife of a testator, and appellees, the testator's two daughters from his prior marriage, sought review of the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), distributing the testator's estate between the wife and daughters.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that a donation made to the wife, through the testator's execution of a power of attorney, was a valid inter vivos donation; that inter vivos donations by the testator should not be added to the estate mass in determining the amount of the forced portion; and that the usufruct in favor of the wife over the daughters' forced portion was an impermissible impingement on their legitime and was thus invalid. All parties appealed. The court held that there was no manifest error in the trial court's factual finding that the testator made a valid inter vivos donation of funds to the wife. The court held that the trial court erred in excluding inter vivos donations to the wife from the calculation of the active mass of the estate in arriving at the disposable portion of the legitime m, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1505, but that it did not err in excluding the inter vivos donations to the daughters, which were exempt under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1502. It further held, overruling Succession of Suggs, 612 So. 2d 297 (La. Ct. App. 1992), that under La. Civ. Code Ann. 890, the wife's usufruct was not an impingement on the legitime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding valid donations and allowing succession expenses to the wife, but reversed the judgment insofar as it failed to include donations to the wife in computing the succession mass and the forced portion, and insofar as it found that the usufruct granted in favor of the wife impinged on the daughters' legitime.

 

664 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Nosser v. Health Care Trust Fund Bd.


No. 27,619-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,619-CA (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/24/96); 666 So. 2d 1272; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 26



January 24, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 396,117. Honorable Gorman E Taylor, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a health care board sought review of a decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which granted a summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a doctor and a chiropractic association, in a action that sought a declaratory judgment that a certain limitation in a health care plan violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:688 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.65.


OVERVIEW: The doctor and the chiropractic association filed an action against the health care board that sought a declaratory judgment that the limitation in the health care plan provided to participating employees of the city violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:688 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.65. The city health care plan limited to $ 500.00 the maximum annual benefit payable for spinal manipulative therapy and any physical therapy type modalities rendered in connection therewith by osteopathic physician, chiropractor or medical doctor. The doctor and the chiropractic association asserted that the city's plan discouraged participants from selecting chiropractic treatment methods, and discriminated against practitioners of the chiropractic profession. The doctor and the chiropractic filed a summary judgment, which was granted. On appeal the court affirmed. The court held that the limiting language in the plan was discriminatory against the method of practice employed by chiropractor. The court determined that although spinal manipulative therapy was not necessarily a method exclusively employed by chiropractors, it was critical to the practice of chiropractic.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision, which granted a summary judgment in favor of a doctor and a chiropractic association in an action that sought a declaratory judgment that a certain limitation in a health care plan violated statutory law.

 

665 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 94-KA-2584


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-2584 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/19/96); 668 So. 2d 420; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 93



January 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 352-264, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED; AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which convicted him of two counts of armed robbery, three counts of attempted second degree murder, and sentenced him to serve three concurrent 50 year sentences on the attempted murder counts, to run consecutively with two concurrent 99 years sentences on the armed robbery counts, without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted based upon evidence that he shot his victims during an armed robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant waived the prosecutor's failure to sign a page of the indictment because he did not object to the defect prior to trial. The court amended the sentence for attempted murder to delete the restrictions against probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The court found that the identifications were not suggestive. The fact that one victim was unable to make an identification while she was heavily sedated did not detract from her subsequent positive identification. The court found that the identifications were reliable because each of the victims had a good opportunity to observe defendant. The court noted that the descriptions they gave immediately after the incident were accurate and that all of them expressed certainty as to the identifications. Moreover, the time between the offense and the line-ups ranged from 10 to 23 days. The court ruled that the consecutive sentences were not excessive given the fact that the defendant "cold-bloodedly and deliberately" tried to execute the victims even though they did not resist the robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and amended the sentence to delete the requirement that the sentences for attempted second degree murder be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The court affirmed the sentence, as amended.

 

666 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kingston


No. 95-K-1935


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1935 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/19/96); 668 So. 2d 395; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 118



January 19, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 6, 1996.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana sought to invoke supervisory jurisdiction to reverse a trial court ruling (Louisiana), which had sentenced defendant to six years at hard labor, two years less than the eight-year minimum sentence required by the Habitual Offender Law and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62. Defendant had withdrawn his plea of not guilty and pleaded guilty to the charge of simple burglary of an automobile in violation La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.


OVERVIEW: After defendant changed his plea to guilty as charged by the bill of information with simple burglary of an automobile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62, the State filed a multiple bill charging that defendant was a third felony offender. The trial court sentenced defendant to less than the minimum sentence required by the Habitual Offender Law and § 14:62, and the State sought to invoke supervisory jurisdiction to reverse the ruling. The court vacated the sentence and remanded the case for resentencing, holding that the trial court failed to sufficiently find that the statutorily mandated minimum sentence would have been unconstitutional as applied to defendant. The trial court merely noted that it had considered defendant's age and that it felt that any higher amount of time than six years would have been unjust. The court held that such statements did not indicate that the trial court made a search and inquiry necessary to justify declaring a legislatively mandated sentence unconstitutional nor did they indicate that the trial court made a meaningful assessment of any mitigating or aggravating circumstances appropriate to the case.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence imposed by the trial court and remanded the case for resentencing.

State v. Davis


NUMBER 94 KA 2332


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2332 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/15/95); 666 So. 2d 400; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3542



December 15, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF TERREBONNE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 244921. HONORABLE JOHN T. PETTIGREW, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana) to two counts of aggravated rape, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14: 42(A)(2), (3), and (5), reserving his right to appeal the trial court's denial of a motion to suppress. He argued that he did not consent to the taking of blood samples, a statement he gave after his arrest was inadmissible, his sentence was excessive, and there was patent error.


OVERVIEW: While officers were investigating the unsolved crimes, defendant stopped, identified himself as a police informant, and offered to help. After rejecting his offer, they realized that he fit the description of the person they were seeking. They invited him to come to the station and he drove there several times to discuss the case. Blood samples implicated defendant and he made a videotaped statement admitting the crimes. On appeal, the court held that the denial of the motion to suppress indicated that the trial court accepted the officers' version of the events and rejected defendant's. The evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant freely and voluntarily consented to the blood test at a time when he was not being detained. The court held that, before giving the statement, defendant waived the presence of counsel. Because he consented to the blood tests, the statement was not fruit of the poisonous tree. Given the circumstances of the crimes, imposition of life sentences for the aggravated rapes was not excessive and did not violate La. Const. art. 1, § 20. The trial court's patent error in failing to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 642 was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for aggravated rape and the mandatory sentences of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.

 

668 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Dawson v. City of Bogalusa


NUMBER 95 CA 0824


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0824 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/15/95); 669 So. 2d 451; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3560



December 15, 1995, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for Washington Parish, Louisiana Trial Court No. 70430. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner challenged a judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for Washington Parish, Louisiana, which dismissed her suit that alleged she was injured by an unreasonably dangerous pothole in a city-owned right-of-way, and found that she failed to show that defendant city had actual or constructive notice of the pothole as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.


OVERVIEW: As the homeowner was exiting her car, she stepped into a pothole, injuring her right knee and ankle; she was very depressed and had crying spells. The city admitted it was aware for five and one-half months before the accident that there was some sort of problem. On appeal, the court held that, based on the length of time the pothole existed and the city's knowledge of the problem, the trial court was clearly wrong in finding that the homeowner failed to show that the city had constructive notice. The trial court was also legally wrong in dismissing the suit for failure to prove notice. Failure to prove notice was not a sound legal basis for dismissal of a claim against a governmental entity. The court, therefore, conducted its own de novo review. Had the city investigated the homeowner's complaint, it would have known of the problem. She, however, was acutely aware of the pothole at the end of her driveway, and she admitted she could easily have avoided the accident had she looked before she stepped. Thus, she was clearly in a superior position to avoid the accident. The court, therefore, assigned fault 75 percent to the homeowner and 25 percent to the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the homeowner's suit. The court rendered judgment in the homeowner's favor and against the city for general and special damages, reduced by 75 percent.

Ayers v. Brazell


No. 27,756-CA, No. 27,757-CA (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,756 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/06/95); 665 So. 2d 694; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3245



December 6, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 84,421 & 84,539. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed from an order of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana), which found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1, absolving public entities from liability for discretionary acts or omissions related to the legitimate objective of their office, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners sued defendant parish, alleging that the parish willfully and recklessly issued building permits without the required information and that, as a result, their homes were flooded. The trial court entered judgment for the parish. The court remanded the matter to allow the trial court to rule on the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1, which absolved public entities from liability for discretionary acts or omissions related to the legitimate objectives of their office. The trial court found the statute constitutional and the court affirmed. A newly enacted amendment, La. Const. art. XII, § 10C, expressly permitted the legislature to limit the liability of state and public entities and permitted the legislature to define the circumstances giving rise to liability. The amendment was curative and entitled to retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that held that the statute was constitutional.

State v. Thomas


No. 27,507-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,507 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/06/95); 665 So. 2d 629; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3260



December 6, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 163635. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which convicted him of second-degree murder and attempted second-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:30.1 and 14.27.


OVERVIEW: An acquaintance drove defendant and his two companions home from the apartment where the girlfriends of the acquaintance and one of the companions lived. After getting out of the car, defendant fired multiple shots at the acquaintance's head, killing the acquaintance and wounding one of his companions. As a result, defendant was convicted of second-degree murder and attempted second-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:30.1 and 14:27. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 801, defendant's failure to object to the omission of jury instructions on self-defense or justification precluded review. Louisiana did not recognize a plain error rule except where the errors substantially affected the fairness of the proceedings and the reliability of the fact-finding process, which was not present in defendant's trial. Because the evidence against self-defense was overwhelming, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 802(1) did not require the trial court to instruct the jury on self-defense or justification. Therefore, the judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of second-degree murder and attempted second-degree murder.

State v. Finley


No. CR95-553


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-553 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/06/95); 664 So. 2d 775; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3425



December 6, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 4, 1996.
Writ denied by State v. Finley, 670 So. 2d 1237, 1996 La. LEXIS 991 (La., Mar. 29, 1996)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Finley v. State, 748 So. 2d 437, 1999 La. LEXIS 2405 (La., Oct. 1, 1999)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Finley v. State, 812 So. 2d 650, 2002 La. LEXIS 1030 (La., Mar. 28, 2002)
Motion denied by State v. Finley, 2017 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 20 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. WILLIAM P. POLK, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number 215,744.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of first-degree robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1, classified defendant as a habitual offender in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and sentenced to 50 years hard labor without parole or probation.


OVERVIEW: After robbing a bank, defendant was given a ride home by a store employee, who later led police to defendant's residence. Police entered the residence without a warrant after noticing defendant in the house. The court affirmed, but remanded in order for the trial court to give defendant credit for time served in accordance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 880. The trial court committed harmless error in failing to specify whether defendant was a second or third offender because the maximum sentence was 80 years for both second and third felony offenders. The police were justified in entering defendant's residence without a warrant because, after seeing defendant enter the bathroom, there was reason to believe he might try to destroy evidence. The trial court did not err in considering defendant's 1967 burglary conviction in his habitual offender hearing because although defendant was discharged from that conviction more than five years before the present offense, his commission of a second felony was within five years of his discharge on the first felony and commission of the instant felony was within five years of discharge on the second felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree robbery, his classification as a habitual offender and his sentence.

 

672 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of New Orleans v. Benson


No. 95-CA-1505


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1505 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/30/95); 665 So. 2d 1196; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3231



November 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 95-1227, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the owners and the manager of a gay bathhouse, challenged a judgment from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division "A" (Louisiana), which denied their motion to dissolve a preliminary injunction or, alternatively, to require that plaintiff City of New Orleans post security for an injunction it obtained preventing defendants from operating the top three floors of the spa until it complied with city fire and building codes.


OVERVIEW: A City fire inspector cited the manager of the bathhouse with 20 separate violations of the city fire code and building code. The City obtained a preliminary injunction enjoining the operation of the top three floors of the spa. Defendants filed a motion to dissolve the preliminary injunction or, in the alternative, to require the City to furnish security. The trial court denied relief. On appeal, the court affirmed. The City was not seeking to punish defendants by enjoining them from endangering the public as long as they failed to correct the deficiencies constituting the fire safety code violations. It was simply fulfilling its duty to protect the public from fire hazards. The injunctive relief it sought was not punishment for defendants' alleged violation of the municipal ordinances and could not constitute cruel, excessive, or unusual punishment. The fact that the manager was charged individually with violating a municipal ordinance did not subject defendants to double jeopardy. La. Const. art. XII, § 10 encompassed the power to dispense with the need for the City to furnish security for the injunctive relief it sought, which was in the nature of a "procedural" matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendants' motion to dissolve the preliminary injunction enjoining the operation of the top three floors of the spa. The court also affirmed that the City was not required to post security for the injunction.

Avenal v. Department of Natural Resources


No. 95-CA-0836 C/W No. 95-C-2421


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0836 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/05/95); 668 So. 2d 1150; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3221



November 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 19, 1995, Reported at: La. App. LEXIS 3446. Released for Publication December 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NO.38-266, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE WILLIAM A. ROE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; WRITS DENIED; STAY ORDER VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee fishermen filed an action against appellant State of Louisiana seeking damages resulting from a freshwater diversion project. The state, through the Department of Natural Resources (the DNR), appealed from a judgment of the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish (Louisiana), denying its exception of improper venue. the DNR sought supervisory writs from the denial of its dilatory exception of nonjoinder of a necessary party.


OVERVIEW: The fishermen asserted that their leases in the St. Bernard and Plaquemines parishes were damaged because of the intrusion of freshwater by way of the state's freshwater diversion project. the DNR contended that the case should be transferred to the East Baton Rouge Parish, where the decision was made to adopt the project. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that the DNR's venue exception was properly denied under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5104(A). The fishermen were not seeking damages because of the DNR's decisions or any state policy to restore wetlands, but rather, they alleged that the project resulted in a taking of their property for which they were entitled to be compensated. The court further held that the trial court properly denied the exception of nonjoinder based on the fishermen's failure to join the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries as a defendant. Although the source of the fishermen's property rights was the leases they obtained from the Department of Wildlife and Fisheries, there was no need to add the department as a defendant. Finally, the court declined to interfere with the trial court's denial of the DNR's motion to compel discovery.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writs filed by the state and affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court also vacated its previous stay order that had been issued in response to the trial court's denial of the DNR's motion to compel discovery in the case.
