State v. Alberto


No. 95-KA-540


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-540 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/28/95); 665 So. 2d 614; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3383



November 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 87-2026, DIVISION "N/H". HONORABLE JAMES L. CANNELLA AND HUBERT A. VONDENSTEIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of forcible rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.1 and aggravated burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60 and sentenced him to serve 20 years at hard labor for the rape conviction and to serve a consecutive term of 15 years at hard labor for the burglary conviction.


OVERVIEW: A victim of a burglary and rape identified defendant in a photographic lineup as the perpetrator of the offenses. Fingerprint and hair samples taken from the victim's home matched those of defendant. On appeal from his convictions and sentences, defense counsel requested only an error patent review. The court affirmed. The trial court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief and the court affirmed; however, the state supreme court ordered an out-of-time appeal. The court, after reviewing defendant's allegations of error, once again affirmed. The fact that the record did not contain a ruling on defendant's motion to suppress the victim's identification prior to trial did not constitute reversible error because the victim made an independent in-court identification of defendant. Defendant's consecutive sentences were not excessive under U.S. Const. amend. VIII or La. Const. of 1974, art. I, § 20. La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 883 allowed the trial court to impose consecutive sentences for offenses arising out of the same scheme or plan; furthermore, the trial court set forth aggravating factors. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

675 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clements


No. 94-KA-2217


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-2217 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/16/95); 665 So. 2d 137; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3120



November 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 355-756, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section J (Louisiana), which resentenced him to 21 years at hard labor after a manslaughter conviction. The issue was whether, after the court vacated an original sentence of 21 years at hard labor, the trial court had, as noted in the remand, properly considered the sentencing guidelines in re-imposing a sentence greater than the range designated by the guidelines.


OVERVIEW: At the second sentencing hearing, the trial court stated that it had considered the sentencing guidelines and the trial court enunciated as reasons for deviating from the guidelines that the victim had taken defendant into his home from off the street and defendant thereafter killed the victim who had helped him. Defendant argued that the 21-year sentence was excessive given that it was three times the term recommended by the sentencing guidelines. On appeal, the court noted that the presentence investigation was not in the record, so the court had to consider the sentence without regard to defendant's juvenile record although the State alluded to prior juvenile offenses. Therefore, without referring to the juvenile record, the court held that, considering the circumstances of the offense and the reasons for sentencing given by the trial court, the trial court adequately provided reasons for the sentence and did not manifestly abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to the maximum sentence of 21 years at hard labor. The sentence was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment resentencing defendant to 21 years at hard labor after his conviction for manslaughter.

 

676 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Rey v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 95-CA-0661 Consolidated/With No. 95-CA-0662


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0661 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/16/95); 665 So. 2d 109; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3126



November 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 93-12660 C/W NO. 94-7720, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE LOUIS A. DiROSA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed an order of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division D (Louisiana), which dismissed the patient's case against defendant, state patient's compensation fund, which sought payment of additional amounts in the patient's medical malpractice action against the doctor who implanted lenses in the patient's eyes. The patient contended that the fund did not have standing to raise prescription as a defense.


OVERVIEW: The patient was diagnosed with bilateral cataracts, and the doctor placed lens implants in both eyes. The patient continued to have problems and one implant was removed. The patient discovered that the lenses were "investigational devices" and filed a medical malpractice suit against the doctor for his failure to inform him. The doctor and his insurer agreed to pay the patient the statutory maximum of $ 100,000. The patient filed for approval of the settlement and made a demand for payment of additional amounts from the state patient's compensation fund. The fund opposed the settlement on several ground, including prescription. The trial court sustained the fund's exception of prescription and dismissed the case against the fund. The patient appealed and contended that the fund did not have standing to raise prescription, since under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.44(C)(5), once the insurer had paid its policy limits, statutory liability was admitted and the fund had no standing to raise the issue of prescription. The court agreed and reversed. The court held that under the statute, the fund was precluded from raising prescription.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the trial court which dismissed the patient's suit, based on prescription, against the state patient's compensation fund, which sought payment of additional amounts in the patient's medical malpractice action against a doctor who placed lens implants in the patient's eyes.

State v. Brown


95-KA-377


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-377 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/15/95); 665 So. 2d 477; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3273



November 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 94-5704. HONORABLE JACOB L. KARNO, JUDGE, PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; MULTIPLE BILL SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR REHEARING ON MULTIPLE BILL


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which sentenced defendant as a multiple offender after defendant pleaded guilty to simple burglary and purse snatching.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's adjudication of defendant as a multiple offender was based solely on defendant's admission to a prior felony conviction. Because defendant agreed to his sentence as part of a plea agreement, the court rejected defendant's contention that the sentence violated his constitutional right against excessive punishment. The court vacated defendant's adjudication and sentence as a multiple offender because there was nothing in the multiple bill transcript to indicate that the trial court complied with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D), which provided that a defendant's admission to a prior felony could not be accepted unless the defendant was first advised of his rights to have a formal hearing and to remain silent. The court ruled that the error was not harmless because the state presented no other evidence of defendant's criminal record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, vacated defendant's adjudication and sentence as a multiple offender, and remanded the matter for a multiple offender hearing and resentencing.

 

678 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Livings


NUMBER CR95-251


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-251 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/15/95); 664 So. 2d 729; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3492



November 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; Honorable Allen M. Babineaux, presiding. Lower Court Number 67330.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which convicted him for possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 40:926(C) and possession of drug paraphernalia in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 40:1033.


OVERVIEW: Acting upon information that he received over his radio, a sheriff's deputy drove to where defendant and another man were standing and approached them. The deputy conducted a pat-down search of defendant after defendant started acting fidgety and found a crack pipe. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of cocaine and possession of drug paraphernalia. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress. The search that revealed the crack pipe was not an unreasonable warrantless search because the deputy was justified in frisking defendant. Based on an informant's tip the deputy knew defendant was in possession of drugs, as defendant was located in a high drug traffic area and defendant acted nervously when the deputy approached him. The seizure was proper under the "plain feel" exception, as the deputy had knowledge of the object as a crack pipe based upon his past experience. In addition, defendant was not constitutionally deprived of his right to due process by the inclusion in the bill of information of facts concerning his prior convictions because the trial judge gave limiting instructions as required by prior caselaw.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of cocaine and possession of drug paraphernalia.

 

679 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Exxon Corp.


No. 95 CA 0392


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0392 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/09/95); 664 So. 2d 1273; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3185



November 9, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 105991. Honorable Timothy C. Ellender, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Louisiana Department of Wildlife, sought review of the judgment of the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana, in favor of plaintiff, a commercial fisherman who was injured when his boat struck a submerged bulkhead.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court's decision to credit the fisherman's version of the events was not manifestly erroneous, and left undisturbed its finding that the alleged boating incident did indeed occur, causing the fisherman to experience back pain. The court also held that the trial court did not err in ruling that the Department as surface owner had a duty to warn boaters of the presence of the submerged bulkhead. It further held that where the Department knew of the exact location of the obstacle and that boaters were striking it, and made a conscious and knowing determination to do nothing about the situation, its conduct amounted to a conscious indifference to the danger and that its failure to warn was willful, and it was thus not entitled to the recreational use immunity provided for in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795. The court also held that there was no manifest error in the trial court's determination that the fisherman was not contributorily negligent. On the issue of damages, the court found that the trial court's conclusion that the accident aggravated the fisherman's pre-existing back condition was not clearly wrong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the fisherman.

 

680 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


94 KA 2145


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2145 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/09/95); 665 So. 2d 38; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3191



November 9, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of Washington, Louisiana. Docket No. 93-CR6-56116, Division "C". Honorable Brady M. Fitzsimmons, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Washington (Louisiana), which sentenced him to serve 16 years at hard labor for selling $ 20 worth of cocaine to undercover officers in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A).


OVERVIEW: In addition to selling the cocaine to the officer, defendant was arrested with a few other rocks of cocaine in his possession. In affirming the judgment, the court held that because the trial court had considered the Sentencing Guidelines, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, the trial court had been free to throw the Sentencing Guidelines out the window and impose any sentence within statutory limits, so long as the choice of sentence was backed up by good reasons. The court held that the Sentencing Guidelines did not constrain the trial court's discretion in sentencing. Turning to the merits of the sentence, the court held that the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. The court noted that it was only slightly more than the statutory maximum for the offense, and that defendant appeared to be an incorrigible criminal based on a prior marijuana offense and a pending prosecution for another drug offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sentenced defendant to 16 years at hard labor for selling cocaine, and remanded with instructions for the trial court to admonish defendant about his rights to post-conviction relief.

State Through Louisiana State Bd. of Examiners of Psychologists of the Dep't of Health & Human Servs. v. Atterberry


No. 95 CA 0391


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0391 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/09/95); 664 So. 2d 1216; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3203



November 9, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, State of Louisiana, Trial Court No. 110,254. Honorable Paul R. Wimbish, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a counselor, sought review of a decision from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff, the State Board of Examiners of the Department of Health and Human Services (board)'s petition for a preliminary injunction enjoining the counselor from administering and using independent psychological testing activities.


OVERVIEW: The board filed a petition for injunctive relief, seeking to enjoin the counselor from using various diagnostic tests. The board alleged that the administration of the tests constituted a prohibited, unlicensed practice of psychology under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:2352(2). The trial court issued a preliminary injunction enjoining the counselor from administering or using certain tests. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the board made a prima facie showing that the counselor was acting indirect violation of the laws prohibiting the unauthorized practice of psychology. The court concluded that the trial court properly granted the preliminary injunction. The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the board was entitled to a permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a preliminary injunction to the board, enjoining the counselor from the administration and use of certain tests. The case was remanded for further proceedings on the issue of whether the board was entitled to a permanent injunction.

 

682 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wright


NUMBER CR95-377


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-377 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/08/95); 664 So. 2d 712; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3059



November 8, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; Honorable F. Rae Swent, presiding. Lower Court Number 236,541.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed a judgment from the Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which suspended defendant's sentence to five years at hard labor for distribution of a controlled substance in a school zone under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:966(A), 40:981:3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty of distribution of a controlled substance in a school zone, which is a violation of §§ 40:966(A), 40:981.3. He was sentenced to five years at hard labor to run concurrent. The trial court suspended the sentence on the condition that defendant serve five years on probation and one year in the parish jail, subject to work release. The State appealed the sentence. The court vacated the sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing. The court held that § 40:981.3 imposed a mandatory minimum sentence for a substantive criminal statute, and not an enhanced sentence like that imposed for the habitual offender statute. The trial court did not have the discretion to impose a sentence under § 40:966, and should have imposed a sentence within the range provided under § 40:981.3. The court concluded that defendant's sentence imposed was illegally lenient because the trial court did not impose the mandatory fine, and it imposed a sentence less than the mandatory minimum provided under § 40:981.3.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence for distribution of a controlled substance in a school zone. The matter was remanded for resentencing and to give defendant an opportunity to withdraw his guilty plea.

 

683 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Liberto v. Rapides Parish Police Jury


No. 95-456


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-456 (La. App. 3 Cir. 11/02/95); 667 So. 2d 552; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2930



November 2, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, Honorable William Polk, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number 178,599.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff club owner sought review of a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which dismissed his action for a judicial declaration that defendant police jury's ordinance restricting the hours that alcoholic beverages could be consumed was unconstitutional. The trial court also rejected the club owner's demand for a preliminary and permanent injunction to prevent enforcement of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The club owner challenged the trial court's dismissal of its action for a judicial declaration that the police jury's ordinance that restricted the hours that alcoholic beverages could be consumed was unconstitutional, and his request that it issue a preliminary and permanent injunction to prevent enforcement of the ordinance. The court affirmed and found that La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3601 authorized the issuance of an injunction in cases where irreparable injury, loss, or damage would result to the club owner from the enforcement of the ordinance. The court noted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 authorized alcoholic regulatory ordinances for the purpose of protection of public health, morals, and safety. The court held that the club owner failed to show that he was irreparably harmed because the ordinance did not close his club but only restricted the consumption of alcohol between certain hours. The court found that the ordinance was constitutional because it was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest of prevention of criminal drug activity and drunken driving, and it did not impermissibly interfere with the club owner's business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the club owner's action.

 

684 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Sevin v. McDermott, Inc.


No. 95-CA-215


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-215 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/31/95); 663 So. 2d 857; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 3106



October 31, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. DISTRICT 07, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 94-641. HONORABLE G. WALTON CAIRE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment from the Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC) (Louisiana), dismissing the claim of plaintiff employee based on the finding that the OWC lacked jurisdiction over the matter.


OVERVIEW: While in the course and scope of his employment, the employee was involved in an automobile accident wherein he injured his lower back, necessitating a two level laminectomy. He did not return to work after the accident. The employee received weekly compensation benefits from his employer for more than 11 years. When the employer terminated the payments, the employee filed suit in district court for wrongful termination of benefits. The employee also filed a claim for wrongful termination of benefits in the OWC. The OWC hearing officer held that the OWC did not have jurisdiction over the matter, but rather, jurisdiction rested in state court. In response to the employer's appeal, the court affirmed because it found that claims arising prior to July, 1983 were under the jurisdiction of the state district courts. According to the court, the employee's claim arose at the time of his accident in 1981, not at the time payments were stopped. Therefore, the state courts had jurisdiction over the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that the employee's worker's compensation claim was under the jurisdiction of the state courts and not the Office of Workers' Compensation.

 

685 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Young


No. 94-KA-1636


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1636 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/26/95); 663 So. 2d 525; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2708



October 26, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 363-355, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced defendant to 30 years, as opposed to a 99-year minimum for fourth offenders under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529, after defendant was convicted of armed robbery by a jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant walked into an aluminum recycling company and pulled out a gun on a man who worked at the recycling company. The man's job was to give money in the form of a check to customers who brought in scrap aluminum. Defendant coerced the man to write him two checks. Defendant cashed the two checks at a liquor store, which were returned as stolen. After another attempt to cash another stolen check, defendant was arrested. Defendant was convicted of armed robbery. The trial court sentenced defendant to 30 years, as opposed to the 99-year minimum for fourth offenders. The court modified the sentence to 99 years, holding that the evidence indicated that defendant was a threat to society and the minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law was not unconstitutional. Minimum sentencing could not be departed from based upon subjective impressions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's armed robbery conviction, but modified the 30-year sentence to 99 years.

 

686 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Tomas v. Conco Food Distribs.


NUMBER 95-348


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-348 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/25/95); 666 So. 2d 327; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2712



October 25, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted in Part and Denied in Part January 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 315. Released for Publication January 10, 1996. As Substituted November 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Office of Workers Compensation Administration District 4, State of Louisiana; Honorable Sharon E. McCauley, Hearing Officer, Presiding. Lower Court Number 93-04723.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant sought review of a decision of the Office of Workers Compensation Administration District 4 (Louisiana), which denied the claimant benefits and declined to rule on the claimant's constitutional challenge La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(e)(i) and (ii).


OVERVIEW: The claimant suffered a stroke while attending a meeting at work. The claimant filed for worker's compensation benefits. The hearing officer ruled that the claimant failed to present evidence of a recoverable work injury pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(e)(i) or (ii), because the claimant's stroke was not caused by physical stress. The claimant challenged the statute's constitutionality. The hearing officer declined to rule on the constitutionality of the statute, finding that she lacked jurisdiction to make such a determination. On appeal the court held that determining a statute's constitutionality was strictly a function of the courts because of the separation of powers doctrine. Except as otherwise provided by the Louisiana Constitution, no branch of the government, nor any person holding office in one of them, was authorized to exercise power belonging to another branch.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative hearing officer's refusal to rule on the claimant's constitutional challenge to the statute in the worker's compensation suit.

 

687 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. McGee


No. 95-K-1863


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1863 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/18/95); 663 So. 2d 495; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2614



October 18, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS. CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 375-801, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AND CASE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana applied to the court for a writ so that it could consider whether a trial judge could waive the fine mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1 for an indigent defendant arising from a matter in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section C (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of firearm or carrying concealed weapon by a person convicted of certain felonies in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. He was sentenced to three years of hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or sentence suspension. The State claimed that it was illegally lenient because it did not include a fine. The court granted the State's application for a writ to consider whether a trial judge had to impose such a fine where defendant was indigent. The court determined that the language of § 1495.1 mandated a fine, and noted the state's highest court had earlier determined that § 14:95.1 imposed a fine that the trial court had no discretion to waive. Accordingly, the court remanded the case to the trial court for imposition of a fine, reserving to defendant the opportunity to change his plea if it was predicated upon the assurance that no fine would be imposed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's application for a writ and remanded the case in order that a mandatory fine could be imposed upon a criminal defendant.

 

688 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


NUMBER 94 KA 1561


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1561 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/06/95); 664 So. 2d 141; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2745



October 6, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1995. Released for Publication January 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE TWENTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST FELICIANA. STATE OF LOUISIANA NUMBER 8-93-833. HONORABLE WILSON R. RAMSHUR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION, HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for attempted murder from the 20th Judicial District Court for East Feliciana Parish (Louisiana). The district court also held that defendant was a third felony habitual offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann § 15:529.1 and imposed a 60-year prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's attempted murder trial, he was identified by the victim based on a chance encounter at the police station after the crime and another encounter at the courthouse. On appeal, defendant contended that the identification procedures were suggestive and resulted in misidentification. Further, he argued that the district court had considered two improper felony convictions in sentencing him as a habitual offender. The court rejected both arguments, and affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held that when immediate and definite identifications result from inadvertent meetings between the victim and the suspect, and there is no indication of impropriety or suggestiveness, an out-of-court identification will be found both reliable and admissible.Rejecting a line of Louisiana cases and adopting the definition of conviction from New Jersey, the court also found that a predicate felony conviction could be used by the district court, although sentence was not imposed in the first case when a second felony was committed, to impose a third felony sentence under the Habitual Offender Law, even if the first two convictions occurred on the same day.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence as a habitual offender.

 

689 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Hammons v. ABB C-E Servs.


NUMBER 94 CA 2444


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2444 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/06/95); 671 So. 2d 370; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2753



October 6, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 1995.
Related proceeding at Hammons v. ABB C-E Servs., 2006 La. App. LEXIS 669 (La.App. 1 Cir., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration in and for the State of Louisiana. Trial Court Number 93-08874. Pamela Moses-Laramore, Administrative Hearing Officer.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In worker's compensation proceedings, defendants, an employer and its insurer, sought review of the judgment of the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration in and for the State of Louisiana, which awarded compensation, interest, and attorney's fees to plaintiff employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in the course and scope of his employment. Defendants initially paid the employee total disability benefits and supplemental earnings benefits (SEB) at the maximum rate; they then reduced and later terminated the SEB. A hearing officer awarded SEB and total disability benefits with legal interest from the date of judicial demand until paid, penalties, and attorney's fees. On appeal the court amended the judgment in part but otherwise affirmed. The finding that the employee was permanently totally disabled was not manifestly erroneous; however, the amount awarded exceeded the maximum weekly rate of compensation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1202(A)(2). Because the employee justifiably relied on the representation of an insurance adjuster that his acceptance of retirement benefits would not alter his worker's compensation benefits, defendants were estopped from using the acceptance of retirement benefits as a basis to terminate SEB under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii). The officer erred in awarding interest from the date of judicial demand; La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.3(A) allowed interest from the date of the hearing officer's order.


OUTCOME: The court amended the hearing officer's judgment by decreasing the amount of permanent total disability benefits and to award interest only from the date of the hearing officer's judgment. As amended, the court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Powell


94 KA 1390


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1390 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/06/95); 671 So. 2d 493; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2743



October 6, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 1995.
Writ denied by State v. Powell, 667 So. 2d 529, 1996 La. LEXIS 438 (La., Feb. 9, 1996)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Powell v. State, 810 So. 2d 1146, 2002 La. LEXIS 639 (La., Feb. 22, 2002)
Writ granted by State v. Powell, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2974 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 20, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Powell, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 1064 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 21, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 7-93-454), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE BONNIE P. JACKSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE OF SECOND DEGREE MURDER AFFIRMED; CONVICTION AND SENTENCE OF SECOND DEGREE FETICIDE VACATED; REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), convicting defendant of murder and feticide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for murder and feticide alleging that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict and that the convictions violated double jeopardy. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction in part and reversed the conviction in part. In affirming the conviction, the court noted that the evidence presented indicated that defendant shot his gun more than once from a slow moving car into a crowd of people. Defendant was not shooting into the air or into another direction in order to frighten the people. Although defendant claimed he did not see anyone in front of the club, there was sufficient evidence to support a finding that just prior to the shooting defendant was talking to people standing in front of the club. Next, the court held that defendant's conviction for both, murder and feticide violated double jeopardy because the evidence needed to support the murder conviction was the same for the feticide conviction. The court reversed defendant's feticide conviction and his sentence and found that resentencing was necessary because defendant received life for the murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and reversed his conviction for feticide.

 

691 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Twin Parish Port Comm'n v. Berry Bros.


No. 95-425


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-425 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/04/95); 663 So. 2d 257; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2572



October 4, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF IBERIA, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. CARL J. WILLIAMS, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number 80299.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff, the Twin Parish Port Commission, for an injunction and declaratory judgment preventing defendants, a corporation and a storage company, from constructing and operating a natural gas storage facility, the Commission sought review of the judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which held that two parish ordinances were unenforceable and entered judgment in favor of defendants.


OVERVIEW: The Commission alleged that defendants' proposed construction and operation of a natural gas storage facility would violate two of its ordinances, one that prohibited dredging and excavating any portion of the water bottom of Lake Peigneur and one that prohibited the discharge of oil, grease, and refuse into the lake. After a hearing, the district court held that the ordinances were unenforceable because one was enacted in violation of the Louisiana Open Meeting Laws, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1-13, and one was preempted by state and federal statutes and regulations. The Commission appealed directly to the Louisiana Supreme Court, which transferred the appeal to the court. The court affirmed. The Commission, a non-home rule charter political subdivision, lacked constitutional authority to enact ordinances regulating Louisiana's waterways. Instead, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2074 gave the Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality the exclusive responsibility for formulating and promulgating environmental regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

Rodgers v. James River II, Inc.


No. 94-CA-1807


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1807 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/28/95); 661 So. 2d 173; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2461



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-14652, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party, individually and on behalf of his minor children, sought review of the judgment of the Civil District Court for the Paris of Orleans (Louisiana), which on a motion for summary judgment, dismissed his tort action against defendants, a company and its insurer, on the grounds that plaintiff was a statutory employee, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1061, and his exclusive remedy was worker's compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was employed by corporation, which contracted with defendant company, to remove asbestos insulation from the company's plant. While working plaintiff slipped on a stairwell and brought suit in tort against defendants. Defendants argued plaintiff was limited to worker's compensation remedies because he was a statutory employee, under § 23:1061. The trial court held the removal of asbestos was within the "trade, business, or occupation of defendant" and plaintiff was a statutory employee. Contrary to plaintiff's argument, the court stated prior decisions of the Circuit recognized that certain precedent, which plaintiff relied on, had been legislatively overruled by the 1989 amendment to § 23:1061. The uncontested facts demonstrated plaintiff was entitled to workers compensation benefits. Plaintiff was injured at the plant while in the course and scope of his employment under a contract between his employer and defendant company and the scope of work was directly related to the operation of defendant company's business. The constitutionality of § 23:1061 was not before the court because plaintiff had not properly raised it before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment in response to plaintiff's action in tort, was affirmed.

In re DiLeo


No. 95-CA-0444


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor sought review of a decision of the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans, (Louisiana), which affirmed a decision of the state medical board that imposed disciplinary actions on the doctor after he was found guilty of violating several provisions of the Medical Practice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1261 et. seq.


OVERVIEW: An administrative complaint was filed against the doctor that charged him with violating the Medical Practice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1261 et. seq. He was charged with prescribing various substances to eight of his patients that were in excess of legitimate medical justification in amounts, frequency, and duration, with continuing and recurring medical practice that failed to satisfy the prevailing and accepted standards of medical practice, and with medical incompetency. Boatwright v. Metropolitan Life Ins. Co.


No. 95-C-1822, C/W, No. 95-C-1823, C/W, No. 95-C-1913


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1822 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/28/95); 661 So. 2d 169; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2475



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused October 25, 1995. Released for Publication October 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-17060, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBIN GIARRUSSO, JUDGE AND CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 95-2302, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE LOUIS A. DiROSA, JUDGE AND 34TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. BERNARD. NO. 75-779, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE MELVYN J. PEREZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals the court granted certiorari from the judgments of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) and 34th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Bernard (Louisiana), which denied the exception to personal jurisdiction raised by relator company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individuals sought damages from various defendants and non-resident relator as a result of exposure to asbestos. Liability was premised on exposure to asbestos manufactured by a 1888 manufacturing company. Through a series of mergers and acquisitions, the asbestos manufacturing corporation merged with series of other corporations and transferred liabilities. However, at one point during the process the liabilities were transferred to a subsidiary. The mergers and acquisitions continued, without the subsidiary, and the manufacturing corporation eventually merged with relator's predecessor corporation. Relator argued the trial court erred when it denied relator's exception to personal jurisdiction. After considering the reasoning used by other state courts, the court held the exception should have been granted. The court held relator could not have foreseen being sued in this state to answer for liabilities of a long nonexistent corporation, the business of which had been taken over by a subsidiary that relator never owned. More important, the relator had no contacts in Louisiana from which it availed itself of the privilege of doing business in this state.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgments, which denied relator's exception to personal jurisdiction, were reversed and the exception was granted as to all cases.

 

695 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Villarrubia


No. 95-CA-0346


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0346 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/28/95); 662 So. 2d 85; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2484



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-2628, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MICHAEL G. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandson appealed from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which issued summary judgment in favor of defendants, the testator's two surviving sons, and dismissed his petition to re-open the succession of his grandmother. The grandson argued that his signing of a receipt for legacy did not constitute a waiver of his rights as a forced heir to assert a claim for his share of the forced portion of the estate.


OVERVIEW: The grandson was the nephew of the two surviving sons, whose brother had predeceased the testator. Upon receiving his particular legacy of $ 1,000, the grandson signed a receipt for legacy acknowledging his receipt of the $ 1,000 and consented to the rendering of a judgment, placing the residuary legatees into possession of the remainder of the estate. The grandson then sought to re-open the succession and recover the forced portion which was denied his father's estate. The court found that the trial judge was clearly wrong in holding that by signing the receipt of legacy, the grandson had waived any right to assert a claim for his share of the forced portion of his grandmother's estate. As a particular legatee, he was required to execute a receipt for legacy to evidence his receiving the $ 1,000 due him. The receipt served as confirmation that the terms of the will were carried out, insofar as his status as a particular legatee was concerned. The receipt contained no language that could have been reasonably construed as a waiver of any rights he may have had as a forced heir. Absent such language, the court found that the document was a receipt for legacy and nothing more.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the testator's sons and remanded the case to the trial court to re-open the succession and to allow the grandson to assert his claims as a forced heir of the estate.

Rivard v. Petroleum Transp. Co.


No. 95-CA-0431


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0431 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/28/95); 663 So. 2d 755; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2472



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused December 19, 1995. Released for Publication December 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 83-19664, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE FRANK V. ZACCARIA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurance guaranty association (association) filed an exception of prescription and appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, No. 83-19664, Division "B," (Louisiana), which awarded plaintiffs, a wife and her children, damages for economic and consortium loss and for the pain and suffering endured by a passenger killed as a result of the negligence of a driver operating the insured vehicle.


OVERVIEW: In August 1983, a driver operating a vehicle owned by his insured employer was attempting to exit a highway at a high rate of speed, when the vehicle turned over and caught fire. In November 1983, the wife and children of an unauthorized guest passenger killed in the accident filed a damages action against the vehicle's insurer. In 1989, an amended petition added a claim against the association, substituted for the insolvent insurer, as an omnibus insurer for the negligent driver. The court held that interest was due from the date of that original judicial demand. The court held that retroactively applying the statutory cap on damages would have unconstitutionally divested the plaintiffs of a property right. The court held that the awards for loss of consortium were not an abuse of discretion but were supported by evidence that the children would enter adolescence without their father's support.


OUTCOME: The court denied the association's exception of prescription and affirmed the judgment awarding damages to the wife and children.

State v. Eggerson


No. 95-KA-1337


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1337 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/15/95); 661 So. 2d 1096; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2429



September 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 370-851, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), sentencing defendant as a third felony offender to serve 10 years at hard labor. The State contended that the trial court erred in concluding that the mandatory minimum sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(F) and 15:529.1 was unconstitutionally excessive for defendant.


OVERVIEW: The State sought review of the trial court's judgment sentencing defendant as a third felony offender to 10 years at hard labor. The court vacated the sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing in conformity with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The trial court did not support its decision to divert from the minimum sentence with sufficient argument and analysis. The mandatory minimum sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(F) and 15:529.1 was 20 years at hard labor. The court held that the trial court failed to conduct a meaningful assessment of any mitigating or aggravating circumstances and its conclusory statements did not qualify as the type of searching inquiry necessary to justify declaring a legislatively mandated sentence unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the trial court sentencing defendant and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Hyorth


No. 95-K-1181


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1181 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/15/95); 661 So. 2d 1059; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2435



September 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION. CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 276-390, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; REVERSED & REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a sentence that had been imposed on defendant, as a multiple offender, by the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which sentenced him to 27 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension on the multiple bill for armed robbery, notwithstanding that it was below the minimum required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been found guilty of two counts of armed robbery, the offense having occurred while he was on probation for another armed robbery, based on his having robbed two persons while armed with a revolver. Having sentenced and resentenced defendant on several occasions for various reasons, the trial court ultimately sentenced defendant to 27 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence on the multiple bill that was below the minimum set by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The court reversed, stating first that while the trial court had discretion to find that the multiple bill minimum sentence was grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime and constitutionally excessive as to defendant, the statutory minimum should not be deviated from unless it was nothing more than a needless infliction of pain. Here, the court said, the original offense and the offense used for the multiple bill conviction were for armed robberies. Because of the possibility of great bodily harm to the victims, because defendant was armed, and because there no mitigating factors, the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing below the minimum.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment sentencing defendant below the statutory minimum reversed and remanded for resentencing.

Guidry v. Bank of Laplace


No. 94-CA-1758


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1758 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/15/95); 661 So. 2d 1052; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2442



September 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 89-8267, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE OKLA JONES, II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant banks appealed a judgment of the Orleans Parish Civil District Court (Louisiana), which entered a jury verdict of $ 4.54 million in favor of plaintiff customer on the customer's claim for breach of fiduciary duty. The trial court refused to instruct the jury on the applicability of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6:1124 (1995).


OVERVIEW: A customer of a bank invested $ 12 million with a swindler who was running a Ponzi scheme out of a second bank. The customer lost over $ 5 million when the scheme collapsed and the customer brought an action against both banks and the swindler. The jury awarded damages and apportioned them among all parties. The court on appeal found reversible error where the trial court refused a requested jury instruction on § 6:1124 which limited the fiduciary duties of the banks to those contained in any written agreement. The court found the remaining jury instructions misleading and confusing because they permitted liability without the imposition of a duty. The court next found that the jury was incorrectly instructed that a cause of action for aiding and abetting existed under Louisiana law. Finally, the court undertook a de novo review of the record and awarded the banks judgment as a matter of law because they had no duty running to the customer to investigate the Ponzi scheme or to disclose to the customer information about the swindler's account.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award as to the liability of the banks and affirmed the award as to the liability of the swindler, who did not appeal.

Rock v. City of New Orleans


No. 94-CA-2613


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-2613 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/15/95); 661 So. 2d 1091; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2443



September 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NO. 92-09390, DISTRICT EIGHT. HONORABLE MARK ZIMMERMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a police officer who sustained a job-related injury in March 1983 and who disputed the termination of her compensation benefits in November 1991, sought review of a decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC) (Louisiana), which sustained an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction filed by appellee municipality on the ground that the accident occurred prior to July 1983.


OVERVIEW: When a municipality in November 1991 terminated the worker's compensation benefits a job-injured police officer was receiving as a result of an injury sustained in March 1983, the officer filed a disputed claim with the (OWC). The office's hearing officer granted an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction filed by the city, because the accident occurred before the July 1983 date on which the OWC was first created and authorized to handle disputed claims for benefits. On appeal, the officer argued that there was no "claim" for worker's compensation until November 1991, which was the date that the dispute between the parties arose, and, thus, the hearing officer erred in his application of the law. The court agreed, pointing to language in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3, which provided that a "claim" for benefits was initiated by the filing of the appropriate form with the OWC, and not dependent upon the date in which an injury was sustained.


OUTCOME: The decision dismissing a police officer's disputed claim for worker's compensation benefits was reversed and the matter was remanded.

State v. Miller


No. CR95-77


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-77 (La.App. 3 Cir. 08/30/95); 663 So. 2d 107; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2425



August 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, Honorable Robert Brinkman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: DECREE Affirmed And Remanded With Instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana) of carnal knowledge of a juvenile, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of carnal knowledge of a juvenile, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80(A)(1). His motion to quash the indictment was denied, and defendant, after reaching a plea agreement with the State, entered a plea of guilty. Pursuant to the terms of the agreement, defendant's sentence of five years at hard labor was suspended, and he was placed on five years active supervised probation, with conditions. In affirming the decision, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81 applied to defendant who was over the age of 17 at the time of the offense. After his 17th birthday had passed, he was considered over the age of 17. Further, § 14:80 did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Louisiana Constitutions. Any equal protection issue raised by §14:80 was well settled in Louisiana law. Nevertheless, defendant was not given credit for time served, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 880.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied defendant's motion to quash, and remanded that case to amend the commitment and the minute entry of sentencing to give defendant credit for time served in accordance with the statute.

State v. White


No. 27,188-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,188 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/23/95); 660 So. 2d 515; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2322



August 23, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 21, 1995. Released for Publication September 28, 1995.
Writ denied by State ex rel. White v. State, 692 So. 2d 1076, 1997 La. LEXIS 1225 (La., Apr. 25, 1997)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at White v. Michael, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 84013 (W.D. La., Oct. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 165,915. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo Louisiana, which convicted him of possession with intent to distribute cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A(1), as charged by the state by bill of information. The state subsequently charged defendant as a third felony offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, to which he was convicted and sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw defendant selling drugs. The officer did not arrest defendant, but continued to patrol the area over the next several days. The officer also warned defendant that the police were watching him. Subsequently, the officer returned with other officers in an "organized routine patrol strike" to conduct field interviews and an investigation. Defendant ran, and several officers pursued. One officer picked up a matchbox that he saw defendant drop. It contained 4.4 grams of cocaine, an amount that was consistent with usage for distribution purposes. Based on the facts, the court concluded that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress the cocaine. Further, defendant did not argue adequate grounds to quash the bill of information under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 532 and 534. Additionally, the evidence was sufficient for the state to conclude that defendant sold crack cocaine for a living and to present this conclusion to the jury in closing argument. Further, the sentence was not excessive because once defendant achieved the status of third felony offender, the trial court lacked discretion and was mandated to impose a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court that convicted defendant of possession with intent to distribute cocaine and with being a third felony offender as charged by the state. The court also affirmed the life sentence that the trial court rendered against defendant.

 

704 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ganier


No. 94-KA-2582


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-2582 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/23/95); 660 So. 2d 928; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2340



August 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 367-959, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant complained of his conviction by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), for possession of 28 or more but less than 200 grams of cocaine. At trial, defendant admitted that the cocaine belonged to him. On appeal, he challenged the validity of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(a), as well as the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(a) did not criminalize non-criminal activity; one was not subject to criminal prosecution for possessing a non-controlled substance as long as it did not contain a detectable amount of cocaine. The court held, too, that § 40:967(F)(1)(a) did not violate equal protection. Hypothetical cases of unequal treatment depending on the amount of pure cocaine and the amount of the non-controlled substance were irrelevant because constitutional challenges could not be based on hypothetical situations. Defendant did not sustain his burden of proving that the classification contained in § 40:967(F)(1)(a) was without a rational basis. The provision constituted an appropriate exercise of police power and furthered a legitimate state purpose. The statute described the unlawful conduct, possession of cocaine, with sufficient clarity that persons of reasonable intelligence were capable of discerning its meaning and conforming their conduct to it. Defendant admitted the cocaine belonged to him, and a criminalist testified that the powder contained cocaine and weighed 58 grams. Thus, the State proved defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Cinel


No. 95-K-1723


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-1723 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/18/95); 660 So. 2d 887; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2302



August 18, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 349-764, SECTION "D". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state filed an application for writs and sought review of a ruling of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to suppress the communication between defendant and his former attorney in spite of the fact that the former attorney testified at a hearing on a motion to quash the bill of information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant priest waived his attorney-client privilege so that his former attorney could testify at a hearing on a motion to quash the bill of information charging defendant with possession of child pornography. Later, the prosecution indicated that it intended to use statements made by defendant to his former attorney at trial because defendant had waived his attorney-client privilege. Defendant filed a motion to suppress his statements to his former attorney and the trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the prosecution argued that defendant had made an unlimited waiver of the attorney-client privilege when he permitted his former attorney to testify at the hearing on the motion to quash the bill of information. The appellate court, in affirming the decision of the trial court, held that the record supported the conclusion that defendant's waiver of the attorney-client privilege was intended to be limited to the hearing on the motion to quash. The court therefore denied the State's application for supervisory writs.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for supervisory writs and affirmed the trial court's ruling on the motion to suppress.

 

706 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Bruscato v. Avant


No. 95-C-0573


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0573 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/26/95); 660 So. 2d 72; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 2130



July 26, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1995. Released for Publication September 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIORARI FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 88-11877, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MICHAEL G. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT APPLICATION GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator mother sought supervisory writs after the judgment from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted respondent father custody of the parties' minor child and held that the Post-Separation Family Violence Act was applicable to proceedings which were initiated prior to its enactment.


OVERVIEW: The mother took the minor child and travelled across the country by way of shelters for battered women. The minor child was returned to Louisiana. Because it was impractical for the trial court to award joint custody, because the mother lived in Montana, the trial court awarded the father sole custody. The judgment was appealed and reversed and remanded for retrial. The Act was enacted, and the trial court held that the Act established new rules, rights, and duties which related to relief from family violence when the family was separated and did not apply retroactively. The mother sought supervisory review of that ruling. The court stated the legislature expressed no intent as to whether the statutes encompassed by the Act were retroactively applicable, but the preamble to the Act clearly indicated that the statute was remedial in nature. The court granted the supervisory writ and held that the Act was applicable to the parties' case. The court took particular notice of certain provisions of the Act, which were applicable to the action between the parties.


OUTCOME: The mother's application for supervisory writs was granted and, upon retrial of the custody issue, the trial court was instructed to consider the pertinent provisions of the Act.

 

707 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Facio v. Glaviano


No. 95-CA-35


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-35 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/28/95); 658 So. 2d 33; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1969



June 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKER'S COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. STATE OF LOUISIANA, DISTRICT 07. NUMBER 93-02544. HONORABLE G. WALTON CAIRE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a judgment from the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration (Louisiana), which denied her claim for worker's compensation benefits for carpal tunnel syndrome which she alleged to be an occupational disease caused by flexing her wrists during the performance of her job duties for defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee stopped working as a dental assistant due to endometriosis. She later developed pain in her hands and was told she suffered from carpal tunnel syndrome. She filed a worker's compensation claim against her former employer, alleging that her disability was the result of a work-related injury. The administrative law judge rejected her claim. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because the employee had worked for her employer for less than 12 months, she was required to prove that her occupational disease was contracted during the course of her employment by an overwhelming preponderance of the evidence pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1031.1(D). The employee did not meet her burden of proof. There were discrepancies in her testimony as to when the complaints of pain actually began. She never mentioned the pain to a doctor who treated her while she was still employed and her medical records from a visit to the hospital prior to the termination of her employment did not mention pain in her wrists. The court refused to address the issue of whether § 23:1031.1 was unconstitutional because the employee did not plead that issue at the trial court level.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the employee's claim for worker's compensation benefits.

Boeing Co. v. La. Dep't of Econ. Dev.


94 CA 0971


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0971 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/23/95); 657 So. 2d 652; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1891



June 23, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 390,534), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ROBERT D. DOWNING, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: DECREE For the above and foregoing reasons, the judgment of the trial court is REVERSED and the petition is dismissed. Costs in the sum of $ 387.68 are to be divided equally.

REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Louisiana Department of Economic Development and the State Board of Commerce and Industry (the Board), sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), vacating the Board's denial of the application by appellee contractor for a tax exemption under the state's industrial ad valorem tax exemption program.


OVERVIEW: The contractor filed an application with the Board for an exemption from ad valorem taxes on equipment, machinery, and building materials purchased for a particular facility.The Board denied the application and the contractor appealed to district court. The district court vacated the Board's denial and remanded the matter with instructions. The Board sought review of the district court's judgment. The court reversed that judgment because it found that the district court had no jurisdiction over the matter. According to the court, because there was no statutory or constitutional requirement mandating that the Board's determination be made after hearing with notice, judicial review under the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:964, was not available. The court also found that there was no original jurisdiction on the part of the district court because the action did not involve constitutional questions or excess of authority claims. And, according to the court, the regulation of ad valorem tax exemptions was not a civil matter within the meaning of La. Const. art. V, § 16(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment vacating the Board's denial of the contractor's application for a tax exemption under the state's industrial ad valorem tax exemption program.

 

709 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Guste v. Green


No. 94 CA 1138


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1138 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/23/95); 657 So. 2d 610; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1898



June 23, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, SUIT NUMBER 364,607. HONORABLE PAUL B. LANDRY, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, certain corporations, appealed from a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which determined that the corporations constituted a single business enterprise and granted a permanent injunction prohibiting the named corporations from disposing of their assets and records and the assets and records of another corporation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the two corporations involved in the appeal, along with other defendants, constituted a single business enterprise (SBE) under the control of an individual. The trial court enjoined the two corporations from disposing of any assets and records and ordered them to deliver all their assets to the commissioner of insurance. The court affirmed. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:731 et seq., the commissioner was authorized to use summary proceedings in a liquidation proceeding. The corporations were not entitled to a jury trial because a trial by jury was not available for summary proceedings. The commissioner was not required to show irreparable harm because the injunction was issued pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:734, which specifically provided for an injunction as a remedy in a liquidation proceeding to restrain persons from disposing of property. The trial court properly determined that the corporations were part of an SBE controlled by one individual. The individual was in control of most of the corporations, they were minimally capitalized and nearly all went out of business after the individual severed his relationship with them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the corporations constituted a single business enterprise and affirmed the decision to grant a permanent injunction prohibiting the named corporations from disposing of their assets and records and the assets and records of another corporation.

Cage v. Adoption Options of La., Inc.


No. 94 CA 2173


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2173 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/23/95); 657 So. 2d 670; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1914



June 23, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 400,993. Honorable Bob Downing, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed from an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which dismissed his petition pursuant to defendant State's exception of no cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The father filed a lawsuit attacking the constitutionality of the Children's Code, alleging that La. Child Code arts. 1137 and 1138 were unconstitutional because they deprived him of equal protection and due process. He contended that he was not served with notice of the mother's surrender of the child, in violation of La. Child Code art. 1133 and was, therefore, entitled to damages from the unlawful surrender. The trial court sustained an exception of no cause of action. The court affirmed, finding that the lawsuit represented an impermissible collateral attack on the judgment of the juvenile court terminating his parental rights. The father challenged the constitutionality of the provisions which required a juvenile court to terminate an alleged father's parental rights in the course of an adoption proceeding where he failed to establish parental rights. The issue of the constitutionality of the challenged provisions was clearly a matter within the exclusive jurisdiction of the juvenile court. There was no legal impediment to prevent the father from raising the constitutional issues in the juvenile court and the appeal represented a collateral attack on the prior judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed the father's petition.

Whittington v. Wall


No. CA 94 2226


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2226 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/23/95); 657 So. 2d 1058; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1919



June 23, 1995, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 388,418. Honorable Bob H. Hester, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sought review of the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) dismissing his challenge to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3(C). The prisoner contended that his ineligibility to earn a diminution of his sentence under § 15:571.3(C) because he was a habitual offender deprived him of equal protection of the laws and subjected him to cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was ineligible for "good time" because he was a habitual offender, as defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. He challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3(C) because other prisoners who committed more serious crimes were eligible for good time credits. Affirming the trial court's dismissal, the court rejected his equal protection challenge under La. Const. art. I, § 3 on the grounds that: (1) the award of good time was a matter of state law; (2) inmates did not constitute a suspect class; (3) a rational basis existed for the classification of crimes because it promoted the state's legitimate desire to prevent the early release of serious offenders; and (4) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3 was amended by 1994 La. Acts 149 and 150 to include more serious offenses and crimes of violence as listed in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13). The prisoner's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment under La. Const. art. I, § 20, or U.S. Const. amend. VIII because the denial of good time was not purposeless, needless, or grossly out of proportion to the severity of his three crimes, and he was serving less than the maximum for simple burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the prisoner's action.
