City of Bogalusa v. Washington Parish Sales/Use Tax Centralization Comm'n


No. 94 CA 2413


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2413 (La.App. 1 Cir.06/23/95); 658 So. 2d 1336; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1930



June 23, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 25, 1995. Released for Publication August 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 70,766. Honorable John W. Greene, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tax centralization commission appealed from the judgment of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Washington (Louisiana), which held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2544.1D was constitutional, declared that the commission's acceptance of the sheriff's proposal was invalid, enjoined an award to the sheriff, and ordered the commission to enter into a contract with plaintiff city to serve as the tax collecting agent.


OVERVIEW: Section 33:2544.1 was enacted without the notice of intent to introduce the bill or publication in an official state journal. When the parish's taxing bodies could not agree on a central tax collector for the parish, the commission was formed. The commission members agreed to proceed under a one member-one vote basis instead of the weighted vote scheme that was set forth under § 33:2544.1D. The commission requested bids, and a majority of the commission agreed to accept the sheriff's proposal to collect the taxes. Had the votes been weighted, the city's proposal would have been accepted. The commission adopted a resolution to accept the sheriff's proposal to serve as the collection agent. The court found that the legislature fulfilled its mandate under La. Const. art. VII, § 3(B)(1) by enacting La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2844.1A. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court held that § 33:2544.1D was unconstitutional because the mandated notification requirements of La. Const. art. III, § 13 were not met, and it was clearly a local law. The court found no reasonable basis for the legislature's decision to determine legislatively the weight to be accorded the commission's votes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that the contested and severable section of the statute was unconstitutional.

Mouton v. Department of Wildlife & Fisheries


No. 95 CA 0101


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0101 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/23/95); 657 So. 2d 622; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1934



June 23, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 25, 1995. Released for Publication July 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 401,015. Honorable Joseph F. Keogh, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent intervenor, the state legislature, sought review of an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of petitioner citizen and petitioner intervenors, a fishing association and an environmental group, in their action for mandamus seeking an order directing respondent, the state wildlife and fisheries commission, to enforce the trout management plan.


OVERVIEW: The state wildlife and fisheries commission adopted a trout management plan that among other things prohibited weekend commercial taking of spotted sea trout. Subsequently the legislature adopted a concurrent resolution nullifying the weekend commercial portion of the trout plan. Petitioners sought an order directing enforcement of the trout plan including the weekend prohibition; they sought to compel performance of a public duty. The trial court found that the trout plan was valid and the concurrent resolution was invalid, and made the writ of mandamus peremptory. The legislature alleged several errors by the trial court including denying their peremptory exception and finding that petitioner had a right of action to compel an agency to enforce a rule, when that rule had general application and petitioners had no special interest, distinct from the public at large, in its enforcement. The court held that while all citizens had an interest in the public trusts of the state's various natural resources, no one citizen or citizen group had a special interest beyond that enjoyed by the general public. The court found that petitioners lacked standing to maintain an action for mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court in favor of the citizen making peremptory the writ of mandamus.

State v. Payne


No. 94-KA-1114


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1114 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/07/95); 657 So. 2d 531; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1763



June 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 365-162, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of being a felon in possession of a firearm and sentenced him to five years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped on a bridge by a police officer. The officer noticed that defendant's license tag had expired. When defendant returned from the officer's car to search for his vehicle registration, the dome light in his car came on and the officer noticed a handgun on the front seat of defendant's vehicle. The officer then discovered that defendant was on probation for possession of cocaine. Defendant was convicted of being a felon in possession of a firearm and sentenced to five years at hard labor. On appeal defendant alleged that the State impermissibly exercised it peremptory challenges to exclude prospective jurors based on their race and was therefor entitled to a new trial. On appeal the court held that considering the fact that 11 of the 12 peremptory challenges were African-American and that the lower court requested race-neutral reasons from the State, that defendant had proved a prima facie case of discrimination. However, the court determined that after reviewing the State's reasons, coupled with the fact that 8 of the 12 members of the jury were African-American, the trial court had not erred when it denied his motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision, which convicted defendant of being a felon in possession of a firearm and sentenced him to five years at hard labor.

Housing Auth. v. Green


No. 94-CA-1650


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1650 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/07/95); 657 So. 2d 552; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1772



June 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 25, 1995. Certiorari Denied April 29, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 2857.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIRST CITY COURT OF NEW ORLEANS. NO. 94-23130, SECTION "B". HONORABLE DOMINIC C. GRIESHABER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff housing authority filed an action for a Rule of Possession against defendant tenant after the tenant had a guest on the leased premises in possession of drugs. The First City Court of New Orleans (Louisiana) granted the Rule for Possession and the tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenant had no knowledge of the presence of the drugs in her apartment, which were brought in by an acquaintance of the tenant's daughter. On appeal, the tenant contended that the trial court erred in evicting her under the circumstances where the housing authority failed to prove that she had knowledge of the illegal drugs in her apartment or that she had control over the actions of her daughter's overnight guest. In addition, the tenant argued that the trial court's eviction violated her due process rights. The court affirmed and stated that there was no constitutional right to public housing. Because the lease provisions provided for the eviction of any tenant with drugs in their apartment and that tenants were presumed to have control over guests, the court held that the eviction was proper. The housing authority's policy of zero tolerance to drugs on the premises was not unreasonable, nor were the lease provisions in question unlawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the eviction.

Bouillion v. City of New Iberia


NUMBER 95-120


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-120 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/31/95); 657 So. 2d 397; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1397



May 31, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberia, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Paul J. deMahy, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 78674.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The city appealed a judgment from the 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberia (Louisiana). The trial court ordered the city to pay plaintiff employees, with the exception of one employee, for accumulated sick leave. The trial court also awarded attorney fees to the prevailing employees but dismissed their claim for penalties.


OVERVIEW: City employees filed an action to be compensated for the unused sick leave each had accumulated prior to January 1, 1991. One employee also sought payment for sick leave that he alleged had accumulated after January 1, 1991. The trial court rejected the latter employee's claims but ordered the city to pay the other employees for the sick leave in dispute. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court committed error in awarding payment for sick leave that had accumulated prior to January 1, 1991. A new civil rule that allowed employees to be paid for accumulated sick leave, although enacted prior to January 1, 1991, had not become effective until January 1, 1991. Prior to January 1, 1991, an employee had no right to payment for unused sick leave. The court rejected the trial court's finding that payment for sick leave accumulated prior to the effective date of the rule was not a retroactive application of the rule but was simply a different method of compensating an employee for a right already earned. An award of the sick leave accumulated prior to the rule change would constitute a retroactive increase in pay prohibited by La. Const. art. VII, § 14(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment to the extent that it awarded payment for sick leave accumulated prior to January 1, 1991 and to the extent that it awarded attorney fees to the prevailing employees. The court otherwise affirmed.

State v. Brown


95-KA-124


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-124 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/30/95); 656 So. 2d 1070; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1468



May 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 94-1045. HONORABLE ROBERT J. BURNS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the 24th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), in which he was found guilty on four counts of intimidating a witness, proscribed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:129.1, and sentenced as a fourth-felony multiple offender to 40-years hard labor pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i).


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of sending threatening letters to a former girlfriend who was set to testify against him on extortion charges and to her daughter. The defendant argued that certain statements in the letters which referred to his criminal past and his criminal history should have been redacted by the trial court because they were inadmissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 404(B)(1). He argued that they did not establish motive, opportunity, intent, nor were they an integral part of the crime of intimidation. The court held that the letters were properly offered because they tended to prove the res gestae of the offense of intimidation. The court held that the defendant failed to preserve claims that his sentence was excessive because he did not set forth specific grounds in his motion to reconsider under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1 and found that it was not unconstitutionally excessive, pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 20. The court found that only one count of the multi-count indictment could be used to enhance the defendant's sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, because the convictions were entered on the same day.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction but remanded for resentencing.

State v. Ellis


No. 94-KA-599


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-599 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/30/95); 657 So. 2d 341; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1718



May 30, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. STATE OF LOUISIANA, PARISH OF JEFFERSON. NO. 93-5555, DIVISION "F". THE HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS TO ELLIS; CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED AS TO KENNAIR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and his co-conspirator appealed their convictions for conspiracy to commit first degree murder from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division F (Louisiana). They also challenged their sentences and adjudications as multiple offenders.


OVERVIEW: The convictions were based on evidence that defendant enlisted the help of the co-conspirator for the purposes of killing his former supervisor and the superintendent of schools. The co-conspirator sought the assistance of another individual about the plan, and that individual notified the police. An undercover investigation ensued, resulting in the arrest and convictions. Both defendants raised numerous errors on appeal. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting hearsay statements made by the co-conspirator into evidence at the pre-trial hearing for the purposes of determining whether a prima facie case of conspiracy had been established. The admission of certain audio and videotapes generated during the course of the investigation were admissible to show defendants' intent, as well as furtherance of the conspiracy. The prosecution's was not obligated to disclose a potentially exculpatory statement of a witness where the defense was aware of the witness prior to trial, and where the defense did not make either a general or a specific request for the statements of all confidential informants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant and his co-conspirator's sentences. The court vacated the co-conspirator's sentence and remanded for re-sentencing because his adjudication as a habitual offender was improper where his prior conviction did not fall within five years of the commission of the principal offense.

State v. Taylor


No. 93-KA-226


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-226 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/30/95); 656 So. 2d 722; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1472



May 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1995.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Taylor v. Hines, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 140061 (E.D. La., May 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, NO. 90-0191, DIVISION "E", HONORABLE JOEL T. CHAISSON, JUDGE.
State v. Taylor, 597 So. 2d 123, 1992 La. App. LEXIS 957 (La.App. 5 Cir., 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 29th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which entered a conviction against him for two counts for distribution of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A(1), and sentenced him to 15 years at hard labor as a multiple offender. Defendant argued that the district court failed to re-sentence him in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of two counts of distribution of cocaine, the district court sentenced him as a multiple offender and imposed a sentence of 15 years at hard labor against him. Specifically, the court held that defendant was re-sentenced in accordance with § 15:529.1 where he was represented by an attorney and was thoroughly advised of his rights, where the state clearly met its burden of proving the existence of defendant's prior guilty plea and that defendant was represented by counsel when it was taken, and where defendant failed to produce any evidence showing an infringement of his rights or a procedural irregularity in the taking of his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence to 15 years at hard labor as a multiple offender.

State v. Moses


No. 94-K-0489


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0489 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/16/95); 655 So. 2d 779; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1234



May 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 28, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: STATE OF LOUISIANA APPLICATION FOR SUPERVISORY WRIT. CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 368-138, SECTION "A". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; MOTION TO QUASH GRANTED; CASE DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for a supervisory writ seeking review of a ruling of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which denied his motion to quash his indictment for violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1463(C)(3) by distributing or causing the distribution of campaign literature that did not contain the name and address of the person responsible for its contents.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not charged with making any false statements or false attribution. The State contended that defendant failed to show a substantial likelihood of a significant inhibitory effect upon valid expression. In reversing the trial court's ruling, the court held that the right to distribute anonymous campaign literature was clearly protected by U.S. Const. amend. I and La. Const. art. 1, §§ 5 and 7. Accordingly, the court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1463(C)(3) to be an unconstitutional restraint on the constitutional rights of freedom of expression and the right to privacy. The court stated that defendant did not have the burden to show a significant inhibitory effect of the statute, but rather, the State had the burden to demonstrate a compelling interest to justify the restraints upon the protected freedom of expression, and to show that the limitation was no greater than necessary to protect such interest. The court noted that as a practical matter, anonymous campaign literature might be the only way, for example, that unclassified government employees would be able to express political views without risking the loss of their jobs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling, granted defendant's writ and the motion to quash the indictment, and dismissed the case.

State v. Slater


No. 26,939-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,939 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/10/95); 655 So. 2d 684; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1201



May 10, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 93-F1088. Honorable John R. Joyce, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his sentence of 10 years at hard labor with a $ 2,000 fine from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), following his guilty plea to possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a state trooper and gave permission to search the car. The search yielded 102 pounds of marijuana in the trunk, which defendant admitted that he was to be paid $ 3,000 for transporting. Defendant, who was 47 years old, had one prior conviction for a similar amount of drugs. Defendant was steadily employed, well educated, and had a 10-year-old son. The trial court imposed a 10-year sentence. In affirming, the court held that the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. The court agreed that the large quantity of drugs to be likely distributed to a large amount of people, defendant's age, defendant's prior conviction, and the fact that defendant was to be paid for his services all merited a severe sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of 10 years and a $ 2,000 fine.

 

722 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pilcher


No. 27,085-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


27,085 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/10/95); 655 So. 2d 636; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1221



May 10, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Thirty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caldwell, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 45,295. Honorable John B. Whitaker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a 15-year-old, sought review of a judgment from the Thirty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caldwell (Louisiana), which convicted him of two counts of second degree murder and sentenced him to life without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stopped at a home to ask to use the telephone. The woman who answered the door complied with his request, and also gave him with a glass of water. Defendant then fatally shot her in the head in front of her two children. Defendant chased the children, fatally shooting one child. Defendant was tried as an adult and convicted of two counts of second-degree murder. His sentence was for life without parole. On appeal, defendant contended that the statutory scheme for treating as adults those juveniles accused of certain crimes, La. Ch. Code Ann. art. 305(B), was unconstitutional because it denied him the opportunity, at any stage of the proceedings, to assert his youth in order to show that he was less culpable than an adult. The court noted that the statute reflected the legislature's determination that those persons 15 and older were of sufficient understanding to be tried as adults for certain serious crimes such as second-degree murder. According to the court, this scheme did not violate any constitutional rights on its face, or as applied against defendant. The court also held that, given the nature of the crime, the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of second-degree murder and his sentence to life in prison without parole.

 

723 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sorrell


No. 95-KH-136


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-136 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/10/95); 656 So. 2d 1045; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1252



May 10, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 89-2382, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the 24h Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) which determined that he was required to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of forcible rape in 1989 and sentenced to five years hard labor. The sentence was suspended and he was placed on active probation. In 1993, his probation was revoked and the original sentence was imposed. Two years later, he was released on good time credit. It was stipulated that he was released as if on parole and was ordered to register as a sex offender under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:542, 15:574.4. The trial court denied defendant's petition challenging the requirement that he register as a sex offender. The court affirmed, rejecting defendant's contention that the statutory requirements of the sexual offender registration law did not apply to him because they were not effective until after his date of conviction. The court held that the legislature clearly intended that the statute apply to all persons convicted of sex offenses before the statute was enacted. Furthermore, the court noted that defendant was ordered to register under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4 which made registration applicable to parol requirements. Because that law was in effect at the time he was paroled, he was subject to its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

724 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Moody v. United Nat'l Ins. Co.


95-CA-1


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


95-1 (La.App. 5 Cir. 5/10/95); 657 So. 2d 236; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1257



May 10, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 453-622. HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF SEPTEMBER 12, 1994 AFFIRMED; JUDGMENT OF OCTOBER 7, 1994 VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents and son, appealed an order from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, finding that the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. § 40:1229, was constitutional and dismissing the suit against defendant doctor.


OVERVIEW: The son was injured when he was assaulted outside a movie theater. The parents alleged that the doctor failed to properly treat the son's head injuries and as a result the son suffered irreversible brain damage. The parents and son challenged the constitutionality of the Medical Malpractice Act (Act), which limited the recovery of a patient against a doctor. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that it was bound by the Louisiana Supreme Court's decision, which found that the Act was constitutional. The court stated that it was not free to overrule the decision of the highest state court. However, the court found that the dismissal of the parents and son's suit was error. A declaratory judgment was the appropriate remedy for the parents and son to challenge the constitutionality of the Act. The court could not force the parents and son to accept the doctor's tender where there was no settlement because such an action would preclude any further relief. The parents and son were entitled to a final ruling on the constitutionality of their claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that the Medical Malpractice Act was constitutional and vacated the judgment dismissing the suit against the doctor.

 

725 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Commission on Ethics for Pub. Employees


No. 95 CW 0021


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0021 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/5/95); 656 So. 2d 670; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1359



May 5, 1995, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1995. Released for Publication June 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to a Decision of the Commission on Ethics for Public Employees, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 94-174. Robert C. Snyder, Chairman, Victor Bussie, Thomas W. Barham, Cary S. Goss and Avis Baker-White, Members.



DISPOSITION: WRIT RECALLED AND APPLICATION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator association sought review of an advisory opinion of respondent Commission on Ethics for Public Employees (Commission) (Louisiana) that determined that the association's employees were public employees within the meaning of the Code of Governmental Ethics.


OVERVIEW: The association challenged the advisory opinion of the commission and asserted that it erred in its finding that the association's employees were public employees and that they were subject to the authority of the commission. The commission asserted that appellate review should not have been granted for a purely advisory opinion, and the legislatively created association could not avoid the application of the Ethics Code. The court denied the association's appeal and found that its application for supervisory writs under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1142A was the appropriate vehicle to challenge the commission's advisory opinions. The court held that the association, despite any language contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1380 that it was not a state agency, was a state agency within the contemplation of the Ethics Code. The association was a creation of the legislature, which specifically defined its powers, and subjected it to the oversight of the Commissioner of Insurance. The association's property, which was derived from mandatory tax assessments upon all insurers, was transferred into the state general fund. Moreover, the association functioned solely for the public benefit.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied the association's appeal of the commission's advisory opinion that the association's employees were subject to the Ethics Code.

Rhodes v. State ex rel DOT & Dev.


No. 94 CA 1758


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1758 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/5/95); 656 So. 2d 650; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1370



May 5, 1995, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 1, 1995. Released for Publication June 1, 1995. Rehearing Granted June 21, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1814.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, State of Louisiana, Docket Nos. 101,305 and 101,432. Honorable Baron B. Bourg, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, vehicle accident victims, appealed the judgment of the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which held that defendant state transportation department was not liable for an accident that occurred between the victims when they both entered an intersection on a green light from a malfunctioning traffic signal.


OVERVIEW: Two victims entered an intersection in their vehicles after they both received a green signal from a defective traffic light, and collided. The victims each sued the state transportation department (agency) in negligence and strict liability. The trial court found for the agency, and the victims appealed the ruling. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 allowing the victims to sue the agency was beyond the legislature's authority because the statute imposed more stringent requirements on plaintiffs who sued state entities over prove entities. The court also determined that because the trial court made a manifestly erroneous by failing to address the constitutionality of § 9:2800, it would review the case de novo. The court stated that under the facts of the case, the agency was strictly liable for the accident, due to the defective condition of the traffic light. Finally, the court concluded that the victims were entitled to general damages, loss of consortium, lost wages, and past and future medical expenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court which had held in favor of the agency.

State v. Johnson


NUMBER CR94-1523


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-1523 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/3/95); 657 So. 2d 178; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1091



May 3, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Fred R. Godwin, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 1604-94.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which denied defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence. Upon a plea of guilty to manslaughter, the trial court had sentenced defendant to 20 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was standing in the street in front of his house with some friends. The victim drove by, stopped, and asked about an individual and for money. Defendant stated that the victim appeared angry and seemed to be reaching for a weapon. Defendant took out his gun and shot the victim. Defendant entered a plea of guilty to manslaughter and was sentenced to 20 years at hard labor. The trial court denied his motion for reconsideration of sentence. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that the trial court stated the factual basis for defendant's sentence and the factors that were weighed in fashioning the sentence and that these factors were supported by the record. The court found that defendant's crime was a violent and serious offense and his victim's actions did not justify homicide. The court noted that by pleading guilty to manslaughter, rather than going to trial on the second degree murder charge, defendant escaped a potential sentence of mandatory life imprisonment. The court found that the sentence imposed was not grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime, even though this was defendant's first conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was affirmed. The judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of manslaughter and sentencing him to 20 years at hard labor was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: A relative of defendants was being prosecuted for second-degree murder. Defendants allegedly had a friend contact a jury member and request help in the trial of the relative. One of the defendants contacted a relative of another juror, who declined to help and contacted the district attorney. The two defendants were indicted on one count and two counts of jury tampering, respectively. The trial court, by jury verdict, found both defendants guilty of attempted jury tampering. The trial court denied their motions for a new trial and for arrest of judgment. Defendants contended that the verdict was not responsive to the indictment, as the crime of "attempted jury tampering" did not exist. The court held that defendants' assignment of error had merit and accordingly it was required to reverse defendants' convictions and sentences and discharge them.

State v. Townley

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which, by jury verdict, convicted him of simple escape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:110(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant escaped from the custody of the State's department of corrections while serving sentences imposed for previous convictions. The trial court, by jury verdict, convicted defendant of simple escape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:110(A)(1). Thereafter, defendant was adjudicated an habitual offender and sentenced to serve five years at hard labor with the sentence to run consecutive to any prior sentence imposed. Defendant appealed the sentence. Prior to the commission of the simple escape, defendant had been convicted of four felonies. The court held that the minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law would be two and one-half years to run consecutive to any other sentence. The court noted that the trial court sentenced defendant to five years at hard labor to run consecutive to any other sentence, or two and one-half years longer than the recommended sentence under the Guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for simple escape and his sentencing under the Habitual Offender Law. The court remanded the case with instructions to provide defendant with notice pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8.

Duplechain v. St. Landry Parish Sch. Bd.


NUMBER 95-16


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-16 (La.App. 3 Cir. 5/3/95); 657 So. 2d 110; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1110



May 3, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Alonzo Harris, Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 92-C-4474-C.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board appealed an order of the 27th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff principal's motion for summary judgment in his suit alleging breach of contract and wrongful demotion.


OVERVIEW: The principal was serving under a two-year contract commencing in 1990. In 1992, the superintendent recommended that the principal's contract be renewed but that a formal reprimand be placed in his personnel file regarding an incident involving grade changing. However, the school board voted not to renew the principal's contract and notified the principal of their decision by letter. The trial court ruled that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:444(B)(c)(iii) and (iv), which became effective in 1991, was applicable to the case. The court affirmed on appeal, holding that the legislature expressly provided for the statute's retroactive application. The statute required that the principal be informed of the written charges and given a fair hearing before the board after reasonable notice. The court found that there were no written charges and no written notice to the principal of any hearing on any charges. The board did not comply with the mandates of the statute and, therefore, there were no issues of material fact that would preclude summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the principal's motion for summary judgment.

State v. Dominick

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which convicted him as a multiple offender as charged by the State under the provisions of the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and sentenced him to serve 20 years at hard labor. The underlying crime was the theft of property valued between $ 100 and $ 500.


OVERVIEW: The multiple bill proceeding was conducted the day after defendant was sentenced to serve two years for the crime of theft. Because defendant was incarcerated pre-trial, his parole release date for the theft was less than two months later. The court found that there was no delay attributable to the State or to the trial court relative to the filing of the multiple bill, the adjudication, or the sentencing. Further, defendant knew the State intended to multiple bill him, so he could not have reasonably expected that he would be released on the charge without the imposition of an enhanced penalty. The court also found that the trial judge had not abused his discretion by refusing to charge the theft trial jury on the multiple offender sentence because the State had not yet proved the allegations for multiple offender sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that sentenced defendant under the habitual offender law.

Charrier v. Charrier


94-CA-921


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-921 (La.App. 5 Cir. 4/12/95); 653 So. 2d 1356; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1011



April 12, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied May 17, 1995. Released for Publication May 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 434-692. HONORABLE ALAN J. GREEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which denied his claim for a portion of his ex-wife's pension plan beyond the date that the parties to the marriage reestablished a community property regime upon reconciliation in 1978.


OVERVIEW: A couple separated in 1978 and partitioned the community with the exception of the wife's pension plan. The couple later reconciled but separated again in 1992. After a couple divorced in 1993, they entered into a consent judgment of partition of the community property. However, they disagreed as to the nature of the ex-wife's pension plan following the 1978 reconciliation and before the final divorce decree. The trial judge determined that the marital community property regime was not reestablished at the time of the 1978 reconciliation and denied the ex-husband's claim for a portion of his ex-wife's pension plan beyond 1978. On appeal, the ex-husband argued that, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:384, the community was reestablished in 1978. The appellate court agreed because it found that the legislature clearly intended § 9:384 to have retroactive application. The court reversed the judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the ex-husband recognizing his entitlement to a portion of the pension plan through 1992.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the ex-husband recognizing his entitlement to a portion of his ex-wife's pension plan accrued between the years 1978 and 1992.

 

735 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Use v. Use


NUMBER 94 CA 0972


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0972 (La.App. 1 Cir. 4/7/95); 654 So. 2d 1355; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 998



April 7, 1995, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended on Grant of Rehearing June 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1715. Rehearing Denied June 8, 1995. Released for Publication June 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 32nd Judicial District Court in and for Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 99268, 99474, 99741, and 101592. Honorable Edward J. Gaidry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant oil company appealed an order from the 32nd Judicial District Court in and for Terrebonne Parish (Louisiana), finding that the oil company was negligent for the injuries sustained by plaintiff victims when they boat sank.


OVERVIEW: The victims' boat sank when it struck the piling of an abandoned oil well. The oil well was owned by the oil company. The oil company challenged the finding of negligence. One of the victims's challenged the trial court's failure to award him medical expenses for surgery. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and amended the case. The court held that under the general maritime law, a party's negligence was actionable only if it was a legal cause of victim's injuries. Legal cause required that the negligence be a substantial factor in the injury. The oil company was negligent in leaving the pilings and well casing protruding out of the water. The pilings constituted an obstacle to navigation and were a substantial factor in causing the victims' accident. If the oil company had cut the casing and removed or cut the pilings to the mud line, or, at a minimum, marked the pilings with reflectors, the accident could have been avoided. Next, the court held that an injured victim could not be faulted for accepting a course of treatment offered by his orthopedic surgeon, which was offered as a means of reducing his pain. There was no evidence that the injured victim acted in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and amended the judgment.

State v. Beason


No. 26,725-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,725 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/07/95); 653 So. 2d 1274; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 824



April 7, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1995. Released for Publication May 4, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 29,367, Criminal Docket. Honorable Robert Y. Butler, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana, which convicted them of negligent homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendants used their cars to pursue another driver who sped away, failed to negotiate a curve, and ran off the road. Defendants were convicted of the negligent homicide of the passenger in the driver's car. The court held that the verdict was supported by sufficient evidence that defendants grossly deviated from the standard of care when they chased another driver in a threatening manner and at a high rate of speed, which chase was a contributing factor to the death. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting rehabilitative and rebuttal evidence, a color photograph of the victim's body, evidence to which no objection was made, and testimony of excited utterances made by the driver while he was still under the stress of the accident. The admission of hearsay testimony that unnamed witnesses at the scene said they did not hear screeching tires was harmless error because it was corroborated by other witnesses. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing charges that were not wholly correct or were included in the general instruction or in imposing a three-year hard labor sentence for the defendant who had prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' sentences and convictions.

 

737 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Mellion v. City of Plaquemine


No. CA 94 1290


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-1290 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/07/95); 654 So. 2d 729; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 973



April 7, 1995, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 25, 1995. Released for Publication June 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 44,217. Honorable Jack T. Marionneaux, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; PERMANENT INJUNCTION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the order form the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana, ordering the city to issue a liquor permit to plaintiff applicant in violation of city zoning ordinances. The city filed a reconventional demand requesting an injunction prohibiting issuance of the license.


OVERVIEW: The city issued a temporary permit to the applicants so that they could obtain a zoning variance that would enable them to operate a nightclub in an area zoned for packaged liquor sales only. After the city failed to render a decision within 35 days of the request under La. Rev. Stat. Ann § 26:87, the applicants were granted an injunction ordering the city to issue a formal permit. On review, the city argued that the district court could not compel the city to violate its own zoning ordinances under § 26:87. The applicants contended that the zoning ordinance denied them due process of law and that the city was estopped from denial under § 26:87. The court rejected both arguments and reversed the judgment. The court held that the only remedy available under § 26:87 was to compel the city to rule on the application for a permit, and the district court had no authority to compel the city to violate its own laws. The court found that no due process violation had occurred because other nightclubs had been grandfathered in after the ordinance was passed. The court found that the city was entitled to an injunction to enforce its zoning law prohibiting the operation of the nightclub.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and granted an injunction in favor of the city on its reconventional demand.

Williams v. Board of Trustees for the Employees' Retirement Sys.


NUMBER 94 CA 1024


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-1024 (La.App. 1 Cir. 4/7/94); 653 So. 2d 1337; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 994



April 7, 1995, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication April 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 392,730. Honorable William H. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant sought review of an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted defendant's, the Board of Trustees for the Employees' Retirement System, peremptory exceptions of no cause and no right of action in the claimant's action seeking disability retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: The claimant, a parish attorney, was convicted of three felonies and applied for disability retirement benefits before retiring. The Board of Trustees for the Employees' Retirement System denied him benefits. The trial court dismissed his suit. The claimant appealed and the court affirmed. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1411 provided that the conviction for a felony of a public officer would suspend him from office without compensation. The claimant argued that he was not a public officer. An individual was a public officer if he acted as an agent of the state and the office occupied involved a large degree of independence in which the individual was not under the direct supervision of an employer. The claimant was a public officer because his office enjoyed a large degree of independence and was not subject to his employer's control. The claimant asserted that § 42:1411 was not applicable because his retirement benefits were not an emolument of his office. The court rejected his claim that the Board dispossessed him of a vested right. The disability retirement benefits were distinguishable from the mandatory contributions he made into the retirement system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted the Board of Trustees for the Employees' Retirement System's peremptory exceptions of no cause and no right of action in the claimant's action seeking disability retirement benefits.

Taylor v. City of Shreveport

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband of the deceased and her 11 children, sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which denied their claims against appellees, the city of Shreveport, the Shreveport Police Chief, and individual police officers, individually, and in their respective official capacities in a wrongful death action. Appellees pled the defense of immunity and qualified immunity.


OVERVIEW: On the day of the incident, a police officer saw an apparent drug transaction. He chased one of the individuals into the deceased's home. The deceased was at home with part of her children when the police broke in. The police arrested the individual and found drugs in the house. Fletcher v. Fletcher


NUMBER 94-1426


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-1426 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/05/95); 653 So. 2d 119; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 848



April 5, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication May 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial Court for the Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, the Honorable B. Dexter Ryland, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 26,461.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child of testator and will opponent, challenged a judgment of the Ninth Judicial Court for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) finding that the bedridden testator had the capacity to make a will in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2442(C), contending that the trial court erred in finding that the testator could read, and that the will was properly witnessed and executed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his death, the decedent executed a statutory will. He had previously been disabled and the right side of his body was paralyzed. The will was drafted by his attorney in accordance with § 9:2442(C), and disinherited the decedent's child, the will opponent. The opponent filed a challenge to the probation of the will, contending that after the stroke, his father could not read, and that the testamentary formalities were not met by the decedent's signature on each page, as opposed to his mark. The court dispensed with the formality challenge, holding that the purpose of the statute was that the testator at least affix a mark to each page because he was physically unable to read, and the signature on each page satisfied the general requirement. The main issue was whether sufficient evidence showed that the decedent could read after his stroke. Testimony included that of his friends and relatives that he could read, and the court affirmed the trial court's finding that the decedent met the capacity requirement. The court held that the findings of capacity and formality were sufficiently supported and affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Magee v. Landrieu


No. 95 CA 0437, No. 95 CA 0438, No. 95 CW 0474,


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0437 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/17/95); 653 So. 2d 62; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 1021



March 17, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication April 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Trial Court Nos. 410,054 and 408,800 and on transfer from the Louisiana Supreme Court, on Application of Supervisory and/or Remedial Writs to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Honorable William H. Brown, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought review of an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which, in the state's action for declaratory judgment, upheld rulings that ceilings in favor of the state on non-economic damages and pre-judgment interest limitations were unconstitutional, and found that all payments made by the state on judgments must be imputed first to legal interest and then to principal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that Rick v. State, Department of Transportation and Development, 630 So. 2d 1271 (La. 1994) applied to all judgments that had not been satisfied at the time Rick had been rendered, that Chamberlain v. State, Department of Transportation and Development, 624 So. 2d 874 (La. 1993) applied to respondent judgment creditor's general damage award, and that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1866 required that all payments made by the state on judgments must be imputed first to legal interest and then to the principal. In light of the substantial injustices that would result from a retroactive application, the court concluded that Chamberlain and Rick should not be applied retroactively, but prospectively only. The court applied the holdings of Chamberlain and Rick to those cases that were still "pending appeal" at the time the judgments were rendered and rejected the argument that a judgment was "pending" until satisfied by payment in full. The court held that the supreme court's holdings in Chamberlain and Rick would be applied to those cases in which a final judgment had not yet been obtained on the dates the decisions were rendered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court to the extent it applied the holding in Rick v. State, 630 So. 2d 1271 (La. 1994), to all judgments that had not been satisfied at the time of the rendition of Rick.

State ex rel. Department of Social Servs. v. Ashy


No. 94 CA 0903


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-0903 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/03/95); 653 So. 2d 20; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 682



March 3, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied May 2, 1995. Released for Publication May 2, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 86,158. Honorable Edward A. de la Houssaye, III, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant putative father appealed the judgment of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary, Louisiana which in an paternity action held in favor of Plaintiff State and intervenor mother and awarded child support and reimbursement to the State for Aid For Dependent Children (AFDC) benefits paid the mother.


OVERVIEW: In a paternity action the trial judge entered judgment establishing paternity and ordered the father to pay child support and to reimburse the State for AFDC benefits which had been paid to the mother. The father appealed contending inter alia that the statutory scheme of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:397 et seq., as applied, resulted in a denial of due process, because it required the filing of the expert reports, which contain statistical opinions unequivocally prejudicial to the father, into the record without an adequate opportunity for the father to test the validity of the expert opinions rendered. The court found that the father was provided with an opportunity at trial to refute the test result, to question the expert's opinions and qualifications, and to explore the testing methodology used. The father's entire defense relied on the correctness of the calculations made by one of the expert witnesses as to the probable date conception occurred; and because the date of conception was not conclusively established, the court could not find that the trial judge was clearly wrong in his finding that the father had access to the mother at or about the probable time of conception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial in a paternity action which found in favor of the State and the mother against the putative father.

State v. Nicholas


94 KW 1096


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-1096 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/03/95); 652 So. 2d 666; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 686



March 3, 1995, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 238,885), PARISH OF TERREBONNE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE EDWARD J. GAIDRY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; MOTION TO SUPPRESS DENIED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed, by writ of certiorari, from an order of the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana) granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence on the grounds that the search was illegal because the warrant did not authorize a nighttime search as required by La. Crim. Code Ann. art. 163.


OVERVIEW: The agents secured a search warrant authorizing a search of the residence where defendant and his grandparents lived. They arrived before dark to execute the warrant. They called the residence and were told by an elderly woman that defendant was not at home. The agents sent up surveillance and after waiting for several hours decided to execute the warrant before the grandparents turned off the lights. At about 9:00 p.m. they knocked on the door, showed the grandmother the warrant, and asked to wait inside for defendant. Defendant arrived home at 9:30, was shown the warrant and advised of his rights, and agreed to go with one of the agents to his bedroom to get the marijuana. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence on the grounds that the warrant was executed at nighttime in violation of art. 163. On appeal by writ of certiorari, the court denied the motion to suppress. The court held that although the warrant was executed at nighttime without the authorization required by art. 163, the search was not unconstitutional. The exclusionary rule did not apply and suppression was not required because the search was not unreasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's writ of certiorari, denied defendant's motion to suppress, and remanded for further proceedings.

PETERSON v. B E & K INC.


No. 94 CA 0005


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0005 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/03/95); 652 So. 2d 617; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 652



March 3, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 9014026 F. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the decision of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which sustained the statutory employer defense and granted summary judgment to defendants, two members of a joint venture and one of its workers, in the employee's tort suit for damages.


OVERVIEW: The two employers entered into a joint venture for a boiler construction project. The employee, who worked for one of the subsidiaries of one of the employers, was injured while attempting to install a boiler door. The employee filed suit in tort against the two employers and the worker responsible for an allegedly defective weld. The defendants countered that the employee's exclusive remedy was workers compensation because the joint venturers were statutory employers. The trial court sustained the defense and granted summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that it was clear that, at the time of his injuries, the employee was performing work in furtherance of the joint venture, namely the installation of the door to the boiler, which was part of the boiler construction project, and that this fact created a statutory employment relationship for purposes of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1032.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had entered summary judgment for the defendants on the employee's claim in tort for injuries sustained while working on a boiler for the joint venture.

 

746 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


First Advantage Ins. v. Green


No. 94 CA 0813


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0813 (La.App. 1 Cir. 3/3/95); 652 So. 2d 562; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 557



March 3, 1995, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 365,352. Honorable Paul B. Landry, Jr., Judge Pro Tempore Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners national bank and insurance subsidiary appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, that affirmed the revocation by respondent state commissioner of insurance of petitioner insurance subsidiary's license to act as a general insurance agent.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner national bank organized petitioner insurance subsidiary for the purpose of selling insurance. Respondent state commissioner of insurance revoked petitioner's license to sell insurance pursuant to state law making it illegal for a bank or its subsidiary to sell any insurance except credit life insurance. The court affirmed the revocation of petitioner's license. The court held that the state law was not preempted by a federal law, 12 U.S.C.S. § 92, that authorized national banks in small towns to sell insurance. The court held that while the two statutes were facially conflicting, the McCarran-Ferguson Act (McCarran Act), 15 U.S.C.S. § 1012(b), saved the state law from preemption. Under the McCarran Act, the court held that state laws enacted for the purpose of regulating insurance were not subject to preemption unless the conflicting federal law clearly stated that it regulated insurance or was intended to preempt state law. Under this analysis, the court concluded that the federal statute that merely granted power for national banks to sell insurance did not entail regulation of that activity, and thus was subject to "reverse preemption" by the state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for respondent state commissioner of insurance revoking petitioners' license to sell insurance because state laws prohibited petitioners' sales of insurance other than credit insurance, and under McCarran-Ferguson Act analysis, federal statute granting national banks authority to sell insurance was not intended to regulate insurance sales and did not preempt state laws.

State v. Jynes


No. 94-KA-745


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-745 (La.App. 5 Cir. 3/1/95); 652 So. 2d 91; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 457



March 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 90-0443. HONORABLE MARY ANN VIAL LEMMON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the District Court for the Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana) of the charge of attempted second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:30.1, and of the charge of attempted manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction in the trial court of attempted second degree murder and attempted manslaughter, and asserted that the jury was improperly charged as to the crime of attempted manslaughter. Defendant asserted that the jury charge contained a statement that attempted manslaughter was committed without any intent to cause death or great bodily harm. Defendant asserted that the instruction was prejudicial error because the crime of attempted manslaughter was a specific intent crime. The court affirmed and found that in the conference regarding the proposed jury charges, the trial court stated that it would define attempt first, and then define attempted manslaughter. The court found that defendant's counsel agreed with the trial court's intended charges, but when the charge was delivered to the jury, it had changed to include the objected to statement. Upon request by the jury, the trial court repeated the same definition of attempted manslaughter. The court noted that the verdict would not be set aside absent proof that the jury charge was prejudicial, and held that the guilty verdict was unattributable to the erroneous jury charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in the trial court of the charges of attempted second degree murder and attempted manslaughter.

Pasqua v. St. Landry Parish Police Jury


No. 94-01196


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-1196 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/01/95); 651 So. 2d 430; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 495



March 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 7, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, Honorable Joseph A. LaHaye, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a municipal association executive director and mayors as representatives of the class of individuals residing in the incorporated municipalities in the parish who paid the gasoline sales tax imposed by defendant State of Louisiana, challenged the grant by the 27th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, Louisiana, of an exception of no cause of action in favor of both the State and defendant parish police jury.


OVERVIEW: The class alleged that the parish police jury arbitrarily denied the incorporated municipalities the right to share in the Parish Transportation Fund Act revenues. That the Parish Transportation Fund Act treated incorporated municipalities in a different manner than it treated the unincorporated areas was not a constitutional violation, and did not violate the class's equal rights, because the distinction was not based on a "suspect classification" such as race or religion. The legislation was merely a rational and appropriate method for providing funds to the citizens of the parish through its parish government, for the maintenance and construction of parish roads and if desired, the same expenditure on the roads located in incorporated municipalities. The court did, however, find that the class action stated a cause of action against the parish police jury. Based on the well-pleaded allegations of fact, a claim was established for an abuse of discretion granted under the Parish Transportation Fund Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:755(A), and for a possible violation of its administrative procedures, by the parish police jury in its method of appropriation of the fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the exception of no cause of action on behalf of the State of Louisiana, but reversed the judgment granting the exception of no cause of action on behalf of the St. Landry Parish Police Jury, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Hodges

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Wilford D. Carter, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), refused to sentence the defender to the mandatory minimum sentence set out in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and the sentencing guidelines and found the mandatory minimum to be constitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of 3 counts of cocaine distribution and found to be a second felony offender. The trial court sentenced her to 9 concurrent years of hard labor instead of the mandatory minimum of 12 to 60 years under the sentencing guidelines and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, concluding that the mandatory minimums were constitutionally excessive. The State appealed arguing that the trial court erred in the sentencing and should have articulated its reasons for deviating from the mandated sentence. On review the court noted if a sentence meted out under § 15:529.1 made no measurable contribution to the acceptable goals of punishment, or was grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime, it was the duty of the sentencing judge to reduce the sentence to one that would not be constitutionally excessive. Finding that the trial court wrote several pages on the reason for his sentence, the court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's reduced sentence and remanded the case with instructions to allow the defendant credit for time served.

State v. Abbott


No. 94-KA-1046


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1046 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/23/95); 650 So. 2d 1223; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 380



February 23, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 1995.
As Corrected March 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 299-714, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which convicted defendant of three counts of armed robbery and sentenced him as a second felony offender to 17 1/2 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of armed robbery after he robbed the players at a dice game of their cash and jewelry. Defendant was sentenced as a second felony offender to 17 1/2 years at hard labor. The State appealed and the court affirmed. The State argued that the trial court erred in failing to sentence defendant to the statutory minimum of 33 years mandated by the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The court held that the sentencing court could find that the statutorily mandated minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law was unconstitutionally excessive and impose a lesser sentence. The trial judge had to find that the punishment mandated by § 15:529.1 made no measurable contribution to acceptable goals of punishment or that it amounted to nothing more than the purposeful imposition of pain and suffering. The court concluded that the trial court justified its departure from the mandatory minimum sentence by acknowledging that defendant's youth, the facts of the case, and the fact that his two prior convictions were for shoplifting did not justify the statutorily mandated minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that convicted and sentenced defendant.

 

752 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Board of Comm'rs of the N. Lafourche Conservation Levee & Drainage Dist. v. Board of Comm'rs of the Lafourche Basin Levee Dist.


No. 94-CA-683


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-683 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/15/95); 652 So. 2d 19; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 351



February 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JAMES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 22,324. HONORABLE JOHN L. PEYTAVIN, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Board of Commissioners of the Lafourche Basin Levee District appealed from the mandamus judgment of the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of St. James, State of Louisiana, which ordered it to pay $ 200,000 to plaintiff Board of Commissioners of the North Lafourche Conservation Levee and Drainage District. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:333, which required the sharing of these funds.


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:333 created two new levee districts, so that there were a total of four. Defendant and a preexisting second levee district were required to share funds with the newly created plaintiff and a fourth district. The purpose of § 38:333 was to partially relieve defendant and the second levee district of the responsibility for providing certain services to areas where the four districts overlapped. Defendant refused to transfer funds to plaintiff, arguing that § 38:333 arbitrarily subjected persons within the overlap to oppressive double taxation and that it could impair defendant's contractual obligations. Although there was no specific authority to overlap districts, there was no express provision limiting the legislature, which did have express authority to consolidate, divide, reorganize, or create new levee districts under La. Const. art. III, § 13. The legislature was aware of the overlap when it enacted § 38:333. The language and purpose were clear. There was no proof of any unfair taxation, possible contract disturbance, or endangerment of bonded indebtedness. Defendant did not prove that the statute was unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court with the costs of the appeal taxed to defendant.

Natchitoches Parish Hosp. Serv. Dist. v. Rachal


No. 94-995


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-995 (La.App. 3 Cir. 2/1/95); 649 So. 2d 1152; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 180



February 1, 1995, Decided

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insured appealed a decision of the 10th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Natchitoches (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff insurer in the insurer's action for a declaratory judgment that it was not liable on the insured's claim for coverage for injuries sustained in an accident.


OVERVIEW: The insured sustained injuries as a result of an accident involving a train which struck a tractor trailer rig driven by the insured. The insured, as the spouse of an employee of a hospital, filed insurance claims for coverage under the hospital's self-funded health insurance plan for the medical expenses he incurred from his injuries. The insurer hospital declined coverage on the basis that the insured was acting within the course and scope of his employment at the time of the accident and thus his claim was subject to an exclusion contained in the policy, which excluded from coverage medical expenses resulting from injury arising out of or in the course of employment. The trial court granted the insurer's motion for summary judgment, which was unopposed, and later denied a motion for a new hearing after the insured claimed that it had not received notice of the hearing on the motion for summary judgment. In affirming the trial court's decision, the court held that the insured's evidence to support its assertion that the insurer was acting within the course of his employment at the time of the accident was sufficient to meet its burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted summary judgment to the insurer in the insurer's action for a declaratory judgment that it was not liable on the insured's claim for coverage for injuries sustained in an accident.

State v. Merrill


No. 94-KA-0716


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0716 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/31/95); 650 So. 2d 793; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 98



January 31, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM 34th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, ST. BERNARD PARISH. NO. 157-262, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE MELVYN J. PEREZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE REVERSED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence of 20 years at hard labor imposed by the 34th Judicial District Court, St. Bernard Parish (Louisiana) for his conviction of distribution of cocaine a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for the distribution of cocaine. Defendant argued inter alia, that his sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and that the trial court improperly departed from the sentencing guidelines. The court reversed and vacated the sentence, finding that sentences as harsh as the one the defendant received had generally been found to be excessive when imposed on first offenders who had not been found to be large-scale drug dealers. The court found that after considering defendant's prior conviction, the maximum range recommended by the sentencing guidelines was 84 months. Defendant's sentence of 240 months was thus nearly 3 times the recommended maximum sentence. Further the court concluded that the notice contained in the record and the predicate for admission presented by the State were sufficient to allow the State to admit the defendant's inculpatory statement into evidence, and the evidence sufficiently supported the conviction for distribution of cocaine.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of distribution of cocaine was affirmed. However, the court reversed and vacated the sentence imposed by the trial court, and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.
