Simmons v. Simmons


No. 26,414-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,414 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/25/95); 649 So. 2d 799; 1995 La. App. LEXIS 57



January 25, 1995, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 93-2632. Honorable Robert W. Kostelka, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which designated plaintiff, her estranged husband, as the primary domiciliary parent of their two minor children. The wife complained that the district court refused to apply the adverse presumption, enunciated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:364(A), concerning any parent with a history of perpetrating family violence.


OVERVIEW: The wife alleged that the district court erroneously failed to apply the presumption enunciated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:364(A) and, accordingly, erroneously designated her estranged husband as the primary domiciliary parent of their children. Nothing indicated that the husband ever directed any anger toward the children. Thus, after viewing the totality of circumstances in light of the children's best interest, the fact-trier found only occasional incidents of violence that might have been provoked by the wife's adultery, and that did not rise to the level of a "history of perpetrating family violence." Accordingly, the court held that there was no manifest error in the refusal to apply the presumption. The evidence of the husband's behavior did not warrant the harsh remedy discussed. The court found that although both parties were generally shown to be good and loving parents, the totality of the circumstances favored the husband. He clearly established a more secure environment for the children. In contrast, the wife's present situation and relevant past did not present a stable situation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed at the wife's costs.

MRT Exploration Co. v. McNamara


NUMBER 94 CA 0063 CONSOLIDATED WITH NUMBER 94 CA 0064


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-0063 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/29/94); 648 So. 2d 1108; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3611



December 29, 1994, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 3, 1995. Released for Publication February 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From The 19th Judicial District Court. In And For The Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Suite Numbers 262,928 and 323,597. Honorable William Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which rendered judgment for defendant, the Department of Revenue and Taxation, on its reconventional demand and dismissed the taxpayers' claims to recover severance taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed an action against the department to recover severance taxes paid under protest. They claimed that the Louisiana Severance Tax Statutes were unconstitutional as applied to oil and gas production from a federal enclave. The department filed a reconventional demand for severance taxes. The trial court dismissed the taxpayers' action, granted the department's reconventional demand, and ruled that the statutes were valid and enforceable. On appeal, the court held that the La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:633 amendment rendered the severance tax an income tax within the meaning of the Buck Act, 4 U.S.C.S. § 106, therefore the department could impose the severance tax on the minerals severed from the federal enclave. The court concluded that the severance tax on natural gas and its equivalents remained a volume-based tax for the determination of the amount of tax due. The court ruled that the Louisiana Severance Tax, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 37:631-646, could be imposed because of the amendment to the Mineral Leasing Act for Acquired Lands, 30 U.S.C.S. § 357.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayers' claims against the department for recovery of severance taxes paid under protest.

State v. Duncan


No. 94-KA-1045


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice accosted the victim and a witness at a bus station. When the victim resisted, defendant put his gun to the victim's head and fired. The court further held that the state did not have to disclose to defendant the initial police investigative report, the witness' grand jury testimony, and her written statement because the information contained therein either did not come from the witness or was not contradictory to the witness' trial testimony.

State v. Hughes


No. 94-KA-1364


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1364 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/29/94); 648 So. 2d 490; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3585



December 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 363-813, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED. MOTION TO QUASH DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed the decision from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), quashing its bill of information charging defendant with molestation of a juvenile. Defendant filed a motion to quash based on expiration of the time limitation to prosecute. The court granted the motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information with molestation of a juvenile. Defendant filed a motion to quash based on expiration of the time limitation to prosecute. The trial court granted the motion and the prosecution appealed. The court held that the trial court erred by finding that the four-year prescriptive period under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 572 had run and that an exception provided in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 573 was not applicable. At the time the offense was allegedly committed, art. 573 did not provide an exception to the four-year time limitation for molestation of a juvenile, but that exception was added before the four-year limitation under art. 572 had expired. The court held that the right against prosecution had not vested because the time limitation had not run when the amendment became effective. Under art. 573 as amended the prosecution had to show that the victim was under 17 years at the time of the offense and did not become 17 years old more than 4 years before institution of prosecution.. The victim was clearly under 17 when the bill of information was filed and the bill was timely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, holding that defendant's motion to quash was denied and that the prosecution's bill of information charging defendant with molestation of a juvenile was filed timely.

Redwine v. State


No. 94 CA 0160


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0160 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/94); 649 So. 2d 61; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3647



December 22, 1994, Judgment rendered

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant department sought review of an order from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff class members that declared that the termination of the $ 50.00 per month salary supplement during the elective term ending December 31, 1990, was in violation of La. Const. art. 5, § 21 and art. 10, § 23.


OVERVIEW: The class members filed the instant class action suit for declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, and damages. The department contended that the trial court erred as a matter of law in ordering the department to pay $ 50.00 per month per class member. The court found that the Louisiana Constitution prohibited the reduction of the salary of justices of the peace and constables, including the $ 50.00 monthly pay supplement, during their terms of office. As such, the Department could not lawfully refuse to remit the $ 50.00 monthly pay supplement to the class members. The court determined that where all the class members' terms of office commenced prior to the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:2591 they were entitled to the salary supplement of $ 50.00 per month.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which found in favor of the class members.

Angelo v. Ales


94 CA 0320


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0320 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/22/94); 649 So. 2d 1042; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3660



December 22, 1994, RENDERED.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 383,790), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE WILLIAM H. BROWN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the judgment of the trial court is AFFIRMED. Costs are assessed against the plaintiff-appellant, Ms. Angelo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heir sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which sustained the dilatory exception of prematurity filed by defendant secretary of the Department of Natural Resources to the heir's suit seeking mandamus to require implementation of the provisions of 1985 La. Acts 245 for confirmation of title to certain swamp lands.


OVERVIEW: Following enactment of 1985 La. Acts 245 (Act 245) to restore titles for certain expropriated swamp lands, the heir filed a petition on behalf of a putative class of successors in interest for a declaratory judgment establishing the class members' title, and judgment was rendered. She then filed suit for mandamus to compel the secretary to implement the provisions of Act 245. On appeal of the judgment sustaining the secretary's exception of prematurity, the heir argued that the trial court erred in granting a collateral attack on the prior judgment and in applying La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1880 to proceedings under Act 245. In affirming, the court ruled that had the legislature wished to exempt declaratory judgment proceedings under Act 245 from the requirements for declaratory judgments under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1880, it could have done so by clearly stating such intention. The court held that art. 1880 required all affected persons to be made parties to a declaratory suit, that no adverse parties were named, served, confronted with any evidence, or given an opportunity to appear in the heir's proceeding, and that the judgment was, therefore, a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Lewandowski


No. 94-KA-0806


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0806 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/15/94); 648 So. 2d 46; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3302



December 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 349-571, SEC. M3. HONORABLE ANDREW SCIAMBRA, JUDGE. BARRY, J., CONCURS WITH REASONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which convicted defendants after they pled guilty to gambling in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:90.


OVERVIEW: Defendants pled guilty to gambling. Upon their conviction the State moved for disposition, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:901 of the property and monies seized from defendants when they were first arrested. Defendants filed motions to quash and for the return of the evidence. Following a hearing, the trial court denied their motions and granted the State's motion to dispose of the property. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the police obtained a search warrant and arrested defendants prior to the search and seizure. Defendants pled guilty to gambling without having moved to suppress the evidence seized and, consequently, without reserving any rights to contest the seizure. As a result they were not in a position to attack the seizure on the ground that the warrant was defective or that the search exceeded the limits of the warrant. Specifically, they were not in a position to attack the seizure of cash found in a safe at the address named in the warrant where the search was authorized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendants' motion to quash and for the return of evidence.

State v. Smith


No. 94-KA-0621


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0621 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/15/94); 647 So. 2d 1321; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3401



December 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 364-970, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION FOR MANSLAUGHTER AFFIRMED; SENTENCE FOR MANSLAUGHTER VACATED; CONVICTION AND SENTENCE FOR SECOND DEGREE FETICIDE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which entered a jury verdict convicting him of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31(A) and second degree feticide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.7 and sentenced him to 30 years at hard labor on the manslaughter conviction and 10 years at hard labor on the second degree feticide conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed the mother of his unborn child; he was charged with second degree murder and second degree feticide. On appeal from defendant's convictions of manslaughter and second degree feticide, the court vacated his conviction of second degree feticide on double jeopardy grounds. Applying the "same evidence" test, the court held that defendant's convictions of both offenses violated La. Const. of 1974, art. I, § 15 because the same evidence used to convict defendant of manslaughter was also used to convict him of second degree feticide. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for mistrial during opening statement when the prosecutor made a reference to a statement defendant gave to police; although the prosecutor violated La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 767, defendant did not show prejudice because he knew, prior to trial, that the State intended to use the statement and the prosecutor gave no details about the statement. Defense counsel's assistance was not constitutionally deficient; counsel's decisions not to give opening or closing arguments or to seek supervisory review of the denial of his motions were part of his trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for second degree feticide, affirmed his conviction for manslaughter, vacated his sentence for manslaughter, and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Houston


No. 94-KA-592


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-592 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/14/94); 648 So. 2d 948; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3541



December 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 93-3420, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted and sentenced her for theft.


OVERVIEW: In March of 1993, defendant cashed her Social Security check at a supermarket and then filed a claim with the Social Security Administration alleging that she had never received the check. After the check was returned to the store owner as "stolen," defendant was arrested. She was found guilty as charged with theft under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67. The court affirmed both the conviction and sentence, holding that the record showed that defendant was informed at her arraignment of her right to trial by jury. The court noted that her testimony later at trial evidenced that she was aware and alert, and able to make appropriate responses to counsel's questions. Finally, defendant had prior experience as an accused in a criminal prosecution. Under those circumstances, the court found that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived her right to a jury trial. The court concluded that because defendant failed to file the requisite motion, she was precluded from raising her argument of an illegal sentence on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for theft.

State v. Franklin


No. 94-KA-409


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-409 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/14/94); 648 So. 2d 962; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3544



December 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 92-4900, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE DOUGLAS A. ALLEN



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, and of his sentence, on his adjudication as a third offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, to 99 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. It held that a rational trier of fact could conclude, based on the testimony of two eye witnesses and a physician, that defendant did not prove by a preponderance of evidence that he was insane at the time of the offense. It held that where defense counsel called and thoroughly examined witnesses in support of the insanity claim, introduced physical evidence on defendant's behalf, and diligently cross-examined state's witnesses, defendant's complaints of his counsel's performance did not amount to ineffective assistance. The court further held that because defendant failed to file a motion for reconsideration of his sentence, he was precluded by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1 from claiming excessiveness on appeal. It also held that where the state produced sufficient evidence that both predicate offenses fell within the five year cleansing period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, the trial court did not err in finding that defendant was a third offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Henderson


No. 94-KA-286


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-286 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/14/94); 648 So. 2d 974; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3556



December 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 93-1560, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which sentenced him to 18 years hard labor upon his conviction of simple burglary, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.2. He claimed that the sentence was vindictive.


OVERVIEW: The state offered defendant six and one-half years if he pleaded guilty to simple burglary, but threatened to multiple bill him if he did not plead guilty. Defendant rejected the offer. After his conviction, the trial court sentenced defendant to 10 years; the state then proved defendant had a prior felony conviction and the trial court sentenced him to 8 more years under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1A(1). In vacating the sentence and remanding the matter, the court first held that there was nothing vindictive about defendant's sentence. The court held that the sentence was a result of the give-and-take of plea negations and was not a violation of due process. But the court found many errors patent, starting with the fact that the trial court had failed to vacate defendant's original sentence, rendering the habitual offender sentence a nullity. The court also noted that the trial court did not bother to find the number of prior felonies defendant had committed. The trial court also failed to give credit for time served and advise defendant of the prescriptive period for filing post-conviction motions.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing.

State v. Foster


No. 26,143-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,143 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/09/94); 647 So. 2d 1224; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3260



December 9, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 19, 1995. Released for Publication January 19, 1995.
Writ denied by State v. Foster, 657 So. 2d 1026, 1995 La. LEXIS 1813 (La., June 30, 1995)
Related proceeding at Foster v. State, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1401 (La.App. 2 Cir., July 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 56,072. Honorable Graydon K. Kitchens, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster (Louisiana), which found him guilty of kidnapping and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed a motel, and ordered the night manager to follow him to a highway, where the defendant eventually released the manager. Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction, and that he was insane at the time of the offense. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction, because after reviewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, a rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant committed an armed robbery by taking money from the hotel and committed kidnapping by forcibly taking the manager from the hotel. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, and denied the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Williams


No. CR94-736


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-736 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/7/94); 647 So. 2d 597; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3340



December 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Preston N. Aucoin, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed the sentence imposed by the 13th Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), following her conviction on five counts of forgery, arguing that the 20-year sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: The defendant entered a guilty plea on five counts of forgery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:72 and was sentenced to four years at hard labor on each count with the sentences to run consecutively. After the defendant's motion for reconsideration of sentence was denied, the defendant appealed, arguing that the sentence was impermissibly excessive. In affirming, the court concluded that the imposition of consecutive sentences totaling twenty years was not so excessive as to require a reversal. The maximum penalty that could be imposed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:72 for each count was a fine of not more than $ 5,000 or imprisonment for not more than ten years or both. The defendant was sentenced to less than one-half the maximum on each count. The Louisiana Felony Sentencing Guidelines recommended a sentence from 60 to 72 months for concurrent sentences and from 180 to 192 months for consecutive sentences. The defendant was sentenced to 48 months, or four years, above the guideline recommendation. The sentence was not so grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crimes and the defendant's criminal history so as to shock the court's sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment imposing sentence was affirmed.

 

772 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Strata v. Williams


No. 94-CA-1150


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1150 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/30/94); 646 So. 2d 522; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3112



November 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 93-20577, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE RONALD J. SHOLES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Assessor for the Third District of New Orleans disputed a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division M (Louisiana), which issued a writ of mandamus requiring him to grant appellees, sellers and purchasers, a homestead exemption on a bond for deed contract. In his answer to appellees' petition for mandamus the Assessor sought a declaratory judgment that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2948 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the purpose of § 9:2948 was to place bond for deed purchasers, with respect to the homestead exemption, in a position equal to that of purchasers who could pay cash or qualify for mortgages to finance home acquisitions. On appeal, the court noted that neither the parties nor the trial court considered the possible application of La. Const. of 1974, art. 7, § 15 to the issue. Inter alia, art. 7, § 15 denied the legislature the power to extinguish any obligation of an individual to the state. An individual's obligation to pay ad valorem taxes arose directly from art. 7, § 15, as contemplated by La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1751. Therefore, art. 7, § 15 created an obligation to pay ad valorem taxes to the state. That obligation rested upon the purchasers, because they had assumed the obligation in the bond for deed contract. The court held that, because § 9:2948 extinguished an obligation owed by individuals, § 9:2948 was unconstitutional. Even if the purchasers could be characterized as residential lessees under La. Const. art. 7, § 18, the result was the same, because it was the extinguishment of the obligation of the sellers that was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment granting the writ of mandamus and rendered declaratory judgment finding the statute unconstitutional.

State v. Melbert


No. CR-140


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


140 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/30/94); 649 So. 2d 740; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3128



November 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ALLEN, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. JOHN P. NAVARRE, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number: CR-1878-92.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION and SENTENCE VACATED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of possession with the intent to distribute a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: A deputy received a tip from a reliable confidential informant that defendant trafficked in cocaine and possessed a large amount of it at his residence. The deputy approached the owner of the home where defendant resided. The owner agreed to the search and signed a form that gave her permission. The home was searched. During the search of defendant's bedroom a bag containing crack cocaine was found in one of his brown boots next to his bed. The deputy also found several stolen watches and additional narcotics and cash stuffed in socks in a dresser drawer. Defendant lived with the residence owners as a guest. He did not rent or lease the room in which he lived. As a result of the search he was convicted of possession with the intent to distribute a controlled substance. On appeal defendant alleged that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress evidence seized from an invalid consensual search. On appeal the court held that because there was no probable cause to search the boot based on the information provided by the confidential informant that the evidence seized from the boot was not admissible under the inevitable discovery doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the decision, which convicted defendant of possession with the intent to distribute a controlled substance.

State v. Boros


No. 94-KA-453, 94-KA-454


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-453 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/29/94); 646 So. 2d 1183; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3229



November 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO. 93-68 AND 93-69, DIVISION "K", HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of two counts of molestation of a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, and sentenced him to seven years at hard labor on each count based upon his guilty plea. Defendant was ordered to receive treatment for sexual deviance while incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of molestation of a juvenile under § 14:81.2 and was sentenced to seven years at hard labor on each count, to be served consecutively. Defendant filed an amended and supplemental motion to reconsider sentence and a motion to withdraw guilty plea, which were denied by the trial court. On appeal, the court held that defendant was on notice that he was charged under § 14:81.2(C) by his counsel and the trial court. Defendant testified that his counsel explained to him his rights to trial by jury, to confront his accusers, and against self-incrimination and that he understood that by pleading guilty, he would give up those rights. Therefore, the court ruled that defendant entered his guilty pleas intelligently and voluntarily with full knowledge of his rights and of the crimes with which he was charged. The court ruled that defendant's sentences were within the statutory range and were below the sentencing cap.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for molestation of a juvenile.

Manuel v. Louisiana Sheriff's Risk Management Fund


93 CA 2177


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93 2177 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/18/94); 647 So. 2d 363; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3180



November 18, 1994, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 19, 1995. Released for Publication January 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 41,594. Honorable Jact T. Marionneaux Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for penalties and damages pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(A)(2) following an automobile accident, plaintiff driver appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana, which maintained an exception of no cause of action raised by defendant, an excess liability insurer, after the insurer failed to pay a settlement within 30 days after an agreement had been reduced to writing.


OVERVIEW: After a sheriff's deputy collided with his automobile, the driver filed suit against several defendants, including the sheriff, his primary and excess liability insurers, the sheriff's risk management fund, and the fund's excess insurers. The driver settled with all defendants but the excess insurers, with whom he had agreed upon a settlement. The trial court ruled that § 22:1220 was a substantive law and its application would be retroactive. The effective date of § 22:1220 was subsequent to the date of the accident and issuance of the contract. However, the it was effective before the settlement was reduced to writing and the insurers' subsequent delay in payment. Prior to the enactment of § 22:1220, an insurer had no duty to a third party claimant. The court held that, although § 22:1220 created new rights, duties, and liabilities regarding the insurer, insured, and non-insured claimant, its application to actions which occurred after its effective date was prospective, not retroactive, regardless of whether the policy and ensuing accident pre-existed the effective date. The delay in payment occurred after the effective date of § 22:1220; therefore § 22:1220 was applicable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court maintaining the insurer's peremptory exception and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Brown


No. 93-KA-2305


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-2305 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/17/94); 645 So. 2d 1282; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3059



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 362-965, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, No. 362-965, Section "E," (Louisiana), which suspended her sentence of five years at hard labor for negligent homicide under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32 and placed her on five years' active probation with the special conditions that she pay a probation fee, serve 18 months in prison, perform community service, and submit to counseling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the negligent homicide of her roommate. Defendant was given a suspended sentence of five years at hard labor and placed on five years' active probation, without good time or parole, with the special conditions that she pay a probation fee, serve 18 months in prison, perform community service, and submit to counseling. The court vacated the illegal sentence because it exposed defendant exposed to imprisonment of six and one-half years, which exceeded the five-year maximum under § 14:32 and exceeded the five-year probationary period permitted by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893(A). The court remanded the matter so that the trial court could specify that, in the event of revocation of probation, defendant's time spent in jail as a condition of probation, together with the imprisonment imposed, would not exceed the maximum sentence or probationary period. The court held that the trial court could not deny good time or parole eligibility on resentencing and that its failure to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.4(C) by stating that it considered and decided to deviate from the sentencing guidelines was an additional reason for remand.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing.

State v. Smith


No. CR94-388


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-388 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/09/94); 645 So. 2d 817; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3072



November 9, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Wilford D. Carter, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: VERDICT REVERSED; CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED AND SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of attempted aggravated crime against nature, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:89.1(A)(6) and 14:27(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered his son's room, lay on the son's bed, and asked the son to sit on his chest so that he could perform oral sex on the son. The court held that the evidence was insufficient to convict defendant of an attempted aggravated crime against nature. The court held that defendant's solicitation of oral sex was mere preparation rather than perpetration and, thus, not an overt "act," within the meaning of the attempt statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27(A), for the purpose of and tending directly toward having unnatural carnal copulation or oral sex in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89.1(A)(6). The court found that the testimony of the victim and a corroborating witness indicated that defendant remained clothed; never touched or threatened the victim, lay next to him, or made any move to undress him; and left the room immediately when the victim refused. The court held that the trial court did not commit reversible error in stating that the meaning of "act" was for the jury to decide because defendant made no objection and the definition of the term was a mixed question of law and fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the verdict and vacated and set aside defendant's conviction and sentence.

Whitnell v. Silverman

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged the judgment of the trial court finding that La. Rev. Stat. State v. Chriceol


No. 26,449-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,449 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/28/94); 645 So. 2d 286; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2787



October 28, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland, Louisiana. Trial Court No. F-93-49. Honorable Chet D. Traylor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland, Louisiana, which sentenced him to 40 years at hard labor for his plea of nolo contendere to a charge of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a drunken brawl in which he killed his friend. He pleaded nolo contendere to a reduced charge of manslaughter and the trial court sentenced him to 40 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. Defendant insisted that he should have been charged with manslaughter initially. The court held that defendant got a break when his charge was reduced. Defendant claimed that there was no specific intent present as required for the offense of second degree murder. Yet he failed to show that his intoxication obviated specific intent. The court found that the fashion of the victim's death exhibited a continuous assault indicative of specific intent. Defendant asserted that his criminal history reflected no convictions for violent offenses, yet his history included an arrest for aggravated assault. He claimed that the trial court's statement that the "victim was beaten so badly that he was unrecognizable by the people who arrived at the scene" was a blatant exaggeration. The official statement of the first officer to arrive at the scene and the autopsy record showed that the statement was not an exaggeration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that sentenced defendant to 40 years at hard labor for his plea of nolo contendere to a charge of manslaughter.

Gibson v. State


No. 94-CA-0476


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-0476 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/27/94); 644 So. 2d 1148; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2782



October 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 93-2517, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GARVEY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate and family sought review of a judgment of the District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division "C" (Louisiana) that granted the motion of defendant State, district attorney, and witness for no cause of action in the inmate and family's action for malicious prosecution.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and family challenged the trial court's judgment that granted the motion of the State, district attorney, and witness for no cause of action in the inmate and family's action for malicious prosecution. The court affirmed and found that the inmate challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1441(A), which exempted the State from responsibility for the acts of district attorneys. Because the inmate's supplemental petition that challenged the constitutionality of the statute was neither filed nor served until after the judgment was signed, the court held that the issue was never before the trial court and was waived. The court noted the inmate's assertion that the State was liable for the district attorney's acts because the Orleans Parish District Attorney's Office was a quasi agency of the State. The court noted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 42:1441.1, 42:1441.2(A), 42:1441.3(A) protected the State from liability due to the acts of the district attorney, and retroactive application of the statutes was permissible because they merely stated the what the law intended, and did not make new law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of no cause of action in the inmate and family's action for malicious prosecution.

State v. Jones


No. 94-KA-383


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


94-383 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/25/94); 645 So. 2d 773; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3012



October 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 40TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE MARY BECNEL, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED, REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed the sentence imposed by the 40th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana) after he entered a guilty plea to the charge of aggravated battery, arguing that the district court impermissibly deviated from the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines and further failed to consider mitigating factors that would have served to lessen his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The defendant pled guilty to aggravated battery and was sentenced to 10 years of imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension and was ordered to pay restitution. The defendant appealed his sentence. The court rejected the argument that the district court erred in deviating from the sentencing guidelines and imposing the statutory maximum sentence. Where the offender's conduct was deliberately cruel and where the victim suffered severe and permanent injuries, the district court did not err in deviating from the sentencing guidelines, and the imposition of the statutory maximum was not excessive. In vacating the sentence and remanding for resentencing, however, the court concluded that patent error existed. The aggravated battery statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34, did not provide for a sentence without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, and restitution was permitted only in cases where the sentence was suspended and the defendant was placed on probation. Further, the district court erred in failing to give the defendant credit for time served prior to the imposition of sentence as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 880.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing where the district court committed patent error in imposing sentence.

 

783 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Automotive Casualty Ins. Co.


No. CA 93 2169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93-2169 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/7/94); 644 So. 2d 723; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2693



October 7, 1994, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 384,804, Div. "C". Honorable Paul B. Landry, Jr., Judge Pro Tempore Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, shareholder and finance company, sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Division C (Louisiana), which granted appellee insurance commissioner's request for injunctive relief and ordered liquidation of the shareholder's companies and declared them a single business enterprise.


OVERVIEW: The shareholder was the sole or majority shareholder in a finance company, insurance company, and automotive services company. The insurance commissioner filed a petition for conservation and injunctive relief against the shareholder. The trial court granted the insurance commissioner's request for injunctive relief and ordered liquidation of the shareholder's companies and declared them a single business enterprise. The court held that the record contained ample evidence to support the trial court's finding that the affiliated entities operated as a single business enterprise. The court determined that the evidence established centralized accounting under direct control of a single individual, transactions conducted on other than arms'-length basis, and transfers of funds without property security. The court further held that there was not a meeting of the minds, resulting in an enforceable contract between the commissioner and the shareholder, or prohibiting the commissioner from seeking control of the companies, in connection with the liquidation as the court found that the shareholder failed to prove the threshold element required to invoke the doctrine of equitable estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the insurance commissioner's request for injunctive relief and ordered liquidation of the shareholder's companies and declared them a single business enterprise.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed the judgment of the 32nd Judicial District Court in and for Terrebonne Parish (Louisiana), which dismissed his medical malpractice lawsuit against defendant physician, on the grounds that the state statute of limitations, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628(A), had expired.


OVERVIEW: The physician removed a rod from the back of a patient, but negligently left a wire in his back. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

Alessi v. Belanger


No. CA 93 2047


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


93-2047 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/7/94); 644 So. 2d 778; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2707



October 7, 1994, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 322,036, Division "C". Honorable Bob H. Hester, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a creditor, and defendant, a debtor, appealed a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which dismissed the creditor's petition for writ of attachment of the debtor's immovable property with prejudice. The debtor's reconventional demand was also dismissed with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The creditor filed a petition for writ of attachment, seeking attachment of the debtor's property and judgment for an outstanding balance due for the sale of a ring. The debtor filed a declinatory exception and sought dissolution of the writ of attachment. The trial court dismissed the creditor's petition with prejudice, holding that the debtor's fiance was the true purchaser of the ring. The debtor's reconventional demand was dismissed with prejudice because she failed to prove that any damages were sustained as a result of the alleged improper physical seizure. The court affirmed the judgment. The debtor's fiance made the payments on the ring. The debtor was not aware that the ring had been paid for until the lawsuit. Therefore the trial court did not err in finding that she was not the purchaser of the ring. Because the creditor failed to prevail on his claim, the writ of attachment was properly dissolved. The court ruled that the debtor was a nonresident at the time that the writ of attachment was filed because her bank account, driver's license, and vehicle registration was from North Carolina; therefore, the writ was properly based upon the nonresidency of the debtor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the creditor's petition for writ of attachment of the debtor's immovable property to collect a balance due on the sale of a ring. The dismissal of the debtor's reconventional demand was affirmed.

Chi v. Pang


No. 94-284


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-284 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/5/94); 643 So. 2d 411; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2617



October 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, Honorable Donald Aaron, Jr., Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which ordered him to pay appellee wife $ 1,000 each month.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife were physically separated, but had not initiated divorce proceedings. The husband had been ordered to live outside the state pursuant to a protective order proceeding initiated by the wife, who alleged that the husband had attacked her with a butcher knife. The trial court ordered the husband to pay the wife support payments of $ 1,000 each month. On appeal, the court first found that the trial court could properly assess the wife's claim for spousal support under either La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:291 or La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:2131. The court also found that that the trial court was not restricted to a time limitation of three months in making its award of spousal support. The court found no error in the trial court's assessment of the husband's support obligation by making an award proportioned to the needs of the wife, the claimant spouse, and the means of the husband, the other spouse. Furthermore, the court could not say that the trial court's $ 1,000 award of support to the wife was not supported by the record. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which ordered the husband to pay the wife $ 1,000 each month in spousal support, was affirmed.

State v. Matthews


No. CR 94-210


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


94-210 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/5/94); 643 So. 2d 854; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2621



October 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Allen M. Babineaux, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, for forcible rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.1, contending that the evidence was not sufficient to support his conviction and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for forcible rape. It held that based on the jury's factual finding that defendant had sexual intercourse with the victim, that such intercourse was without her consent, and that despite trying to physically resist, her resistance was overcome by acts of force, the record contained sufficient evidence for a rational jury to find defendant guilty. The court further held that the trial court was within its discretion in deviating from the sentencing guidelines where it found the aggravating circumstance that defendant attempted to intimidate a witness in the proceeding. The court further held that, considering the factors considered by the sentencing court, defendant's sentence did not constitute an unnecessary infliction of pain and suffering, nor did the sentence shock any sense of justice, and thus was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Alexander v. Louisiana State Bd. of Medical Examiners


No. 94-CA-0101

September 29, 1994, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought review of an affirmation of a decree of the State Board of Medical Examiners imposing disciplinary sanctions against him in the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division G (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: The doctor was indicted for robbing a savings and loan, but that conviction was reversed. He was re-tried and convicted, and the latter conviction was affirmed. Further, the requirement that he demonstrate his skills as a physician was clearly within the Board's authority.

State v. Wise


No. 93-KA-0105


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-0105 (La.App. 4 Cir. 9/29/94); 644 So. 2d 230; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2546



September 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused November 15, 1994. Released for Publication November 15, 1994.
Writ granted by, in part, Remanded by State v. Wise, 684 So. 2d 408, 1996 La. LEXIS 3446 (La., Dec. 6, 1996)
Related proceeding at State v. Wise, 128 So. 3d 1220, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2359 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS. PARISH NO. 358-790, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS TO EXCESSIVENESS; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, pro se, appealed his convictions and sentences in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section J (Louisiana). He claimed that the sentences were excessive, his right to appeal was violated by an incomplete record, he stood trial in prison attire, his counsel was ineffective for failure to object and investigate, the State used its peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory manner, and it withheld exculpatory evidence.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of theft and aggravated battery. The trial court modified the theft verdict and sentenced him to consecutive sentences of six months for the theft and 10 years at hard labor for the aggravated battery. The sentences were consecutive to a previously imposed six month sentence for contempt of court. An oral motion to reconsider the sentence was denied, and defendant appealed. The court held that where defendant created an outburst and used obscene, offensive language in the court, the sentence was not grossly out of proportion to the severity of the offense. As to the 10 year sentence, the court found that where the trial court clearly articulated considerations and the factual basis for the sentence, and defendant's actions were egregious and sufficient to support a charge of attempted murder, the sentence was not excessive. Yet the trial court did not express reasons for imposing consecutive sentences. Where the record on appeal was incomplete, defendant was not entitled to a new trial because he did not state that his substantive rights had been affected. Any other claims were not objected to in a timely fashion and were not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences as to excessiveness, but the matter was remanded for the trial court to articulate reasons for imposing consecutive sentences. Defendant's right to seek review of those reasons was reserved.

State v. Farley


No. 26,377-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,377 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/21/94); 643 So. 2d 300; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2419

PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 158,274. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated and sentenced him to serve three years at hard labor, the first year without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. At sentencing the trial court stated: "Considering the guidelines and arguments of counsel, the Court will sentence (defendant) to three years at hard labor; first year is without the benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence." On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction but vacated the sentence. The court held that because of the trial court's failure to set forth, on the record, its consideration of the sentencing guidelines and to outline the basis for its sentencing decision, it was necessary to vacate the defendant's sentence and to remand the case to the trial court to allow it an opportunity to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The court also held that defendant's waiver of a trial jury at the arraignment remained valid even after the bill of information was amended because the amendment did not change the nature of the charge against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of driving while intoxicated, but vacated the sentence and remanded to the trial court for resentence.

 

792 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Bumgarden v. Wackenhut Corrections Corp.


NUMBER 93-1349


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-1349 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/21/94); 645 So. 2d 655; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2425



September 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Allen, State of Louisiana, the Honorable John P. Navarre, Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: C-92-223



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate sought review of a judgment from the 33rd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Allen (Louisiana), which dismissed his personal injury suit against defendant, the contractor operating a private prison facility, on the ground that he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies under the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure (ARP), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq., and for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The former inmate was seriously injured while he was incarcerated at a private prison facility. He filed suit against the contractor operating the facility after he was released. The trial court dismissed his suit on the ground that he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies under the ARP and for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court declined to decide whether the ARP was applicable only to public bodies and not private corporations. The court held that the ARP did not apply to a plaintiff who was no longer in custody, regardless of whether the cause of action arose while the plaintiff was in custody. The ARP addressed itself to actions brought by offenders. "Offender" was defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1174(2) as someone who was in the physical custody of the state or a sheriff. The court pointed out the absurd consequence of interpreting the term "offenders" to include former inmates. Under such an interpretation, an inmate injured on the day prior to being released would have to have his rights governed by the ARP and would have to file his complaint in the prison system.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the former inmate's personal injury suit against the contractor operating a private prison facility and remanded for further proceedings.

Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81 and sentenced him to six years at hard labor on each count with the sentences to run concurrently.

Whittington v. Langston Drilling Co.


No. 26,001-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


26,001 (La.App. 2 Cir. 9/21/94); 643 So. 2d 336; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2455



September 21, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 387,271. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which sustained appellee employer's declinatory exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and which dismissed the employee's action for breach of contract and constitutional challenge of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1271.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured during the course and scope of his employment. The employee was collecting worker's compensation benefits and thereafter entered into a settlement with the employer's insurer. The worker's compensation hearing officer refused to approve the settlement in the absence of the employer's approval. Thereafter, the employee commenced a breach of contract action against his employer and also contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1271 was unconstitutional. The employer filed an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction, the trial court sustained the exception and dismissed the action. The employee appealed. The court upheld the trial court's judgment. The court held that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the case, therefore dismissal was proper. The court reasoned that the case whether referred to as a breach of contract action or worker's compensation action, still stemmed from the employee's worker's compensation action, therefore jurisdiction was not proper. The court remanded to the trial court for further proceedings with respect to the constitutional issue raised.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the employee's breach of contract action and remanded for further proceedings with respect to the constitutionality of a worker's compensation statute.

 

797 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of Zwolle v. Polk


No. K93-1102


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


93-1102 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/14/94); 643 So. 2d 201; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2396



September 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI OR REVIEW FROM THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF SABINE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, THE HONORABLE ROBERT BURGESS, DISTRICT JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: The defendants' writs are granted and the Bills of Information in these matters are quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An application for a writ from the 11th Judicial District Court, Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana, was filed by six defendants convicted of violation of a city ordinance that prohibited the sale of alcoholic beverages on Sunday. Defendants' motions to quash the bills of information were denied. Defendants claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional for failure to submit it to the local voters as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191.


OVERVIEW: The Sunday closing ordinance was passed by the local governing body but was not approved by the subdivision voters in an election. The issue was whether or not the ordinance was valid if the voters had not voted on the issue as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 a local subdivision could enact an ordinance regulating, but not prohibiting, the sale of alcoholic beverages where its enactment was a reasonable exercise of police power necessary for public health, morals, safety, and peace. To the extent that § 26:493 could be read to authorize Sunday closing ordinances without an election, it conflicted with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191. Upon review, the court pointed out that the jurisprudence provided that the statute more specifically directed to the matter at issue governed. In the situation at hand, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. § 26:493 dealt with regulation of alcohol generally while La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191 dealt specifically with the narrow issue of Sunday sales. Accordingly, the provisions of § 51:191 governed. Defendants' bills of information were quashed because the ordinance could only be enacted through the election process.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' writs, and the bills of information filed against them were quashed.

Bamma Leasing Co. v. Secretary of Dep't of Revenue & Taxation


No. 93-CA-881


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


93-881 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/14/94); 646 So. 2d 917; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2424



September 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 1995.
Dissenting Opinion Dated November 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 368-745, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, II, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff leasing company appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which denied a challenge to a tax assessment on leased cars under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:302(B). The company argued that the assessment was erroneous, it was exempt from sales taxes under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.36, it was entitled to a refund of certain taxes, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1486 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The company financed car sales through leases. Its standard forms identified the transactions as leases and referred to the parties as "lessor" and "lessee." On appeal, the court noted that such terms were not consistent with a financing agreement of a sale. Using the criteria in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(12) and jurisprudence, the court held that there was no manifest error in the trial court's affirmance of the judgment of the Louisiana Board of Tax Appeals (Board), which found that the transactions were leases with options to purchase and not conditional sales and that the lease tax in § 47:302(B) was due. The taxes in § 47:302(B) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:302(A) were not duplicative, so the company was not exempt under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.36 from paying initial sales taxes on the cars involved in the transactions and it was not entitled to a refund of taxes paid. The exemption applied only to cars the company bought after it obtained an exemption certificate under § 47:305.36. The court did not address the constitutionality of § 47:1486 because the company's suit had proceeded under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1431 et seq. and § 47:1486 never figured in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded to the Louisiana Board of Tax Appeals for recomputation of the assessment, interest and penalties, and collection of the taxes.

 

799 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State in re R.E.


NUMBER 94 CJ 1759


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-1759 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/14/94); 642 So. 2d 889; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2538



September 14, 1994, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1994. Released for Publication October 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Honorable Ian Claiborne, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff biological father sought review of a judgment from the 18th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which terminated the biological father's parental rights with regard to the minor child. The biological father had filed a petition in opposition to the child's adoption by defendant adoptive parents.


OVERVIEW: The biological mother voluntarily surrendered custody of the minor child and the child was placed with an adoption service. The biological father executed an authentic act of acknowledgment and filed a petition in opposition to adoption. He also registered with the putative father registry for the state. The trial court rendered a judgment that the biological father had forfeited his parental rights. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new hearing. Initially, the court held that no other state had jurisdiction to make a child custody determination under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1702(A). The voluntary act of surrender was executed in the state and the child was born in the state. The biological father preserved his right to be heard and met his burden of proving his affirmative efforts to establish a parental relationship with the minor child pursuant to La. Child. Code art. 1137. The court held that under La. Child. Code art. 1035, the trial court erred in imposing the preponderance of the evidence standard as opposed to the clear and convincing evidence standard in order to extinguish the father's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment terminating the biological father's parental rights was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new hearing. The trial court was ordered to appoint a curator ad hoc for the minor child and to order the minor child to be returned to the state and to be placed temporarily with the state Department of Social Services until a determination was reached as to the biological father's parental rights.

 

800 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grant


No. 93-KA-2183


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


93-KA-2183 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/27/94); 641 So. 2d 691; 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2202



July 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 363-395, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence, by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), for second degree battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction for second degree battery, defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction and that his sentence was constitutionally excessive. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that a rational trier of fact could conclude that the victim was a credible witness and that defendant made an unprovoked physical assault on the victim with the intent to inflict serious bodily injury. The court also affirmed the sentence. It held that a review of the sentencing transcript showed that the trial judge adequately articulated sufficient reason for imposing the three-year sentence, which in fact was lenient as compared to the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines recommended range. The court further held that the sentence was not constitutionally excessive, in light of defendant's three prior felony convictions and the violent nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.
